Ruling on Expiation and Inheritance in Shibh al-'Amd
Discusses whether kaffarah is obligatory in shibh al-'amd and the effect on inheritance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kaffarah in shibh al-'amd, identify the reason for its obligation, and explain the effect on inheritance.

Core Idea
Shibh al-'amd is treated like khata' for expiation because the killing was unintended, but the killer is sinful for the intentional strike.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq tackles an important nuance: although shibh al-'amd involves an intentional strike, the resulting killing is not intended. The Hanafi school, in its established view, requires kaffarah because the act partakes of error from one aspect. However, a minority transmission attributes to Abu Hanifa the opposite view. The author defends the majority position and also clarifies that the killer is deprived of inheritance, just as in accidental killing, but with an aggravated blood-money due to the deliberate nature of the strike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is shibh al-'amd (intentional strike causing unintended death). The ruling under discussion is whether kaffarah (expiation) is obligatory. The majority Hanafi position states it is wajib.
Kaffarah is an act of worship prescribed for expiation of sins.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage states that shibh al-'amd falls under the text on khata' (error). The primary textual basis is the Quranic verse on accidental killing (4:92), which prescribes kaffarah for khata'.
The author uses general inclusion under the ruling for khata'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Although the strike was intentional, the killing itself was not intended. Therefore, from the perspective of the killing, it is considered a mistake, bringing it under the verse on khata'.
The distinction between the intent of the strike and the lack of intent for death is critical.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
A minority view within the Hanafi school, reported from Abu Hanifa via al-Īḍāḥ, holds that kaffarah is not obligatory because the sin of striking is complete, and kaffarah as leniency is inappropriate.
This is an intra-Hanafi transmission, not the established position.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author rebuts the minority view by dividing the act into the sin of striking (intentional) and the act of killing (unintentional). Kaffarah attaches to the killing, not the strike. The majority view is mufta bihi.
The tarjih is based on the clear distinction and the weight of zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإنما كان آثماً في شبه العمد لأنه ارتكب محرماً في دينه قاصداً له وإنما وجبت الكفارة به لأنه خطأ من وجه فيدخل تحت النص على الخطأ . أقول : المتبادر من قوله لدخوله تحت الخطأ أن هذه الكفارة إنما وجبت في شبه العمد باعتبار الدخول. فإن قلت : يرد عليه أن تعين الكفارة لدفع الفني الأمنى بالشرع لا تعينها كما قالوا في العمد إذ لا شك أن شبه العمد أعلى ذنباً من الخطأ المحض فإن الجاني في شبه العمد قد قصد الضرب وفي الخطأ لم يقصد الضرب. وقد يجاب بأن ذنب شبه العمد دائر بين الأدنى والأعلى فإلحاقه بالأدنى أولى طلباً للتخفيف فلذا وجبت فيه الكفارة. وذكر صاحب الهداية أن صاحب الإيضاح قال في الإيضاح وجدت في كتب أصحابنا أن الكفارة في شبه العمد لا تجب على قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى فإن الإثم كامل وتناهيه يمنع شرع الكفارة لأن ذلك من باب التخفيف. وجوابه على الظاهر أن يقول : إنه إثم الضرب لأنه قصده لا إثم القتل لأنه لم يصدقه، وهذه الكفارة تجب بالقتل وهو فيه مخطئ ولا تجب بالضرب ألا ترى أنها لا تجب بالضرب بدون القتل وبعكسه تجب فكذا عند اجتماعهما يضاف الوجوب إلى القتل دون الضرب وأما وجوب الدية فلما روينا وإنما وجبت على العاقلة لأنه خطأ من وجه على ما بينا فيكون معذوراً فيتحقق التخفيف كذلك، ولأنها تجب بنفس القتل فتجب على العاقلة كما في الخطأ ولهذا أوجبها عمر رضي الله عنه في ثلاث سنين. ويتعلق بهذا القتل حرمان الميراث كالخطأ بل أولى لأنه جزاء القتل وهو أولى بالمجازاة لوجود القصد منه إلى الفعل، فحاصله أنه كالخطأ إلا في حق الإثم وصفة التغليظ في الدية على ما تبين من بعد إن شاء الله .
And indeed, he is sinful in shibh al-'amd because he committed something forbidden in his religion intentionally. And expiation is obligatory because it is a mistake from one aspect, so it falls under the text on mistake. I say: The apparent meaning of his statement 'because it falls under mistake' is that this expiation is only obligatory in shibh al-'amd by virtue of falling under it. If you say: It is objected that the designation of expiation to ward off loss (?) by the Law does not designate it; as they said regarding 'amd, there is no doubt that shibh al-'amd is a graver sin than pure mistake, because the perpetrator in shibh al-'amd intended the strike, while in mistake he did not intend the strike. It may be answered: The sin of shibh al-'amd oscillates between the lower and the higher, so attaching it to the lower is preferable seeking leniency, hence expiation is obligatory. And the author of al-Hidayah mentioned that the author of al-Īḍāḥ said in al-Īḍāḥ: I found in the books of our companions that expiation in shibh al-'amd is not obligatory according to the saying of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, because the sin is complete and its perfection prevents the legislation of expiation, as that is a matter of leniency. The answer to that is apparent: He says: It is the sin of the strike because he intended it, not the sin of killing because he did not intend it. And this expiation is obligatory due to killing, in which he is mistaken, and is not obligatory due to the strike. Do you not see that it is not obligatory due to the strike without killing, and conversely it is obligatory? Thus when both combine, the obligation is attributed to the killing, not the strike. As for the obligation of blood-money, it is based on what we narrated. And it is only obligatory on the 'āqila because it is a mistake from one aspect, as we explained, so he is excused and thus leniency is achieved. And because it is obligatory by the act of killing itself, it is obligatory on the 'āqila as in khata'. For this reason, 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, made it obligatory in three years. And connected to this killing is the deprivation of inheritance, as in khata', rather more so, because it is a penalty for killing, and it is more deserving of requital due to the presence of intent in the act. So the conclusion is that it is like khata' except regarding the matter of sin and the description of exaggeration in blood-money, as will be explained later, God willing.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage addresses whether kaffarah (expiation) is required in shibh al-'amd. The author initially states that kaffarah is obligatory because shibh al-'amd partakes of khata' (error) from one angle, and the verse on khata' includes it. A potential objection is raised: since shibh al-'amd involves deliberate striking, it is a greater sin than pure khata', so why should it get the leniency of kaffarah? The response: the sin is due to the striking, not the killing; the killing itself was unintentional, so the act is partly mistaken. The text then cites a difference within the Hanafi school: some (from al-Īḍāḥ) claim that according to Abu Hanifa, kaffarah is not obligatory because the sin is complete, and kaffarah is a form of leniency not deserved. The author rebuts this by distinguishing sin: the intentional strike creates sin, but the killing is inadvertent, so kaffarah attaches to the killing aspect, which is partly mistaken. The passage also discusses diyah: it is heavy and on the 'āqila. Additionally, the killer is deprived of inheritance from the victim, similar to khata', but even more so because the strike was intentional. The overall principle: shibh al-'amd resembles khata' except in the realm of sin and the aggravated diyah.

Key Terms
الكفارة (al-kaffarah): Expiation required for certain offenses, typically fasting or charity; in shibh al-'amd, it is required due to the partially mistaken killing.
الخطأ (al-khata'): Accidental killing, no intent; contrasted with shibh al-'amd.
حرمان الميراث (ḥirmān al-mīrāth): Deprivation of inheritance; the killer cannot inherit from the victim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author's conclusion, why is kaffarah obligatory in shibh al-'amd?
A) Because the killer intended the strike
B) Because the killing is completely intentional
C) Because the killing is considered a mistake from one aspect
D) Because it is not obligatory at all

Key Takeaway
In shibh al-'amd, kaffarah is wajib because the killing is unintended, and the killer is denied inheritance; the diyah is heavy and on the 'āqila.

Inheritance of Qisas and Diyah
Ruling with proof on inheritance of qisas and diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that qisas and diyah are inheritable in Hanafi fiqh and identify the primary proofs for this ruling.

Core Idea
Qisas and diyah are inheritable rights like property, passing to heirs.

In Hanafi law, the right of retaliation (qisas) and blood money (diyah) are not lost upon the victim's death; they pass to the heirs as inheritable claims. This lesson unpacks the textual and practical evidence for this principle, drawing on a hadith and the practice of Ali (RA). You will learn why qisas shares the same legal status as property for inheritance purposes.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the core ruling: qisas and diyah are inheritable rights. The passage begins by asserting that if one leaves property or a right, it is for his heirs, and then applies this to qisas.
This is the core hukm.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith reference: the Prophet (ﷺ) ordered that the wife of Usaym al-Dhababi inherit from her husband's diyah. This shows diyah is treated as property.
The hadith is not fully quoted but referenced.
3
Understand the analogy (qiyas)
The passage argues: since diyah is like property, it is inherited. Similarly, qisas is a substitute for life like diyah, so it too is inherited. The practice of Ali (RA) dividing diyah among heirs reinforces this.
Analogy to property is key.
4
Analyze the counterargument (implicit)
Consider why someone might think qisas is not inheritable (e.g., it seems personal). The passage addresses this by noting that women inherit diyah even though they do not pay it, showing inheritance is based on relationship, not liability.
This refutes the misconception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم كتاب الجنايات باب القصاص فيما دون النفس ترك مالاً أو حقاً فلورثته (۱) الحديث والقصاص حقه فيكون الجميعهم كالمال، وأمر عليه الصلاة والسلام بتوريث امرأة أسيم الضبابي من دية زوجها أسيم، ولأن القصاص حق يجري فيه الإرث حتى إذا قتل وله ابنان فمات أحدهما عن ابن كان القصاص بين الابن وبين ابن الابن فيثبت كسائر الورثة والزوجية تبقى بعد الموت حكماً كما في حق الإرث أو يثبت الإرث مستنداً إلى سببه وهو الجرح، وكان علي رضي الله عنه يقسم الدية على من أحرز الميراث. والدية حكمها حكم سائر الأموال ولهذا لو أوصى بثلث ماله تدخل الدية فيه والقصاص بدل النفس كالدية فيورث كسائر أمواله ولهذا لو انقلبت مالا يقضى به دینه وتنفذ به وصاياه واستحقاق الإرث بالزوجية كاستحقاقه بالقرابة لا بالعقد ألا أنه لا يرتد بالرد بخلاف الوصية ولهذا يتبين أن الاستحقاق ليس بالعقد بل بالعقد ولا يلزم من عدم التناصر وعدم العقل عدم الإرث للقصاص ألا تری أن النساء من الأقارب لا يعقلن ويرثن القصاص والدية أقرب منه إذا المرأة لا تعقل عنها أبناؤها الكبار ويرثونها.
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Book of Crimes, Chapter of Retaliation for Less Than Life. If one leaves property or a right, it is for his heirs. Hadith: and retaliation is a right, so all of it is like property. And the Prophet, peace be upon him, ordered that the wife of Usaym al-Dhababi be given inheritance from the blood money of her husband Usaym. And because retaliation is a right in which inheritance flows; so if a person is killed and he has two sons, then one of them dies leaving a son, the right of retaliation lies between the surviving son and the grandson. So it is established like other heirs. And marital relationship remains after death in a legal sense, as in the right of inheritance, or inheritance is established based on its cause, which is the wound. And Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, used to divide the blood money among those who received the inheritance. And the blood money has the same ruling as other properties; thus if one bequeaths one-third of his property, the blood money enters into that. And retaliation is a substitute for the soul like blood money, so it is inherited like other properties; hence if it is converted into property, debts are paid with it, and bequests are executed. And the entitlement to inheritance by marriage is like entitlement by kinship, not by contract, except that it is not returned by rejection unlike a bequest. Thus it becomes clear that entitlement is not by contract but by the [marriage] contract. And the lack of mutual assistance or lack of blood money liability does not necessitate lack of inheritance of retaliation. Do you not see that women among relatives do not pay blood money, yet they inherit retaliation and blood money? Even closer, a woman does not pay blood money on behalf of her adult sons, but they inherit from her.
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the inheritance of the right of qisas (retaliatory punishment) and diyah (blood money). The author explains that qisas, like property, is a right that passes to the victim's heirs. This is supported by the hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) ordered that the wife of Usaym al-Dhababi inherit from the diyah of her husband. Moreover, if the victim has two sons and one dies before retaliation, the right passes to the grandson, showing it is inheritable. The marital relationship persists in legal effect for inheritance purposes. Ali (رضي الله عنه) practiced dividing diyah among heirs. Since diyah is like other property, it enters into bequests and debt repayment. The passage also clarifies that inheritance of qisas is based on kinship or marriage, not the compensation contract itself, using the example that women inherit diyah even though they are not liable for paying it.

Key Terms
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment, specifically the right of a victim's heirs to demand execution of the killer or equivalent.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid as compensation for homicide or bodily harm.
إرث (irth): Inheritance, the transfer of rights and property from deceased to heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does the right of qisas pass to the victim's heirs?
A) Yes, it is inheritable like property.
B) No, it lapses with the victim's death.
C) Only if the victim was married.
D) Only male heirs inherit qisas.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, qisas and diyah are inheritable rights that pass to the victim's heirs, based on hadith, qiyas, and practice of the sahaba.

Slave Kills Two: Inheritance and Priority in Diyat
Explains multiple sub-cases of inheritance and priority when a slave kills two victims and one is the master's brother.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the distribution of a slave who kills multiple victims, applying Hanafi faraid and diyat rules with priority and inheritance effects.

Core Idea
A master cannot claim blood-money from his own slave; inherited claims against the slave fall instantly.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a series of scenarios where a slave commits accidental killings of two individuals: another man's slave and the master's brother. The rulings hinge on the order of killings, the presence of additional heirs, and the master's dual role as both the brother's heir and the slave's owner. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi resolution of competing claims (tazāhum) when one claimant's right must fall due to impossibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the victims and claimants
List all parties: the slave (the object of compensation), the first victim (another man's slave), the second victim (master's brother), and the guardians/heirs (the other slave's owner, the master, and possibly the brother's daughter).
2
Determine order of killings and attachment of rights
The sequence affects whether both claims attach to the slave simultaneously or sequentially. Hanafi rules prioritize earlier attachments unless inheritance causes a claim to fall.
If killings are simultaneous, both attach at once and share proportionally.
3
Apply inheritance rules to master's brother's claim
When the brother dies, his right to compensation passes to his heirs. If the master is the sole heir, he inherits that right, but since it is a claim against his own slave, it is extinguished (sāqiṭ).
The master cannot owe himself blood-money.
4
Resolve tazāhum (competition) between remaining claimants
If a claim remains after inheritance, it competes with the other victim's claim. If both attach, they divide the slave's value proportionally. If one falls, the other takes the entire slave.
Tazāhum is resolved by proportional sharing when rights are simultaneous.
5
Account for additional heirs (daughter)
If the brother has a daughter, she inherits a quarter of his claim. That quarter does not fall because it belongs to her, not the master. The master's inherited half (from the brother) still falls, so the daughter's quarter and the other victim's half result in a 3:1 split.
The daughter's share is fard (Quranic), not extinguished by the master's ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هشام عن محمد قال : مملوك قتل مملوكاً لرجل خطأ ثم قتل أخا مولاه وليس لأخي مولاه وارث غيره فإنه يدفع نصف العبد كله إلى مولى العبد أو يفديه والنصف الباقي للمولى لأن حق أخي المولى تعلق برقبة الجاني بعدما تعلق به حق المولى فتقع المزاحمة بينهما فيكون بينهما نصفين وإذا انتقل النصف إلى المولى بالإرث سقط بعد الوجوب لأن المولى لا يستوجب على عبده شيئاً فبقي حق الأول في النصف، فإن قتل أخا مولاه أولاً ثم قتل مملوك رجل خطأ فإنه يدفع العبد كله إلى مولى العبد المقتول أو يفديه لأنه لما انتقل الحق إلى المولى بالإرث سقط عنه، وإذا جنى على الثاني ولا يزاحمه الأول فقد تعلق حق ولي الجناية الثانية من غير مزاحمة، وإن كان لأخي مولاه بنت وقد قتله العبد أولاً فإنه يضمن ثلاثة أرباع العبد لمولى العبد المقتول وربعه للبنت لأن حق ولي الجناية الثانية تعلق بالنصف وتعلق حق الوارثين بالنصف إلا أنه سقط حق المولى عن الربع وبقي حق البنت في الربع، فإن كانت الضربتان معاً وليس له بنت فالعبد بينهما نصفان لأن الجنايتين افترقتا فلم تصادف إحداهما محلاً فارغاً
Hishām narrated from Muhammad: A slave killed another slave belonging to a man accidentally, then he killed his master's brother. The master's brother has no other heir besides the master. Then he hands over half of the entire slave to the owner of the killed slave, or ransoms him, and the remaining half is for the master. Because the right of the master's brother attached to the slave's body after the master's right had attached; so they become partners, and it is divided in half. When that half transfers to the master by inheritance, it falls after obligation, because the master does not claim anything from his own slave; so the first right remains in the half. If he killed the master's brother first and then killed another man's slave accidentally, then he hands over the entire slave to the owner of the killed slave or ransoms him, because when the right transferred to the master by inheritance, it fell from him. When he commits the second injury, the first does not compete; so the right of the second victim's guardian attaches without competition. If the master's brother had a daughter, and the slave killed him first, then he guarantees three-quarters of the slave to the owner of the killed slave and one-quarter to the daughter. Because the right of the second victim's guardian attached to half, and the right of the two heirs attached to half, except that the master's right to the quarter fell, and the daughter's right remains in the quarter. If the two killings occurred together and he has no daughter, then the slave is divided in half between them, because the two injuries are separate and neither found the body unoccupied.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage presents a series of inheritance-injury scenarios involving a slave who kills two individuals: another slave and the master's brother. The rulings depend on the order of killings, the presence of additional heirs (a daughter), and whether the killings occur simultaneously. The central issue is how the master's right to inherit from his brother interacts with claims against the slave. When the slave kills the brother after killing another slave, the brother's right to compensation attaches to the slave, but since the brother dies leaving only the master as heir, that right transfers to the master, which then falls because a master cannot claim from his own slave. Thus, only the first victim's guardian gets half the slave. If the brother is killed first, the master inherits the brother's right, which falls, leaving the second victim's guardian with the entire slave. If the brother has a daughter, she inherits a share, complicating distribution. If both killings occur simultaneously, the slave is divided equally between the two guardians. This demonstrates the Hanafi approach to fara'id (inheritance) principles intersected with diyat and slave injuries.

Key Terms
تزاحم (tazāḥum): Competition or conflict of rights among claimants seeking compensation from the same slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A slave kills his master's brother accidentally, then kills another man's slave accidentally. The brother leaves only the master as heir. How is the slave distributed?
A) Half to master, half to other owner
B) Entire slave to the other owner
C) Entire slave to master
D) Divided equally between master and other owner

Key Takeaway
When the master inherits a claim against his own slave, that claim is extinguished; prioritization of victims' rights depends on the order of killings and existence of other heirs.

Division of Ransom When One Heir of Intentional Homicide Forgives
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing ransom when one heir of ‘amd forgives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn over dividing a slave's ransom when one intentional‑homicide heir forgives, and calculate the shares under each method.

Core Idea
When one intentional homicide heir forgives, Abu Hanifa divides the ransom in thirds (proportional to claims); the Sahibayn divide in fourths (halving the disputed half).

This passage from al‑Bahr al‑Ra’iq presents a nuanced intra‑Hanafi dispute about distributing the ransom (fidya) of a slave who has committed both intentional and erroneous homicide. The key question is: when one of the two intentional‑homicide heirs forgives his right to qisas (converting to diyah), how should the ransom be split among the remaining claimants? Abu Hanifa’s answer differs from that of his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al‑Shaybani, and the disagreement hinges on whether the erroneous‑homicide heirs’ claim covers the entire slave or only a part.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their claims
The slave has two sets of heirs: one from erroneous killing (khata) with a claim of 10,000 dirhams, and two heirs from intentional killing (amd) with a combined claim of 10,000 (5,000 each). One of the amd heirs forgives.
The forgiving heir's right (5,000) is waived; the non‑forgiving amd heir still claims 5,000.
2
Determine the effect of forgiveness
The forgiving amd heir’s right to qisas converts to a right to diyah and is then forfeited, meaning the remaining non‑forgiving amd heir has a claim of 5,000, and the khata heirs have 10,000. Total claims = 15,000.
The forgiving heir's share does not go to the master; it becomes part of the pot for distribution.
3
Apply Abu Hanifa’s proportional method
Abu Hanifa divides the 15,000 ransom in proportion to the claims: 10,000 for khata (2/3) and 5,000 for the non‑forgiving amd heir (1/3). This is a direct application of ‘awl (proportional reduction when claims exceed assets?).
Here claims equal ransom, so no reduction needed; it's simply proportional.
4
Apply the Sahibayn’s contest (manāza‘a) method
The Sahibayn argue that half the ransom (7,500) is undisputed for the khata heirs because it corresponds to the forgiving heir's share? Actually, they say: 'half surrendered to the heir of erroneous killing without dispute, so their dispute becomes equal in the other half, so it is halved.' Thus, the remaining half (7,500) is divided equally between the khata heirs and the non‑forgiving amd heir, giving each 3,750. So total to khata = 7,500 (undisputed) + 3,750 = 11,250 (3/4 of 15,000); to non‑forgiving amd = 3,750 (1/4).
The 'half' they refer to is not the forgiving heir's 5,000 but half of the total ransom (7,500), which they consider undisputed for khata because the forgiving amd heir's right has fallen.
5
Evaluate the response to a potential objection
The text rebuts an alternative that would allocate the forgiving heir’s share to the master. The response is that the khata heirs’ claim covers the entire slave, so the master gets nothing; the whole ransom is subject to ‘awl among the claimants. This reinforces that the khata heirs didn't waive any part of their claim.
This shows the fundamental difference: Abu Hanifa sees claims as proportional to the whole; Sahibayn see a part as undisputed and then apply equal division.

Source Text

لولي الخطأ وبنصفها لأحد وليي العمد لأن حقهما في الدية عشر آلاف وحق وليي العبد في القصاص، فإن عفا أحدهما انقلب نصيب الآخر مالاً وهو نصف الدية خمسة آلاف، فإذا فداه بخمسة عشر ألف درهم عشرة آلاف لولي الخطأ وخمسة آلاف لغير العافي من وليي العمد، وإن دفعه إليهم أثلاثاً ثلثاه لولي الخطأ وثلثه للساكت من ولي العمد بطريق العمد لأن حقهم في الدية كذلك فيضرب ولياً الخطأ بعشرة آلاف ويضرب غير العافي من وليي العمد بخمسة ألاف، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله : يدفعه أرباعاً بطريق المنازعة ثلاثة أرباعه لوليي الخطأ وربعه لغير العافي من وليي العمد لأن نصفه سلم الولي الخطأ بلا منازعة فاستوت منازعتهم في النصف الآخر فينتصف . فإن قيل : ينبغي أن يسلم للمولى ربع العبد في هذه المسألة وهي نصيب العافي من وليي العمد ويدفع ثلاثة أرباعه إليهم تقسم بينهم على قدر حقوقهم كما سلم له النصف وهو نصيب العافين قلنا : لا يمكن ذلك هنا لأن لوليي الخطأ استحقاق كله ولم يسقط من حقهما شيء، وهذا لأن حق كل واحد من الفريقين تعلق بكل الرقبة في المسألتين غير أنه لما عفا ولي كل قتيل سقط حق العافين على الرقبة في المسألة الأولى وخلى نصيبهما منه عن حقهما وصار كذلك للمولى وهو النصف بخلاف ما نحن فيه فإن حق ولي الخطأ ثابت في الكل على حاله وكانت الرقبة كلها مستحقة لهما والنصف لغير العافي من ولي العمد فلهذا افترقا فيقسمونها كلها على قدر حقوقهم بطريق العول والمنازعة ولهذه المسألة نظائر ذكرناها في كتاب الدعوى من الكتاب بأصولها الذي نشأ منها الخلاف بتوفيق الله تعالى فلا نعيدها.
For the heir of erroneous killing, and half of it for one of the two heirs of intentional killing because their right in the blood money is ten thousand, and the right of the two heirs of the slave is in retaliation. Then if one of them forgives, the other's share converts to property, which is half of the blood money, five thousand. So if he is ransomed for fifteen thousand dirhams, ten thousand go to the heir of erroneous killing, and five thousand to the non-forgiving of the two heirs of intentional killing. And if he is given to them in thirds, two-thirds for the heir of erroneous killing and one-third for the silent one of the heir of intentional killing by way of intentional, because their right in blood money is like that. So the two heirs of erroneous killing are paid ten thousand and the non-forgiving of the two heirs of intentional killing is paid five thousand. This is according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: he is paid in fourths by way of dispute: three-quarters for the two heirs of erroneous killing, and one-quarter for the non-forgiving of the two heirs of intentional killing, because half surrendered to the heir of erroneous killing without dispute, so their dispute becomes equal in the other half, so it is halved. If it is said: quarter of the slave should be surrendered to the master in this issue, which is the share of the forgiving one from the heirs of intentional killing, and he should pay three-quarters to them, divided according to their rights as half was surrendered to him, being the share of the forgivers. We say: that is not possible here, because the heirs of erroneous killing have entitlement to all of it, and nothing of their right has fallen. This is because the right of each of the two groups attaches to the entire slave in the two issues, except that when the heir of each slain forgave, the right of the forgivers on the slave fell in the first issue, and their share was vacated from their right, and so it became for the master, which is the half. Unlike our case, where the right of the heir of erroneous killing is established in all of it as it is, and the entire slave is due to them, and the half is for the non-forgiving of the heirs of intentional killing. For this reason they differ, and they divide it all according to their rights by way of 'awl and dispute. This issue has parallels which we mentioned in the Book of Claims from the book with its principles from which the difference arose, by the grace of Allah, so we do not repeat them.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a specific scenario: a slave has committed both intentional homicide (amd) and erroneous homicide (khata'), with separate sets of heirs. The heirs of the erroneous killing are entitled to full blood money (10,000 dirhams), while the heirs of the intentional killing have the right to retaliation or blood money. When one of the two heirs of the intentional homicide forgives, his share (half the intentional blood money, i.e., 5,000) becomes property of the forgiving heir, and the remaining heir's share (also 5,000) remains as a claim against the slave. If the slave's owner chooses to ransom him for 15,000 dirhams, the distribution of this ransom is disputed. Abu Hanifa holds that the ransom is divided into thirds: two-thirds (10,000) go to the heirs of the erroneous killing, and one-third (5,000) goes to the non-forgiving heir of the intentional killing. This is because the heirs of erroneous killing are entitled to the full blood money (10,000), and the non-forgiving heir of intentional killing is entitled to his share (5,000). The total claim is 15,000, so the ransom is distributed proportionally according to the claims. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the ransom should be divided into fourths: three-quarters (11,250) go to the heirs of erroneous killing, and one-quarter (3,750) goes to the non-forgiving heir of intentional killing. Their reasoning is that half the ransom (7,500) is undisputed for the heirs of erroneous killing because it corresponds to their right from the intentional victim's share that was converted to property? Actually, the text explains: 'half surrendered to the heir of erroneous killing without dispute' meaning that the 5,000 from the forgiving intentional heir's share is uncontested, so that portion goes entirely to the erroneous heirs? Then the remaining half (5,000) is disputed among the parties? The Sahibayn then apply proportional division (awl) to the remaining half. The commentary further addresses an objection: why not give the master (owner of the slave) a quarter (the share of the forgiving heir) and then divide the remaining three-quarters? The response is that the heirs of erroneous killing have not waived their right to the entire slave; their claim covers the whole value, unlike the first case where the forgiving heirs dropped their claim. Therefore, the whole ransom is divided according to the claims of the parties using awl (proportional reduction). This is a classic Hanafi application of 'awl in the context of slave investments.

Key Terms
ولي العمد (wali al-‘amd): The heir(s) of a victim of intentional homicide (amd). They have the right to demand qisas (retaliation) or diyah (blood money) upon forgiveness.
ولي الخطأ (wali al-khaṭa’): The heir(s) of a victim of erroneous homicide (khata). They are entitled only to diyah (blood money), not qisas.
العافين (al-‘āfīn): The forgiving ones, i.e., those heirs who forgive the right to qisas or diyah, thus waiving their claim against the slave.
الرقبة (al-raqaba): The slave's person; in this context, the entire value of the slave is considered as a pooled asset subject to claims.
العول (al-‘awl): Proportional reduction when total claims exceed the value of the estate; here applied analogically to the distribution of the slave's ransom.
المنازعة (al-munāza‘a): Dispute or contest among claimants; the Sahibayn's method of dividing based on contest (manāza‘a) rather than direct proportional claims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a slave has committed both intentional and erroneous homicide, and one heir of the intentional victim forgives, how is the ransom of 15,000 dirhams divided?
A) Three-quarters to khata heirs, one-quarter to non-forgiving amd heir
B) Two-thirds to khata heirs, one-third to non-forgiving amd heir
C) Half to each set of heirs
D) All to the khata heirs

Key Takeaway
The distribution of a slave’s ransom when one heir forgives depends on whether the remaining claims are treated proportionally or through contest; the difference yields thirds versus fourths.

Dividing the One-Third: Bequests of a Sword and Fractions
Numerical example of dividing one-third when multiple bequests exceed one-third.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the proportional distribution of the one-third of an estate among legatees when bequests exceed one-third, using both Abu Hanifa's and the two companions' methods.

Core Idea
When bequests exceed one-third and heirs do not consent, the one-third is divided proportionally among legatees, but the method of proportion differs between Abu Hanifa and the two companions.

This lesson works through a complex numerical example from Al-Bahr al-Raiq illustrating how to distribute the one-third of an estate when multiple bequests exceed the limit. The example involves a man who leaves an estate of 600 dirhams including a sword valued at 100, and bequeaths one-third to one person, one-sixth to another, and the sword to a third. The passage shows both Abu Hanifa's and the two companions' methods of calculation, highlighting the practical difference between their approaches.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Scenario
Understand the estate: total 600 dirhams, sword value 100. Bequests: 1/3 of the estate, 1/6 of the estate, and the sword itself. These total 200+100+100=400, which exceeds the one-third limit (200). The ruling depends on whether the heirs consent.
The numbers in the text may have OCR errors; focus on the method.
2
Trace Abu Hanifa's Proportional Method
When heirs do not consent, Abu Hanifa divides the one-third (200 dirhams) in proportion to the legatees' prescribed shares as if taken from the entire estate. The example calculates a base of 116 shares representing these proportions, then apportions the 200 accordingly: sword owner gets 36, one-third legatee gets 60, one-sixth legatee gets 30.
The derivation of 116 shares involves multiplying and adjusting fractions; follow the arithmetic carefully.
3
Examine the Two Companions' Method
The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) use a method based on 'awl and mudaraba. They treat the sword as a specific item and divide it into 9 shares. The one-third is then divided differently, yielding different amounts for the legatees (e.g., sword owner gets 18, etc.).
Their approach emphasizes treating the specific legacy separately.
4
Compare the Outcomes
Under Abu Hanifa's method without consent, the sword owner gets 36, one-third legatee 60, one-sixth legatee 30 (total 126 from the one-third of 200? The text says 106? Note the discrepancy due to OCR). Under the companions' method, the shares are smaller (e.g., sword owner gets 18, etc.). The practical difference is significant.
Verify the sums: the text states 'so the shares of the bequests become one hundred six' for Abu Hanifa's method without consent.
5
Note the Role of Heir Consent
When heirs consent, the legatees receive their full bequests from the entire estate (or a different calculation). The example shows that with consent, the amounts are larger (e.g., for the companions' method, consent gives the one-third legatee 30, etc.). Consent removes the one-third restriction entirely.
Consent must be explicit and voluntary.

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed numerical example from Al-Bahr al-Raiq illustrating how to divide the one-third of an estate when multiple bequests exceed one-third and the heirs either consent or do not. The scenario involves a man who leaves an estate worth 600 dirhams, including a sword valued at 100. He makes three bequests: (1) one-third of the estate to one person, (2) one-sixth to another, and (3) the sword itself to a third. The total bequests would normally exceed one-third if all were fulfilled. The commentary first shows the calculation according to Abu Hanifa: when heirs consent, each legatee gets his full specified share from the entire estate (one-third=200, one-sixth=100, sword=100, total 400, but the one-third limit is 200, so only 200 is distributed? Actually the text calculates differently—it seems they adjust the shares proportionally). When heirs do not consent, only one-third of the property (200) is divided among the legatees in proportion to their prescribed shares. The example then shows the method of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), who use a different approach based on 'awl (proportional reduction) and consider the sword as a specific item. They divide the one-third proportionally as well but with a different calculation, resulting in different shares. The passage demonstrates the practical difference between the two opinions within the Hanafi school. The author uses fractions and multiplication to arrive at the final distribution, showing that when heirs consent, the shares increase for all, but when they do not, only the one-third is distributed. This exemplifies the Hanafi rule that bequests beyond one-third are suspended unless the heirs approve.

Key Terms
سهام الوصايا (sihām al-waṣāyā): The shares of the bequests; the total units assigned to each legatee in the calculation of distribution from the one-third.
إجازة الورثة (ijāzat al-warathah): Consent of the heirs to allow bequests exceeding one-third of the estate to be executed.
العول (al-ʿawl): Proportional reduction of shares when the total of fixed shares exceeds the estate; applied in inheritance and here analogically to bequests.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The intra-Hanafi dispute on calculating the distribution of the one-third when bequests exceed the limit illustrates that the method of proportion can affect the amounts received by legatees.

Bequest of a Hypothetical Heir's Share: Calculation Example
Calculates two faraid examples of bequests of hypothetical heirs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares when a testator bequeaths the share of a hypothetical daughter, applying Hanafi faraid rules.

Core Idea
A bequest of a hypothetical heir's share is valid; it is calculated as if the heir existed and is subject to the one-third limit.

This lesson examines a specific faraid scenario from Imam Muhammad's Al-Asl: a man dies leaving his mother and father, and bequeaths to a third person the share that a daughter would have received if she had existed. Since no daughter exists, the bequest is determined by projecting her hypothetical share. We will walk through the calculation step by step, understanding how the shares of the mother, father, and legatee are derived.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actual heirs and the hypothetical heir
The actual heirs are the mother and father. The hypothetical heir is a daughter who is assumed to exist for the purpose of calculating the bequest.
The bequest is made to a non-heir, so it is taken from the one-third of the estate, subject to the one-third limit.
2
Determine the hypothetical daughter's share
If a daughter existed alongside the parents, her share would be 1/2 of the estate (since she is a single daughter and the father is an asabah). The mother would get 1/6, and the father would get the residue (1/3).
These base shares are from the Quran: daughter 1/2 (Surah 4:11), mother 1/6 (Surah 4:11), father as asabah.
3
Compute the bequest amount and adjust for the one-third limit
The bequest is the daughter's share (1/2). However, bequests to non-heirs are limited to 1/3 of the estate. The daughter's share (1/2) exceeds 1/3. Therefore, the bequest is reduced to 1/3, and the remaining 1/6 is redistributed to the heirs proportionally.
The reduction is mandatory unless the heirs consent to the excess.
4
Calculate the final shares using a common denominator
To distribute the estate, we use a base number (asl al-masalah). The shares of the mother (1/6), father (asabah, but after adjusting), and the legatee (1/3) must be expressed with a common denominator. The given result is 17 shares: legatee gets 5, mother 2, father 10.
The calculation yields 5/17 for the legatee, 2/17 for the mother, and 10/17 for the father. This satisfies the one-third limit (5/17 is slightly less than 1/3, but the precise ratio matches the rule).
5
Verify the total and consider heirs' consent
The total shares sum to 17/17. If the heirs had not consented to the bequest exceeding the one-third, the legatee would have received at most 1/3 of the original estate; however, here the distribution already respects the limit.
In the second example, where a son is present and a hypothetical son's share is bequeathed, the heirs' consent allows a larger share (7/15 each).

وفي الأصل الوصية بنصيب الابن أو بمثل نصيب الابن إن لم تجز الورثة لم يجز أو يجز بعضهم وقال محمد : رجل هلك وترك أماً وأباً وأوصى لرجل بنصيب بنت لو كانت فالوصية من سبعة عشر منها الموصى له خمسة أسهم وللأم سهمان وللأب عشرة أسهم قال : ولو ترك ابناً فأوصى بنصيب ابن آخر لو كان وأجازت الورثة الوصية فالفريضة من خمسة عشر للموصي سبعة أسهم وللابن سبعة وكذلك إذا أوصى بمثل نصيب ابنه لو كان الجواب كما قلنا وفي شرح الطحاوي قال : ومن أوصى لرجل بمثل نصيب ابنه فهذا لا يخلو إما أن كان أوصى له بمثل نصيب ابنه أو بنصيب ابنه كان له ابن أو لم
And in al-Asl: The bequest of the share of a son or the like of the share of a son – if the heirs do not consent, it is not permissible, or if some consent. Muhammad said: A man died leaving a mother and a father and bequeathed to a man the share of a daughter if there had been one. Then the inheritance (distribution) is from seventeen: the legatee gets five shares, the mother two shares, and the father ten shares. He said: And if he left a son and bequeathed the share of another son if there had been one, and the heirs consented to the bequest, then the distribution is from fifteen: the testator (i.e., the legatee?) gets seven shares and the son seven shares. Similarly, if he bequeathed the like of the share of his son if there had been one, the answer is as we said. And in Sharh al-Tahawi: Whoever bequeaths to a man the like of the share of his son, this is not free from either that he bequeathed to him the like of the share of his son or the share of his son, whether he has a son or not.
Source pages p. 228

Commentary
This passage provides specific inheritance calculations for bequests of hypothetical heirs' shares. Imam Muhammad gives two examples: (1) A man dies leaving a mother and father, and bequeaths to X the share of a daughter if one existed. Since there is no daughter, the bequest is computed as if a daughter were alive. The shares: the daughter would have a fixed share (1/2 if only child? Actually in presence of parents, daughter gets half? The text says the total shares are 17, with legatee getting 5, mother 2, father 10. This is based on a specific faraid calculation. (2) If the deceased left a son and bequeathed the share of another (hypothetical) son, and heirs consented, the distribution is from 15: the legatee gets 7, the son gets 7? That seems to imply the bequest is half the estate? Actually it requires careful faraid computation. The passage ends with a comment from Sharh al-Tahawi distinguishing the two phrases.

Key Terms
نصيب بنت لو كانت (nasib bint law kanat): The share a daughter would receive if she existed; used to determine the bequest amount.
أجازت الورثة (ajazat al-warathah): The heirs consent to the bequest, allowing it to exceed one-third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 12
B) 15
C) 17
D) 24

Key Takeaway
Bequests of hypothetical heirs' shares are calculated by projecting the heir's share, then applying the one-third limit, with heirs' consent allowing the full amount.

Multiple Fractional Bequests and Imam Muhammad's Taqsir
Complex faraid case with multiple bequests, loss, and intra-Hanafi dispute on calculation method.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the distribution of bequests of half, third, and sixth in an estate of cash and a slave, apply the adjustment for loss, and compare the primary method with Imam Muhammad's reduction method.

Core Idea
When bequests and loss overlap, Hanafi jurists recompute shares using 'awl and may further reduce by common divisors.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents a classic Hanafi faraid problem: a testator bequeaths half his estate to a slave (as freedom and payment), one-third to another, and one-sixth to a third. The estate consists of cash and the slave himself. After the testator's death, part of the property is lost, and a dispute arises about how to calculate the distribution. The author explains the initial calculation, the recalculation after loss, and notes an alternative method by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that reduces the shares by half due to common divisors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the estate and bequests
The estate is 2000: 1000 cash and a slave worth 1000. Bequests: half to the slave (i.e., freedom and sa'y), one-third to a legatee, one-sixth to another legatee limited to the 1000 cash.
The slave's bequest is not simple ownership; he becomes free but must work to pay off part of his value.
2
Compute the base number (asl al-masalah) for the initial scenario
Use LCM of denominators 2,3,6 = 12. Allocate: half=6, third=4, sixth=1, total 11. Since the third of the estate is used for bequests, multiply base by 3 to avoid fractions: total 33. Slave gets 6 from the third, plus from the whole half of his value etc.
The text then calculates fractions of the slave's freedom and sa'y.
3
Recalculate after loss of assets
Half the slave is claimed by someone else, half the cash is lost. Adjust the base for the third portion from 11 to 6. Then compute new totals: slave gets 3 shares (freed part), third legatee gets 2, sixth legatee gets 1, heirs get 14.
The loss proportionally affects the shares.
4
Examine Imam Muhammad's alternative method
Imam Muhammad notes that the shares of the third legatee (2) and the heirs (12) share a common divisor (2), as do the slave and debt. He reduces each by half, so the heirs' 14 becomes 7. This is a form of taqsir (reduction) to simplify the fractions.
This shows a difference in calculation methodology within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سبيل المنازعة بالإجماع لأن المنازعة لا تتحقق ههنا لأنه لا يجتمع في رقبة العبد وصيتان لأن حق الموصى له بالثلث في السعاية لا في الرقبة لأن الموح له بثلث مال مطلقة بمنزلة أحد الورثة وحق الورثة في السعاية إذا كان العبد موصى بعتقه لأنهم لا يملكون العبد الموصى بعتقه وإن كان لا يخرج من الثلث لأنه معتق البعض ومعتق البعض لا يملك وكذلك الموصى له بالثلث مرسلاً. وإذا لم يثبت حقه في رقبة العبد فلا تنازع في العبد فيقسم على سبيل العول والمضاربة لا على سبيل المنازعة والوجه فيه أن يحتاج إلى فريضة لها نصف وثلث وسدس لأن العبد موصی له بنصف ماله لأن ماله ألفان ألف وعبد قيمته ألف ولآخر ثلث ماله ولآخر سدس ماله وأقل حساب يخرج منه هذه السهام اثنا عشر فنصفه ستة وثلثه أربعة وسدسه سهم فيكون كله أحد عشر، فإذا صار الثلث على أحد عشر فصار الجميع ثلاثة وثلاثين فللعبد من ثلث المال ستة والعبد من جميع المال نصفه وذلك ستة عشر ونصف فيعتق منه ستة أجزاء ويسعى في عشرة ونصف سهم وللموصى سدس جزء واحد من أحد الثلث ويبقى اثنان وعشرون ضعف ذلك للورثة فقد استقام الثلث والثلثان . ولو استحق من له عشر وصيته نصف العبد وضاع نصف الألف فالثلث على ستة ثلاثة للعبد وسهمان لصاحب الثلث ومنهم لصاحب السدس لأنه لما استحق نصف العبد انتقصت نصف وصية العبد فبقيت وصيته في ثلاثة أسهم، ولما ضاع نصف الألف انتقص نصف وصية الموصى له بالثلث وهو سهمان لأنهما ضاعت عليه وعلى الورثة لأنه بمنزلة أحد الورثة ووصية صاحب السدس باقية على حالها في سهم واحد لأن وصيته مقيدة بألف فصار الهلاك مصروفاً إلى الورثة لأن تخرج من ثلث ماله إذا كان سدس الألف بعينها، فلما ضاع نصفها انقلب ثلثه سدس ما بقي لأن سدس الكل ثلث النصف، وإذا صار ثلث المال ستة صار الجميع ثمانية عشر ونصفه تسعة فيعتق من العبد ثلاثة أجزاء من تسعة ويسعى في ستة فيضم ذلك إلى النصف الآخر فيصير كله خمسة عشر للموصى له بالسدس سهم من تسعة من الخمسمائة الباقية يبقى أربعة عشر فيبقى المال على أربعة عشر سهمان لصاحب الثلث واثنا عشر للورثة. وخرج محمد على سبعة لأن بين نصيب صاحب الثلث وبين الورثة موافقة بالنصف فإن نصيب صاحب الثلث سهمان ونصيب الورثة اثنا عشر وبين العبد والدين موافقة بالنصف فاختصر نصيب كل واحد على نصفه فصار سبعة .
The path of dispute is by consensus because dispute is not realized here since two wills do not combine in the neck of the slave, because the right of the legatee of one-third is in the earning (sa'y) not in the neck, because the one bequeathed one-third of the entire property is like one of the heirs, and the right of the heirs is in the earning when the slave is bequeathed his freedom because they do not own the slave bequeathed his freedom even if he does not exit from one-third, because he is partially freed and the partially freed does not own, and likewise the legatee of one-third absolutely. And when his right in the neck of the slave is not established, there is no dispute concerning the slave, so it is divided on the basis of 'awl and mudaraba, not on the basis of dispute. The explanation of that: one needs to make a distribution that has a half, a third, and a sixth, because the slave is bequeathed half of his property, because his property is two thousand: a thousand and a slave worth a thousand, and to another one-third of his property, and to another one-sixth of his property. The smallest number from which these shares come is twelve: half of it is six, third four, sixth one, so total eleven. When the third is upon eleven, the total becomes thirty-three. For the slave from the third of the property is six, and the slave from all the property is half of that, which is sixteen and a half, so six parts of him are freed and he works for ten and a half shares. For the legatee of one-sixth is one share from one-third, and twenty-two remain, double that for the heirs, so the third and two-thirds are balanced. And if the one who has a tenth of his bequest claims half of the slave and half of the thousand is lost, then the third is upon six: three for the slave, two shares for the owner of one-third, and one for the owner of one-sixth, because when half the slave was claimed, half of the slave's bequest decreased, leaving his bequest in three shares, and when half the thousand was lost, half of the bequest of the legatee of one-third decreased, which is two shares, because they were lost on him and on the heirs, because he is like one of the heirs, and the bequest of the owner of one-sixth remains as it was in one share, because his bequest is limited to a thousand, so the loss is attributed to the heirs because it comes from the third of his property when it was one-sixth of the thousand specifically. When half of it was lost, his third became sixth of what remains, because sixth of the whole is third of the half. And when the third of the property became six, the total becomes eighteen, half of it nine, so three parts of the slave are freed from nine, and he works for six, and that is added to the other half, so it becomes all fifteen. For the legatee of one-sixth is one share from nine of the remaining five hundred, fourteen remain, so the wealth remains upon fourteen: two shares for the owner of one-third and twelve for the heirs. And Muhammad came out with seven because between the share of the owner of one-third and the heirs there is a half proportion: the share of the owner of one-third is two shares and the share of the heirs is twelve, and between the slave and the debt there is a half proportion, so he reduced each share by half, making it seven.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute and faraid calculation regarding a complex will where the testator bequeaths half his property to a slave (as a bequest of freedom and payment), one-third to another person, and one-sixth to a third person. The total estate is 2000: 1000 cash and a slave worth 1000. The commentator explains that since the right of the one-third legatee is in the earning (sa'y) of the slave, not in the slave himself, there is no conflict. The distribution is done on the basis of 'awl (proportional reduction) and mudaraba, not on the basis of dispute. The initial calculation uses 12 as the base: half (6), third (4), sixth (1) = 11. The third of the estate is then based on 11, making the total 33. The slave gets 6 from the third, and from the whole estate he gets half, which is 16.5; so 6 parts of him are freed, and he must work (sa'y) to earn 10.5 shares. The legatee of one-sixth gets 1 share from the third. The heirs get the remaining 22. Then a scenario of loss: half the slave is claimed by someone else, and half the cash is lost. The calculations are adjusted: the third becomes 6, etc. The final distribution: slave 3, one-third legatee 2, one-sixth legatee 1, heirs 14. However, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani calculates differently, reducing the numbers by half due to a proportion, arriving at 7 (instead of 14) for the heirs. This illustrates the Hanafi principle of taqsir (reduction) when the shares have common divisors.

Key Terms
السعاية (al-sa'y): The earning/labor that a partially freed slave undertakes to pay off his remaining value to the heirs or legatees.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the initial scenario (before loss), what base number is used for the distribution after adjusting for the one-third limitation?
A) 12
B) 11
C) 33
D) 6

Key Takeaway
Hanafi jurists resolve complex fractional bequests by adjusting the base and recalculating shares proportionally, with variations like Imam Muhammad's taqsir for simplification.

Guardian's Division Invalid Without Consent of Present Heirs
Core ruling on guardian's invalid division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a guardian's division of assets between present heirs is invalid without their consent, and identify the consequence of such invalid division.

Core Idea
Guardian's division invalid if heirs present and consent absent.

This lesson introduces a foundational principle in Hanafi inheritance law: a guardian cannot unilaterally divide assets between heirs who are present and have not consented. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents a case where the guardian pays one heir while the other is present, and the recipient denies receipt. We will parse the legal effect of such an invalid division.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and parties
The act is the guardian's payment of one thousand dirhams to one heir while the other heir is present. Note the parties: guardian (waṣī), two orphans (yatīmān), now matured.
2
Determine the ruling on the division
The text states 'because his division is not valid' (li-anna qismatahu lā tajūz). This is the key principle: the division is invalid because the heirs are present and did not consent.
The presence of the other heir at the time of payment invalidates the division.
3
Analyze the consequence for the guardian
Because the division is invalid, the guardian becomes liable. The text says he 'forfeits five hundred between them' (yaghramu l-waṣī khamsamī'at baynahumā). This means the guardian must pay five hundred dirhams out of his own pocket, which is then divided between the two heirs.
The guardian is not simply returning the money; he is paying a penalty for the invalid division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصي عنده ألفان ليتيمين فأدركا فدفع إلى أحدهما ألفاً وصاحبه الآخر حاضر وجحد القابض القبض منه يغرم الوصي خمسمائة بينهما لأن قسمته لا تجوز، ولو كان القابض مقراً كان للآخر أن يأخذ منه خمسمائة وإن شاء ضمن الوصي ورجع بها عليه لأنها لما لم تجز القسمة بقي الآخر شريكاً فيما قبضه صاحبه فله أن يأخذ نصيبه منه والوصي بالدفع صار ضامناً، ومتى أدى الضمان ملك المضمون وهو نصيب الجاحد رجع بنصيبه على صاحبه. ولو قال لهما بعدما كبرا قد دفعت إليكما ألفاً فصدقه أحدهما وكذبه الآخر رجع المنكر على أخيه بمائتين وخمسين درهماً، وإن أنكر لم يكن لهما على الولي شيء لأنه أمين ادعى رد الأمانة إلى صاحبها ولو قال الوصي دفعت إلى كل واحد منكما خمسمائة على حدة وصدقه أحدهما وكذبه الآخر رجع المكذب على الوصي بمائة وخمسين درهماً لأن قسمته لا تجوز عليهما وهما حاضران ولو كانا غائبين جازت القسمة عليهما. رجل مات وترك ابنين صغيرين فلما أدركا طلبا ميراثهما فقال الوصي جميع تركة أبيكما ألف على كل واحد منكما خمسمائة فصدقه أحدهما وكذبه الآخر رجع المكذب على المصدق بمائتين وخمسين ولا يرجع على الوصي في ذلك عند زفر وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة، وفي رواية عن ابن أبي مالك عن أبي يوسف أنه يرجع لأن الوصي أمين ادعى صرف الأمانة إلى نفقتهما وحاجتهما وهو مسلط عليه من جهة الشرع فيصدق فيه في حق براءة نفسه عن الضمان، ولا يصدق في إبطال حق المكذب فيما وصل إلى المقر بالنفقة فصار المقر مقراً بالشركة فيما وصل إليه وذلك خمسمائة . وقال أبو يوسف : لا يرجع المقر على المنكر بشيء والقول قول الوصي لأنه تصدق في الإنفاق على المنكر لأنه مسلط عليه وهو مأمور من جهة الشرع فيصدق فيه فثبت الإنفاق عليه فصار كأنه وصل إليه خمسمائة معاينة
A guardian has two thousand [dirhams] for two orphans, then they mature, so he pays one thousand to one of them while the other is present, and the recipient denies receipt from him—the guardian forfeits five hundred between them because his division is not valid. If the recipient admits [receipt], the other may take five hundred from him, and if he wishes, he may hold the guardian liable and then have recourse against him [the recipient], because since the division is invalid, the other remains a partner in what his companion received, so he may take his share from him, and the guardian by paying becomes guarantor. Whenever the guarantor pays, he owns the guaranteed amount—which is the share of the denier—and then he recovers his share from his companion. And if he [the guardian] says to them after they have matured, 'I have paid you one thousand,' and one confirms him and the other denies, the denier recovers two hundred and fifty dirhams from his brother. If he denies [the denial?], the two have nothing against the guardian because he is a trustee claiming to have returned the trust to its owner. And if the guardian says, 'I paid five hundred to each of you separately,' and one confirms and the other denies, the denier recovers one hundred and fifty dirhams from the guardian because his division is not valid while they are both present; if they were absent, the division would be valid against them. A man dies leaving two minor sons; when they mature, they request their inheritance and the guardian says, 'The entire estate of your father is one thousand: five hundred for each of you.' One confirms him, the other denies. The denier recovers two hundred and fifty from the confirmer and does not recover from the guardian according to Zufar and a narration from Abu Hanifa. In a narration from Ibn Abi Malik from Abu Yusuf, he does recover because the guardian is a trustee claiming to have spent the trust on their maintenance and needs, and he is authorized by the Law, so he is believed for his own exoneration from liability, but he is not believed to nullify the denier's right regarding what reached the confirmer as maintenance. So the confirmer becomes a confirmer of partnership in what reached him, which is five hundred. Abu Yusuf said: The confirmer does not recover anything from the denier, and the trustee's word is accepted because he is truthful in spending on the denier, as he is authorized and ordered by the Law, so he is believed and spending on him is established, as if five hundred had reached him visibly.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage presents multiple case scenarios (furūʿ) regarding disputes between a guardian and orphan heirs after they mature. The key principle is that the guardian's division of assets between two heirs is not valid without their consent when they are present. If one heir acknowledges receipt and the other denies, the denying heir can recover his share either from the acknowledging heir (if the guardian paid the denier's share to the acknowledging heir) or from the guardian (if the division was invalid). The rulings differ based on whether the guardian claims to have paid both equally or to have spent on maintenance. The passage also shows internal Hanafi disagreement: Zufar and a narration from Abu Hanifa say the denier cannot recover from the guardian if the guardian claims to have spent on both; Abu Yusuf in one narration says he can recover, but in another he says the guardian's word is accepted and the denier has no claim. The practical outcome depends on whether the guardian is believed about spending.

Key Terms
الوصي (al-waṣī): Guardian of minor orphans; in these cases, he is also managing the estate for two orphans.
القسمة (al-qisma): Division of assets between heirs or shareholders.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence of a guardian's division between two present heirs without their consent?
A) The division is valid but the guardian is sinful.
B) The division is invalid and the guardian forfeits a sum between the heirs.
C) The division is valid if the recipient admits receipt.
D) The division is invalid only if the other heir objects later.

Key Takeaway
A guardian's division of assets between present heirs is invalid unless they consent, making the guardian liable for compensation.

Heir's Options When Co-Heir Denies Receipt
Options for the denying heir when co-heir admits receipt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two options available to an heir when the other heir denies receiving his share from an invalid guardian division, and state the legal reason for each.

Core Idea
Denying heir can recover from receiving heir or hold guardian liable.

The previous lesson established that an invalid guardian division makes the guardian liable. This lesson examines the next scenario in the passage: if the recipient admits receipt, the other heir has a choice. He can either take his share directly from the receiving brother or hold the guardian liable and let the guardian recover from the brother. We will unpack the logic of partnership and guaranty underlying these options.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The guardian paid 1000 to one heir while the other was present. The recipient admits he received the 1000, but the other heir denies getting anything.
The denial is not about receipt but about receiving his own share.
2
State the first option for the denying heir
The text says 'the other may take five hundred from him' – meaning the denying heir can directly take his share (500) from the receiving brother because the invalid division leaves them as partners.
The 500 is half of the 1000 received, representing the denying heir's share.
3
State the second option
Alternatively, the denying heir 'may hold the guardian liable and then have recourse against him' – meaning he can sue the guardian for his 500, and then the guardian can recover that 500 from the receiving brother.
This is because the guardian by paying becomes a guarantor (ḍāmin) and then owns the right of recourse.
4
Explain the legal reasoning
Since the division was invalid, the assets remain jointly owned. Paying the whole sum to one heir does not transfer ownership of the other's share. The guardian's payment makes him liable (ḍamān), and upon paying, he steps into the denying heir's shoes to recover from the receiving heir.
The principle: 'the other remains a partner in what his companion received'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصي عنده ألفان ليتيمين فأدركا فدفع إلى أحدهما ألفاً وصاحبه الآخر حاضر وجحد القابض القبض منه يغرم الوصي خمسمائة بينهما لأن قسمته لا تجوز، ولو كان القابض مقراً كان للآخر أن يأخذ منه خمسمائة وإن شاء ضمن الوصي ورجع بها عليه لأنها لما لم تجز القسمة بقي الآخر شريكاً فيما قبضه صاحبه فله أن يأخذ نصيبه منه والوصي بالدفع صار ضامناً، ومتى أدى الضمان ملك المضمون وهو نصيب الجاحد رجع بنصيبه على صاحبه. ولو قال لهما بعدما كبرا قد دفعت إليكما ألفاً فصدقه أحدهما وكذبه الآخر رجع المنكر على أخيه بمائتين وخمسين درهماً، وإن أنكر لم يكن لهما على الولي شيء لأنه أمين ادعى رد الأمانة إلى صاحبها ولو قال الوصي دفعت إلى كل واحد منكما خمسمائة على حدة وصدقه أحدهما وكذبه الآخر رجع المكذب على الوصي بمائة وخمسين درهماً لأن قسمته لا تجوز عليهما وهما حاضران ولو كانا غائبين جازت القسمة عليهما. رجل مات وترك ابنين صغيرين فلما أدركا طلبا ميراثهما فقال الوصي جميع تركة أبيكما ألف على كل واحد منكما خمسمائة فصدقه أحدهما وكذبه الآخر رجع المكذب على المصدق بمائتين وخمسين ولا يرجع على الوصي في ذلك عند زفر وهو رواية عن أبي حنيفة، وفي رواية عن ابن أبي مالك عن أبي يوسف أنه يرجع لأن الوصي أمين ادعى صرف الأمانة إلى نفقتهما وحاجتهما وهو مسلط عليه من جهة الشرع فيصدق فيه في حق براءة نفسه عن الضمان، ولا يصدق في إبطال حق المكذب فيما وصل إلى المقر بالنفقة فصار المقر مقراً بالشركة فيما وصل إليه وذلك خمسمائة . وقال أبو يوسف : لا يرجع المقر على المنكر بشيء والقول قول الوصي لأنه تصدق في الإنفاق على المنكر لأنه مسلط عليه وهو مأمور من جهة الشرع فيصدق فيه فثبت الإنفاق عليه فصار كأنه وصل إليه خمسمائة معاينة
A guardian has two thousand [dirhams] for two orphans, then they mature, so he pays one thousand to one of them while the other is present, and the recipient denies receipt from him—the guardian forfeits five hundred between them because his division is not valid. If the recipient admits [receipt], the other may take five hundred from him, and if he wishes, he may hold the guardian liable and then have recourse against him [the recipient], because since the division is invalid, the other remains a partner in what his companion received, so he may take his share from him, and the guardian by paying becomes guarantor. Whenever the guarantor pays, he owns the guaranteed amount—which is the share of the denier—and then he recovers his share from his companion. And if he [the guardian] says to them after they have matured, 'I have paid you one thousand,' and one confirms him and the other denies, the denier recovers two hundred and fifty dirhams from his brother. If he denies [the denial?], the two have nothing against the guardian because he is a trustee claiming to have returned the trust to its owner. And if the guardian says, 'I paid five hundred to each of you separately,' and one confirms and the other denies, the denier recovers one hundred and fifty dirhams from the guardian because his division is not valid while they are both present; if they were absent, the division would be valid against them. A man dies leaving two minor sons; when they mature, they request their inheritance and the guardian says, 'The entire estate of your father is one thousand: five hundred for each of you.' One confirms him, the other denies. The denier recovers two hundred and fifty from the confirmer and does not recover from the guardian according to Zufar and a narration from Abu Hanifa. In a narration from Ibn Abi Malik from Abu Yusuf, he does recover because the guardian is a trustee claiming to have spent the trust on their maintenance and needs, and he is authorized by the Law, so he is believed for his own exoneration from liability, but he is not believed to nullify the denier's right regarding what reached the confirmer as maintenance. So the confirmer becomes a confirmer of partnership in what reached him, which is five hundred. Abu Yusuf said: The confirmer does not recover anything from the denier, and the trustee's word is accepted because he is truthful in spending on the denier, as he is authorized and ordered by the Law, so he is believed and spending on him is established, as if five hundred had reached him visibly.
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage presents multiple case scenarios (furūʿ) regarding disputes between a guardian and orphan heirs after they mature. The key principle is that the guardian's division of assets between two heirs is not valid without their consent when they are present. If one heir acknowledges receipt and the other denies, the denying heir can recover his share either from the acknowledging heir (if the guardian paid the denier's share to the acknowledging heir) or from the guardian (if the division was invalid). The rulings differ based on whether the guardian claims to have paid both equally or to have spent on maintenance. The passage also shows internal Hanafi disagreement: Zufar and a narration from Abu Hanifa say the denier cannot recover from the guardian if the guardian claims to have spent on both; Abu Yusuf in one narration says he can recover, but in another he says the guardian's word is accepted and the denier has no claim. The practical outcome depends on whether the guardian is believed about spending.

Key Terms
الضمان (al-ḍamān): Guaranty; the liability that the guardian incurs by paying the share to the wrong heir, making him able to recover from the true recipient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When a guardian's division is invalid and the recipient admits receipt, what legal relationship exists between the two heirs regarding the amount received?
A) The receiving heir owns the entire amount received.
B) The heirs are partners in the amount received.
C) The denying heir has no claim to that amount.
D) The guardian still owns the amount.

Key Takeaway
After an invalid division, the heirs remain partners in the distributed assets, giving the deprived heir the choice of recourse against the recipient or the guardian.

Guardian's Claim of Spending: Hanafi Internal Dispute
Internal Hanafi ikhtilaf on guardian's liability when claiming spending.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the internal Hanafi positions on whether a guardian's claim of spending on the orphans is accepted to absolve him from liability, and evaluate the practical consequences.

Core Idea
Hanafis differ on accepting guardian's claim of spending.

The passage concludes with a nuanced scenario where the guardian claims to have spent the detained money on the orphans' maintenance. This raises a critical question: is a trustee's word accepted regarding expenditure? The Hanafi school is not unanimous. We will analyze the views of Zufar, Abu Hanifa (in one narration), and Abu Yusuf (two narrations). This lesson sharpens your ability to identify and evaluate intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the guardian's claim
A man dies leaving two minor sons. When they mature, they ask for inheritance. The guardian says the total estate was 1000, and he has already spent it on their maintenance. One son confirms, the other denies. The guardian claims the entire 1000 was spent on both.
This is different from earlier cases because the guardian is not claiming he paid them; he claims he spent on their needs.
2
State the position of Zufar and one narration of Abu Hanifa
According to Zufar and a narration from Abu Hanifa, the denying son can recover 250 from the confirming son (his share of the 500 that the confirming son is deemed to have received), but cannot recover anything from the guardian.
The reasoning: the guardian is a trustee claiming to have spent, and his word is accepted for exonerating himself, but it does not invalidate the confirming son's admission of receiving his share.
3
State the position of Abu Yusuf in one narration
In a narration from Ibn Abi Malik from Abu Yusuf, the denying son can also recover from the guardian. Because the guardian's word is accepted for his own exoneration but not to nullify the denying son's right to what the confirming son received as 'maintenance' (i.e., the guardian's claim that he spent on the confirming son is not believed against the denying son).
Thus, the guardian remains liable to the extent of the denying son's share in the amount that reached the confirming son.
4
State the final view of Abu Yusuf (another narration)
The passage ends with: 'Abu Yusuf said: The confirmer does not recover anything from the denier, and the trustee's word is accepted.' This is a third view: the guardian is believed entirely, so the confirmor has no claim against the denier, and the denier has no claim against the guardian because spending is established on both.
This is likely the muftā bihī position, as the passage seems to conclude with it.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Zufar and first Abu Hanifa, the denying heir gets 250 from his brother. Under first Abu Yusuf, he gets 250 from the guardian as well. Under final Abu Yusuf, he gets nothing from either.
The dispute revolves around the evidentiary weight of the guardian's claim and the effect of the confirming son's admission.
