Determining the Sex of a Hermaphrodite: Precedence vs. Quantity of Urine
Defines khuntha and explains urination-based sex determination with intra-Hanafi dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rule for determining the sex of a hermaphrodite (khuntha) based on urination, distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding quantity, and apply the mufta bihi ruling to cases of sequential and simultaneous urination.

Core Idea
Sex is determined by the first organ to emit urine; quantity is irrelevant in the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Some individuals are born with both male and female genitalia. How does Islamic law determine their sex for purposes of inheritance, marriage, and other rulings? This lesson unpacks the classical Hanafi method: the evidence from the Prophet's hadith and a pre-Islamic story, the primary rule that urine from one organ establishes sex, and the intra-Hanafi dispute when both organs emit urine—does precedence alone decide, or should we consider the quantity? You will learn why Imam Abu Hanifa rejected quantity as a valid criterion and why this remains the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Define the khuntha and the foundational rule
Understand that a khuntha has both a male organ (dhakar) and a female organ (farj). The basic rule from the Prophet (peace be upon him) is that sex is determined by which organ urine emerges from. Confirm this with the pre-Islamic story that the Prophet approved.
The hadith is: 'How should he inherit? From where he urinates.'
2
Apply the rule when urine comes from both: precedence
If the hermaphrodite urinates from both organs—first from one, then later from the other—the ruling goes to the organ that emitted first. The first emission is a complete sign that the organ is original.
Agreed by Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
3
Analyze the dispute on equal urination: quantity vs. no quantity
If both organs urinate simultaneously, there is no precedence. Here the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) would attribute sex to the organ producing more urine, based on the principle 'the majority has the ruling of the whole' and that quantity indicates originality. Abu Hanifa rejects this: quantity depends on outlet width, not originality, and the emission itself is the sign—quantity cannot preponderate, just as with witnesses.
Abu Hanifa famously asked: 'Have you seen a judge weighing urine in ounces?'
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, simultaneous urination leaves the person ambiguous (mushkil) with no determination until other signs appear. Under the Sahibayn, sex is determined by majority urine. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view, so for fatwa, quantity is ignored.
The author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq implies tarjih by criticizing the consideration of quantity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الخنثى هو من له فرج وذكر فإن بال من الذكر فغلام وإن بال من الفرج فانثى لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام سأل كيف يورث فقال: من حيث يبول. وعن علي الله عنه مثله . أن قاضياً . العرب في الجاهلية رفع عليه هذه الواقعة فجعل يقول هو ذكر وامرأة فاستبعد قوله ذلك فتحير ودخل فجعل يتقلب على فراشه ولا يأخذه النوم لتحيره وكانت له بنت تغمز رجله فسألته عن ذكره فأخبرها بذلك فقالت : دع واتبع الحكم المبال فخرج إلى قومه فحكى لهم ذلك فاستحسنوا فعرف بذلك أن هذا الحكم كان في الجاهلية فأقره الشرع، ولأن البول من أي عضو كان فهو دليل على أنه هو والأصلي الصحيح والآخر بمنزلة العيب. قال رحمه الله : (فإن بال منهما فالحكم للأسبق لأنه دليل على أنه العضو الأصلي، ولأنه كما خرج البول حكم بموجبه . لأنه علامة تامة فلا يتغير بعد ذلك بخروج البول من الآلة الأخرى. قال رحمه الله: (فإن استويا) أي في السبق فمشكل لعدم المرجح . رحمه الله : ( ولا عبرة بالكثرة) وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وقالا ينسب إلى أكثرهما بولاً لأنه قال يدل على أنه العضو الأصلي ولأن للأكثر حكم الكل في أصول الشرع فيترجح بالكثرة. وله أن كثرة ما يخرج ليس بدليل على الآلة لأن ذلك لاتساع المخرج وضيقه لا لأنه هو العضو الأصلي، ولأن نفس الخروج دليل بنفسه فالكثرة لا يقع بها الترجيح عند المعارضة كالشاهدين والأربعة، وقد استقبح أبو حنيفة اعتبار ذلك فقال : هل رأيت قاضياً يكيل البول بالأواقي؟
The Book of the Hermaphrodite. The hermaphrodite is one who has a female organ and a male organ. If he urinates from the male organ, he is a boy; if from the female organ, she is a girl because the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked how to inherit and said: from where he urinates. And from Ali (may God be pleased with him) similar. That a judge of the Arabs in pre-Islamic times was presented with this case and kept saying he is a male and female, found his statement improbable, became confused, entered, turned on his bed unable to sleep due to confusion, and he had a daughter who massaged his leg; she asked about his matter and he informed her, so she said: leave it and follow the rule of urine. He went out to his people and related that to them, and they approved it, so it became known that this ruling existed in pre-Islamic times and the Law confirmed it. And because urine from any organ is evidence that it is the original and sound [organ], and the other is like a defect. He (the author) said, may God have mercy on him: (If he urinates from both, the ruling is for the earlier [urination] because it is evidence that it is the original organ, and because as soon as urine came out, it is ruled by its implication, for it is a complete sign and does not change thereafter by urine coming from the other organ. He (the author) said, may God have mercy on him: (If they are equal) i.e., in precedence, then it is problematic due to lack of preponderance. He (the author) said, may God have mercy on him: (And no consideration is given to quantity) and this is according to Abu Hanifa, while the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is attributed to the one from which most urine comes, because they said it indicates that it is the original organ, and because the greater quantity has the ruling of the whole in the principles of the Law, so it is given preponderance by quantity. And for him (Abu Hanifa) that the quantity of what comes out is not evidence for the organ because that is due to the width or narrowness of the outlet, not because it is the original organ; and because the very emission is evidence in itself, so quantity does not give preponderance in case of conflict, like two witnesses and four. And Abu Hanifa regarded consideration of that as objectionable, saying: Have you seen a judge weighing urine in ounces?
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on how to determine the sex of a hermaphrodite (khuntha) when both organs are present. The author first defines khuntha and states the primary rule: sex is determined by which organ urine comes from, based on the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and a pre-Islamic story confirmed by sharia. The rationale is that the urinating organ is the original, functional one, while the other is like a defect. If urine comes from both, the ruling is for the one that emitted first, as it is a complete sign that does not change later. If both urinate simultaneously, it becomes problematic (mushkil) because there is no preponderance. Then comes the dispute: Abu Hanifa says no consideration is given to the quantity of urine; the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is attributed to the one from which most urine comes, because quantity indicates originality and because the greater part has the ruling of the whole in sharia principles. Abu Hanifa responds that quantity is not evidence because it depends on the width of the outlet, not originality, and that the emitted urine itself is evidence, so quantity does not preponderate, just as with witnesses. He even criticizes weighing urine in ounces as an absurd analogy. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is generally Abu Hanifa's view: quantity is not considered; only precedence matters.

Key Terms
خنثى (khuntha): A person who has both male and female genital organs.
فرج (farj): The female genital organ (vagina).
ذكر (dhakar): The male genital organ (penis).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a hermaphrodite urinates from both organs simultaneously, how is the sex determined?
A) By which organ produced more urine.
B) The person is considered ambiguous (mushkil).
C) The person is considered male because the male organ is the default.
D) The person is considered female because the female organ is more common.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the sex of a hermaphrodite is determined by the organ from which urine first emerges; if both emerge simultaneously, the person remains ambiguous (mushkil) and quantity of urine is not considered.

Inheritance with a Khuntha and Conflicting Claims
Faraid case: a man dies leaving a son, a khuntha, and a wife; then khuntha dies with conflicting claims on gender.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares of a khuntha when there is a conflicting claim about the khuntha's gender and apply the Hanafi rule for resolving such conflicts.

Core Idea
In khuntha inheritance, the brother's claim is initially accepted with an oath, unless physical evidence (urination) overrides.

This lesson deals with a complex scenario in Hanafi faraid where a khuntha dies after inheriting from the father, and the mother and surviving brother disagree on the khuntha's gender. We will trace the inheritance calculations and see how the Hanafi school resolves conflicting claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs of the father
List all surviving heirs: the known son, the khuntha, and the wife. Note that the wife is also the mother of the khuntha.
2
Calculate the base inheritance from the father
The wife takes 1/8. The residue (7/8) is divided between the son and the khuntha. But the share depends on the khuntha's gender: if male, the residue is split equally (each 7/16); if female, she receives half the son's share (son 7/12, daughter 7/24).
The text uses fractions like 'half after the eighth' for the male scenario.
3
Determine the second inheritance (from the khuntha)
The khuntha dies, leaving the mother (the wife) and the brother (the known son). The mother inherits 1/3 of the khuntha's share, the brother inherits 2/3.
This is standard Hanafi faraid for heirs: mother and brother.
4
Analyze the conflicting claims
The mother claims the khuntha was male (so she gets a larger share from the khuntha). The brother claims the khuntha was female (giving him a larger share).
The dispute affects the final distribution.
5
Apply the Hanafi evidentiary rule
Initially, the brother's statement is accepted (he must swear an oath that he does not know the khuntha was male). However, if either party brings physical evidence of urination signs (male or female), that evidence overrides the presumption.
This rule is based on the principle that the ambiguous state (khuntha) is resolved by the most reliable indicator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رجل مات وترك ذكراً وخنثى وزوجة فمات الخنثى بعد موت أبيه فادعت أم الخنثى أنه ذكر وأنه كان ورث من أبيه نصف المال بعد الثمن لأنه مات وترك ابنين وامرأة ثم مات الخنثى فورثت ثلث ذلك النصف لأن الخنثى مات وترك أماً وأخاً ترث الأم ثلث ذلك النصف وقال ابن الميت وهو أخ الخنثى لا بل كانت الخنثى جارية وورثت الثلث من الميت بعد الثمن ثم ماتت فورثت أنت ثلث ذلك فالقول قول أخي الخنثى إلا أن الأخ يستحلف على العلم بالله ما تعلم أنه كان ذكراً. وإذا قامت الأم البينة أنه كان يبول من مبال الرجال ولا يبول من مبال النساء فإنه يرث أبيه ميراث النصف بعد الثمن، ثم ترث الأم ثلث ذلك النصف من الخنثى. وإن أقام أخ من الخنثى البينة أنه يبول من مبال النساء ولا يبول من مبال الرجال وأنها ورثت الثلث من الأب بعد الثمن فلأم الخنثى ذلك الثلث
A man died leaving a (known) male, a khuntha, and a wife. Then the khuntha died after the death of his/her father. The mother of the khuntha claimed that it was a male and that it inherited from its father half of the property after the eighth (the wife's share), because he died leaving two sons and a woman (wife). Then the khuntha died, so she (the mother) inherited one third of that half, because the khuntha died leaving a mother and a brother; the mother inherits one third of that half. The son of the deceased (the brother of the khuntha) said: "No, rather the khuntha was a female, and she inherited one third from the deceased after the eighth, then she died, so you (the brother) inherited one third of that." So the statement is the statement of the brother of the khuntha, except that the brother is required to swear an oath by Allah: "I do not know that it was male." If the mother brings evidence that the khuntha used to urinate from the place of men and did not urinate from the place of women, then he inherits from his father half after the eighth, then the mother inherits one third of that half from the khuntha. If the brother of the khuntha brings evidence that it used to urinate from the place of women and did not urinate from the place of men, and that she inherited one third from the father after the eighth, then the mother of the khuntha receives that one third.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This is a complex inheritance case involving a khuntha. The father dies leaving a known son, a khuntha, and a wife. The khuntha then dies. The khuntha's mother (who is also the wife) claims the khuntha was male to maximize her inheritance from the khuntha. If the khuntha was male, he inherited half of the residue after the wife's eighth (i.e., 7/16 of the estate). Upon his death, his mother (the wife) inherits one third of his share, and the brother inherits two thirds. But the brother claims the khuntha was female, in which case she inherited only one third of the residue (7/24). Upon her death, the brother claims he inherited one third of her share (7/72) and the mother gets the rest. The text holds that the brother's statement is accepted (with an oath), because he is the one claiming a lesser share for the mother? Actually it says the statement is the brother's, but he must swear he does not know the khuntha was male. If either party brings evidence based on urination signs, that evidence overrides the presumption, and the ruling follows the evidence. The case illustrates how the Hanafi school handles conflicting claims by taking into account the burden of proof and the presumption of continuity (istishab) of the ambiguous state.

Key Terms
خنثى (khuntha): A person with ambiguous gender, neither clearly male nor female.
ميراث (mīrāth): Inheritance shares.
بينة (bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two females.

Ruling on Dispute over Khuntha's Gender: Brother's Statement Accepted with Oath
Ruling on acceptance of brother's statement in gender dispute of deceased khuntha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the mother and brother dispute the gender of a deceased khuntha, and identify the condition attached to accepting the brother's statement.

Core Idea
In a dispute over a khuntha's gender, the brother's claim is accepted but he must swear he does not know otherwise.

When a khuntha dies, his or her gender affects inheritance shares. If the mother claims the khuntha was male and the brother claims female, which statement prevails? The Hanafi school gives preference to the brother's statement, but with a condition: he must swear an oath that he has no knowledge of the khuntha being male. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
The mother claims the khuntha was male; the brother claims the khuntha was female. The inheritance distribution depends on whose claim is accepted.
The text mentions specific fractions but the core issue is gender determination.
2
Recognize the default rule
The Hanafi rule is 'al-qawl qawl al-akh' – the brother's statement is taken as true in this context.
This is a specific application of the broader maxim that the word of the closer relative is accepted on matters of lineage and status.
3
Note the exception
The brother's statement is not accepted unconditionally; he must swear an oath by Allah that he does not know the khuntha was male. This is called istihlaf 'ala al-ilm.
The oath is on knowledge, not on certainty – he swears he has no knowledge to the contrary.
4
Understand the rationale
The brother is presumed to have closer knowledge of the khuntha's gender due to upbringing and daily association, outweighing the mother's claim.
This presumption is specific to Hanafi fiqh; other schools may differ.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ذلك النصف لأن الخنثى مات وترك أماً وأخاً ترث الأم ثلث ذلك النصف وقال ابن الميت وهو أخ الخنثى لا بل كانت الخنثى جارية وورثت الثلث من الميت بعد الثمن ثم ماتت فورثت أنت ثلث ذلك فالقول قول أخي الخنثى إلا أن الأخ يستحلف على العلم بالله ما تعلم أنه كان ذكراً.
That half, because the khuntha died and left a mother and a brother; the mother inherits one-third of that half. And the son of the deceased, who is the brother of the khuntha, said: 'No, rather the khuntha was a girl, and she inherited one-third from the deceased after the eighth, then she died, so you inherited one-third of that.' So the word is the word of the brother of the khuntha, except that the brother is sworn by Allah regarding his knowledge: 'You do not know that he was male.'
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This is a ruling statement regarding a dispute over the gender of a deceased khuntha. The mother claims the khuntha was male, which would give her a different inheritance share. The brother claims it was female. The text rules that the brother's statement is accepted, but he must take an oath that he does not know it was male. This is because the brother, being a close relative, is presumed to have knowledge of the khuntha's gender from upbringing or observation. The oath of knowledge (istiḥlāf ʻalā al-ʻilm) is a form of swearing that one does not have knowledge to the contrary. The ruling upholds the brother's claim, affecting inheritance distribution.

Key Terms
الخنثى (al-khunthā): A hermaphrodite, a person with ambiguous or both male and female genitalia.
القول قول فلان (al-qawl qawl fulān): A legal maxim meaning 'the word of so-and-so is accepted' (i.e., their statement is taken as true) in the absence of contrary evidence.

Evidence of Urination Pattern and Marriage Claims Involving a Khuntha
Rulings on evidence of urination pattern and a marriage claim for a khuntha.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that evidence of urination pattern determines the khuntha's gender for inheritance, and evaluate the effect of a marriage claim on inheritance and dower.

Core Idea
A khuntha's gender is determined by evidence of urination pattern, affecting inheritance shares and the validity of a marriage claim.

This lesson examines three scenarios from Hanafi fiqh concerning a khuntha (intersex person). The first two involve conflicting evidence about urination pattern, which fixes the khuntha's gender for inheritance. The third involves a man claiming marriage to the khuntha with evidence, and how this affects inheritance and dower.

Guided Path
1
Identify the evidence presented
Determine who brings the evidence (mother, brother, or husband) and what it proves about urination pattern or marriage.
Evidence is bayyinah, typically two male witnesses.
2
Determine the gender implied
Based on urination pattern evidence, classify the khuntha as male or female for inheritance purposes.
Urinating from male organ indicates male; from female organ indicates female.
3
Apply the inheritance shares
Calculate the shares from the father's estate and from the khuntha's own estate based on gender.
Male khuntha inherits half of father's estate after the mother's eighth; female khuntha inherits one-third after the eighth.
4
Handle the marriage claim
If a man brings evidence of marriage to the khuntha, his claim is accepted, he must pay the dower, and he inherits as a husband. The mother inherits from the dower and the rest of the estate.
The mother's lack of counter-evidence leads to acceptance of the husband's word.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا قامت الأم البينة أنه كان يبول من مبال الرجال ولا يبول من مبال النساء فإنه يرث أبيه ميراث النصف بعد الثمن، ثم ترث الأم ثلث ذلك النصف من الخنثى. وإن أقام أخ من الخنثى البينة أنه يبول من مبال النساء ولا يبول من مبال الرجال وأنها ورثت الثلث من الأب بعد الثمن فلأم الخنثى ذلك الثلث وإن أقام رجل البينة أن أبا الخنثى كان زوجها منه على ألف درهم وطلب ميراثها وصدقه الابن أو كذبه ولم تقم الأم البينة أن أب الخنثى على ما ادعت فإنه يقبل قول الزوج ويجعل عليه المهر وورث من الخنثى ميراث الزوج وورث أم الخنثى من الصداق الذي يبقى على الزوج وما ترك الخنثى.
And if the mother brings evidence that he used to urinate from the place of urination of men and does not urinate from the place of urination of women, then he inherits from his father the inheritance of a half after the eighth; then the mother inherits one-third of that half from the khuntha. And if a brother of the khuntha brings evidence that he urinates from the place of urination of women and does not urinate from the place of urination of men, and that she inherited one-third from the father after the eighth, then for the mother of the khuntha that one-third. And if a man brings evidence that the father of the khuntha had married him (the khuntha) to him for a thousand dirhams and demands her inheritance, and the son (the brother of the khuntha) verifies him or denies him, and the mother does not bring evidence that the father of the khuntha was as she claimed, then the word of the husband is accepted, and the dower is made binding on him, and he inherits from the khuntha the inheritance of a husband, and the mother of the khuntha inherits from the dower that remains due from the husband and what the khuntha left.
Source pages p. 339

Commentary
This passage presents three scenarios. First, if the mother provides evidence that the khuntha urinates as a male, then the khuntha is considered male for inheritance from his father, inheriting half after subtracting the eighth (the father's estate was already divided with a share for the khuntha's mother?). Then the mother inherits from the khuntha as a male's mother. Second, if the brother provides evidence of female urination, the khuntha is considered female, and the mother inherits one-third from the original paternal estate. Third, if a man claims marriage to the khuntha with evidence, and the mother has no counter evidence, the man's claim is accepted, he pays the dower and inherits as a husband, and the mother inherits from the dower debt and the rest of the khuntha's estate. The acceptance of the husband's word is based on the principle of tasdiq (corroboration) in marriage claims.

Key Terms
البينة (al-bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two females, presented to prove a claim.
الصداق (al-ṣidāq): The dower or bride price given by the husband to the wife in a marriage contract.
الخنثى (al-khunthā): An intersex person who has both male and female genitalia or ambiguous genitalia.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Inheritance Claims Involving a Khuntha: Need for Evidence
Ruling on inheritance claims for a khuntha with disputed gender

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding inheritance claims by a mother or executor for a khuntha when other heirs deny, and identify the requirement of independent evidence (bayyinah).

Core Idea
In inheritance disputes, a khuntha's gender claim requires proof, not just executor affirmation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with a delicate situation: a khuntha's gender is ambiguous, and after death, claims about inheritance shares arise. The ruling distinguishes between cases where the khuntha is deceased or alive, but consistently requires independent evidence (bayyinah) to support a claim of male status. Even the executor's affirmation is insufficient if other heirs deny. This lesson unpacks the two scenarios and the underlying principle of protecting the rights of all heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage carefully. The first scenario involves both father and khuntha deceased; the mother claims the khuntha was a boy. The second scenario involves the khuntha alive claiming to be a boy. Note the difference.
The khuntha's gender is unknown; the claim alters inheritance shares.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
For the first scenario, the judge says the mother is not believed; she is liable for what she claimed. For the second, the judge does not give inheritance without evidence (bayyinah).
The executor's affirmation does not change the ruling.
3
Explain the underlying principle
The principle is that in property claims, especially those affecting others' shares, mere assertion is insufficient. Independent evidence is required to avoid injustice.
This protects the rights of other heirs who deny.
4
Note the role of the executor (wasi)
The executor is appointed by the father but his confession does not bind other heirs. The judge does not accept his affirmation alone.
The executor's duty is to manage the estate, not to decide gender disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو مات أبو الخنثى ثم مات هذا الخنثى فادعت أمه ميراث غلام وأقر الوصي بذلك وجحد بقية الورثة وقالوا هي جارية قال : إذا جاءت الدعوى في الأموال لم يصدق وعلى الأم على ما ادعى. وإن كان هذا الخنثى حياً لم يمت فقال أنا غلام وطلب ميراث غلام من أبيه وصدقه الوصي في ذلك وأنكر بقية الورثة ذلك وقالوا هي جارية قال : لا أعطيه ميراث غلام ولا أصدقه على ذلك إلا ببينة.
And if the father of the khuntha died, then this khuntha died, and his mother claimed inheritance of a boy, and the executor affirmed that, and the rest of the heirs denied it and said she is a girl, he said: when the claim comes regarding property, he is not believed, and the mother is [liable] for what she claimed. And if this khuntha is alive and did not die, and said 'I am a boy' and demanded inheritance of a boy from his father, and the executor affirmed him in that, and the rest of the heirs denied that and said she is a girl, he said: I do not give him inheritance of a boy nor do I believe him in that except with evidence.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage is a ruling about inheritance disputes involving a khuntha. Two scenarios: (1) Both father and khuntha have died; the mother claims the khuntha was a boy (entitled to double share of a girl), and the executor agrees, but other heirs deny. The qadi states that in property claims, the mother's claim alone (even with executor) is not sufficient to override the denial of other heirs; she is liable for what she claimed (i.e., if she took property, she must return it). (2) If the khuntha is alive and claims to be a boy seeking inheritance, the qadi does not accept his claim without independent evidence (bayyinah), even if the executor agrees. This shows caution in inheritance matters due to the ambiguity of the khuntha's gender.

Key Terms
وصي (wasi): Executor of the will or guardian appointed by the deceased father.
جحد (jahada): Denial or rejection of a claim by the heirs.
بينة (bayyinah): Clear evidence, typically two male witnesses or one male and two females in financial matters.

Khuntha Inheritance: The Lesser of Two Shares
Establishing the Hanafi principle for khuntha inheritance: give the lesser of the male and female shares

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of 'aqall al-nasibayn' to calculate the inheritance share of an ambiguous khuntha in given scenarios.

Core Idea
A khuntha inherits the lesser of the male/female shares because ownership cannot be established with doubt.

This lesson introduces the Hanafi rule for ambiguous khuntha inheritance. When a person's gender is indeterminate, the shari'ah gives them the lesser of the two possible shares to avoid giving more than is certain. The passage provides examples and contrasts with the view of al-Sha'bi and Ibn Abbas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
State the Hanafi principle: 'aqall al-nasibayn' – the khuntha receives the smaller of his/her hypothetical male and female shares. This is the mufta bihi ruling.
The principle is based on certainty: inheritance is a new ownership, so doubt prevents awarding the larger share.
2
Understand the Rationale
The text argues that ownership (milk) cannot be established with doubt. Since the khuntha's gender is unknown, we give only the certain minimum. This is contrasted with ambiguous manumission/divorce where distribution of possibilities is accepted.
The key difference: inheritance creates new rights, while manumission/divorce involve rights already in effect.
3
Work Through Examples
Analyze each of the four examples to see how the lesser share is computed: (1) two full brothers, (2) husband, mother, sister, (3) husband, mother, uterine brothers, full brother, (4) son's son and uncle. In each, the khuntha's share is the smaller of the two estimates.
In example 4, the khuntha gets nothing because as female she is excluded, which is the lesser amount.
4
Compare with Opposing View
Al-Sha'bi and Ibn Abbas hold that the khuntha receives half of the male share and half of the female share, averaging the possibilities. Understand their proof based on ambiguous scenarios in manumission and divorce.
The Hanafi rebuttal: inheritance is different because it involves new entitlement, not distribution of existing rights.
5
Evaluate the Practical Consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis give a lower amount; the opposing view gives a middle amount. The Hanafi position is operative (mufta bihi) to protect against overpayment.
This principle applies in all faraid calculations involving an ambiguous khuntha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قال رحمه الله : (وله أقل النصيبين) يعني لو مات أبوه كان له الأقل من نصيب الذكر الأنثى فإنه ينظر نصيبه على أنه ذكر وعلى أنه أنثى فيعطى الأقل منهما، وإن كان محروماً على أحد التقديرين فلا شيء له؛ مثاله أخوان لأب وأم أحدهما خنثى مشكل كان المال بينهما أثلاثاً للأخ الثلثان وللخنثى الثلث فيقدر أنثى لأنه أقل، ولو قدر ذكراً كان له النصف. ولو تركت امرأة زوجاً وأماً وأختاً لأب وأم . خنثى كان للزوج النصف وللأم الثلث من النصف الباقي وللخنثى ما بقي وهو السدس على أنه غصبة، ولو قدر أنثى كان له النصف وكانت المسألة تعول إلى ثمانية. ولو تركت زوجاً وأماً وأخوين من أم وأخاً لأب وأم هو خنثى كان للزوج النصف وللأم السدس وللأخوين لأم الثلث ولا شيء للخنثى لأنه عصبة ولم يفضل له شيء، ولو قدر أنثى كان له النصف فعالت المسألة إلى تسعة. ولو ترك الرجل ولد أخ هو الخنثى وعماً لأب وأم أو لأب كان المال للعم وقدر الخنثى أنثى لأن بنت الأخ لا ترث، ولو قدر ذكراً كان المال له دون العم لأن ابن الأخ مقدم على العم. وقال الشعبي : للخنثى نصف ميراث ذكر ونصف ميراث أنثى. وعن ابن عباس مثله لأنه مجهول والتوزيع على أحوال عند الجهل طريق معهودة في الشرع كما في العتق المبهم، والطلاق المبهم إذا تعذر البيان فيه بموت الموقع قبل البيان. ولنا أن الحاجة إلى إثبات الملك ابتداء فلا يثبت مع الشك فصار كما إذا كان الشك في وجوب المال بسبب آخر غير الميراث بخلاف المستشهد به الاستحقاق متيقن به وهو الإنشاء السابق ومحلية كل واحد من العبدين والمعتقين سبب بحكم ذلك السبب ثابت لكل واحد منهما على السواء من غير ترجيح أحدهما على الآخر بالشك.
And he (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And he has the lesser of the two shares' means if his father died, he gets the lesser of the share of a male or a female. So his share is considered as if he is a male and as if he is a female, and he is given the lesser of them. If he is excluded on one estimate, then nothing for him. Example: two full brothers, one of them an ambiguous khuntha: the wealth is divided into thirds: for the brother two-thirds, for the khuntha one-third, considering him female because it is less; if considered male, he would get half. And if a woman left a husband, a mother, and a full sister who is a khuntha: the husband gets half, the mother gets a third of the remaining half, and the khuntha gets what remains which is a sixth as a residuary; if considered female, she would get half and the case would 'awl to eight. And if a woman left a husband, a mother, two uterine brothers, and a full brother who is a khuntha: the husband gets half, the mother a sixth, the uterine brothers a third, and nothing for the khuntha because he is a residuary and nothing remains; if considered female, she would get half and the case would 'awl to nine. And if a man left a son's son who is a khuntha and a full or agnatic paternal uncle, the wealth goes to the uncle, and the khuntha is considered female because a son's daughter does not inherit; if considered male, the wealth would go to him over the uncle because a son's son takes precedence. And al-Sha'bi said: the khuntha gets half the inheritance of a male and half of a female. And from Ibn 'Abbas similar, because he is unknown, and distribution according to possibilities when in ignorance is a recognized method in shari'ah, as in ambiguous manumission and ambiguous divorce when clarification is impossible due to the death of the initiator before clarification. Our proof: the need to establish ownership from the beginning, so it is not established with doubt; it becomes like doubt regarding the obligation of property due to a cause other than inheritance, unlike the cited analogy: entitlement is certain, it is the prior creation, and the subject of each of the slaves and the emancipators is a cause, by that cause's ruling it is established for each equally without preferring one over the other by doubt.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling with proof. It establishes the Hanafi principle for the ambiguous khuntha's inheritance: he/she receives the lesser of the two possible shares (male or female). The author (Rahmatullah) states 'and he has the lesser of the two shares' and explains: when the father dies, calculate the khuntha's hypothetical share as a male and as a female, then give the smaller amount. If on one estimate he is excluded (e.g., as a female in some scenarios), then nothing is given. Examples illustrate: (1) Two full brothers: if both were male, they'd share equally; but as khuntha, he is considered female (since that gives less) so he gets 1/3 vs brother's 2/3. (2) Heirs: husband, mother, and sister (khuntha): husband gets 1/2, mother gets 1/3 of the remainder, khuntha gets 1/6 as residuary; if considered female, she would get 1/2 and the fractions would exceed 1 ('awl) to 8. (3) Heirs: husband, mother, two uterine brothers, and full brother (khuntha): as male, he gets nothing because residue is consumed by others; as female, she would get 1/2 causing 'awl to 9. (4) A man leaves a son's son (khuntha) and a paternal uncle: as female, she doesn't inherit (since daughter's son is not an heir? Actually here بنت الأخ means 'son's daughter'? The text says 'ولد أخ هو الخنثى' meaning the child of a brother is the khuntha. So 'ولد أخ' is a brother's child. If khuntha is female, she is not a residuary in presence of uncle, so uncle inherits. If male, he is a residuary and excludes uncle. So the lesser share is to treat as female (nothing). Then the view of al-Sha'bi and Ibn Abbas is mentioned: they say give half of male's inheritance and half of female's. This is rejected by Hanafis because ownership cannot be established based on doubt; the khuntha's gender is unknown, so we give the certain minimum. The Hanafi response: in manumission and divorce ambiguity, the person distributes shares among possibilities, but inheritance is different because entitlement here is certain only to the extent of the lesser share.

Key Terms
أقل النصيبين (aqall al-nasibayn): The lesser of the two shares; the khuntha gets the smaller of his possible male or female shares.
عول (awl): Proportional reduction of shares when the total exceeds the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Quran explicitly commands it
B) Because inheritance is a new ownership that cannot be established with doubt
C) Because the khuntha is considered female by default in all cases
D) Because the khuntha can later sue for the difference

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle of 'aqall al-nasibayn' ensures that an ambiguous khuntha inherits only the certain minimum, avoiding overpayment based on doubt.

Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's Takhrij of al-Sha'bi's View on Khuntha Inheritance
Intra-Hanafi dispute on calculation method for al-Sha'bi's khuntha ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in deriving al-Sha'bi's ruling for khuntha inheritance and apply Abu Yusuf's calculation of 4:3 shares.

Core Idea
In faraid, when a khuntha inherits, Abu Yusuf calculates by considering each heir's hypothetical solo share — giving male 4/7 and khuntha 3/7 out of seven.

The standard Hanafi rule for a khuntha is to give the lesser share (treat as female), giving the son double the khuntha. But Imam al-Sha'bi offered a different approach: give the khuntha half of what a male would get and half of what a female would get. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad both accepted al-Sha'bi's statement but disagreed on how to implement it. In this lesson, we explore Abu Yusuf's method and the resulting inheritance ratio.

Guided Path
1
Recall the Standard Hanafi Rule
The default Hanafi position: when a son and a khuntha inherit together, the son takes twice the share of the khuntha (treating khuntha as female). This is the 'least share' principle.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Recognize al-Sha'bi's Alternative
Al-Sha'bi says: give the khuntha half the inheritance of a male and half the inheritance of a female. This statement does not specify the calculation method.
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad both accept this statement but differ in its takhrij.
3
Learn Abu Yusuf's Method
Abu Yusuf calculates by considering: what share would the son get if he were alone? What share would the khuntha get if alone (using the lesser of the two possible shares)? Then he combines these to find the ratio.
The text cuts off but the result is a 4:3 split in favor of the son out of 7 shares.
4
Understand Muhammad's Alternative View
Muhammad disagreed and had a different method (not detailed in this passage). His method would yield a different distribution ratio.
The author does not give tarjih; the standard Hanafi rule remains in effect for fatwa.
5
Apply the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: with Abu Yusuf's method, the son gets 4/7 and the khuntha 3/7, whereas Muhammad's method would give different fractions. This shows how ikhtilaf within the school affects calculation.
In practice, the standard rule (2:1) is followed unless a mufti adopts al-Sha'bi's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the interpretation of al-Sha'bi's view on khuntha inheritance. The author (Marghinani) first restates the Hanafi principle: if the father dies leaving a son and a khuntha, the son gets two shares and the khuntha one (i.e., the khuntha is treated as female, giving the lesser share). Then he mentions that al-Sha'bi says give half of male's inheritance and half of female's. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad debated how to implement that. According to the text, Abu Yusuf's method: consider the shares if each heir were alone. The male alone would take the whole (say 1), the khuntha alone (as male or female?) The text is cut off but it says 'four for the male and three for the khuntha' from seven. This likely means: male alone takes 1 (or 7/7), khuntha alone as male takes? Actually the calculation: if the male were alone, he gets all; if the khuntha were alone, he would get? Possibly the khuntha as male gets 1, as female gets 1? This requires full context, but the lesson type is clear: it shows the ikhtilaf within the school on how to apply a non-Hanafi view for those who follow it.

Key Terms
تخريج (takhrij): Derivation or interpretation of a general statement into a specific calculation.
انفراد (infirad): Being alone; the scenario where only one heir exists.
خنثى (khuntha): A person with ambiguous genitalia; in inheritance, they are treated as the lesser category.

The Hermaphrodite's Inheritance: The Lesser of Two Shares (Aqall al-Nasibayn)
Explaining the Hanafi rule for hermaphrodite inheritance and rebutting al-Sha'bi's view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for a hermaphrodite's inheritance (aqall al-nasibayn), explain its basis in yaqin (certainty), and compare it with al-Sha'bi's half-and-half method.

Core Idea
The hermaphrodite gets the lesser of the two possible shares — certainty over doubt.

The inheritance of a person with ambiguous sex (khuntha mushkil) requires careful legal reasoning. The Hanafi school applies the principle of certainty (yaqin): only the minimum share that is definitely due is given. This lesson covers the rule 'aqall al-nasibayn' (the lesser of the two shares) and the proofs behind it, contrasting with the view of al-Sha'bi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states: 'wa lahu aqall al-nasibayn' meaning the khuntha gets the lesser of the two possible shares (male vs female).
This is the core Hanafi rule.
2
Work through the examples
The passage gives several scenarios (e.g., with a brother, with husband/mother/sister) to illustrate how the ruling applies in practice.
Pay attention to how the lesser share is determined in each case.
3
Understand the opposing view
Al-Sha'bi and Ibn Abbas hold that the khuntha gets half of the male share and half of the female share (half-and-half).
This is based on ignorance of the true sex.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi argument is that ownership is being established initially (ibtida'); it cannot be established with doubt. They distinguish from ambiguous manumission/divorce where entitlement is already certain.
The principle of yaqin is central.
5
Evaluate the practical difference
Under the Hanafi view, the khuntha gets the minimum; under al-Sha'bi, he gets an average. This can significantly affect shares.
E.g., with a brother, Hanafi gives 1/3, al-Sha'bi gives 3/7 (0.33 vs 0.43).

Source Text

الله : (وله أقل النصيبين) يعني لو مات أبوه كان له الأقل من نصيب الذكر الأنثى فإنه ينظر نصيبه على أنه ذكر وعلى أنه أنثى فيعطى الأقل منهما، وإن كان محروماً على أحد التقديرين فلا شيء له؛ مثاله أخوان لأب وأم أحدهما خنثى مشكل كان المال بينهما أثلاثاً للأخ الثلثان وللخنثى الثلث فيقدر أنثى لأنه أقل، ولو قدر ذكراً كان له النصف. ولو تركت امرأة زوجاً وأماً وأختاً لأب وأم . خنثى كان للزوج النصف وللأم الثلث من النصف الباقي وللخنثى ما بقي وهو السدس على أنه غصبة، ولو قدر أنثى كان له النصف وكانت المسألة تعول إلى ثمانية. ولو تركت زوجاً وأماً وأخوين من أم وأخاً لأب وأم هو خنثى كان للزوج النصف وللأم السدس وللأخوين لأم الثلث ولا شيء للخنثى لأنه عصبة ولم يفضل له شيء، ولو قدر أنثى كان له النصف فعالت المسألة إلى تسعة. ولو ترك الرجل ولد أخ هو الخنثى وعماً لأب وأم أو لأب كان المال للعم وقدر الخنثى أنثى لأن بنت الأخ لا ترث، ولو قدر ذكراً كان المال له دون العم لأن ابن الأخ مقدم على العم. وقال الشعبي : للخنثى نصف ميراث ذكر ونصف ميراث أنثى. وعن ابن عباس مثله لأنه مجهول والتوزيع على أحوال عند الجهل طريق معهودة في الشرع كما في العتق المبهم، والطلاق المبهم إذا تعذر البيان فيه بموت الموقع قبل البيان. ولنا أن الحاجة إلى إثبات الملك ابتداء فلا يثبت مع الشك فصار كما إذا كان الشك في وجوب المال بسبب آخر غير الميراث بخلاف المستشهد به الاستحقاق متيقن به وهو الإنشاء السابق ومحلية كل واحد من العبدين والمعتقين سبب بحكم ذلك السبب ثابت لكل واحد منهما على السواء من غير ترجيح أحدهما على الآخر بالشك. قال رحمه الله : فلو مات أبوه وترك ابناً له سهمان وللخثنى سهم) لأنه الأقل وهو متيقن فيستحقه، وعلى قول الشعبي نصف ميراث ذكر ونصف ميراث أنثى . واختلف أبو يوسف ومحمد في تخريج قول الشعبي فقال أبو يوسف : المال بينهما على سبعة أسهم أربعة للذكر وثلاثة للخنثى ؛ اعتبر نصيب كل واحد منهما حالة انفراده فإن الذكر لو كان وحده

كان كل المال له والخنثى إن كان ذكراً كان له كل المال، وإذا كان أنثى كان له نصف المال فيأخذ نصف النصيبين نصف الكل ونصف النصف وذلك ثلاثة أرباع المال وللابن كل المال فيجعل كل ربح سهماً فبلغ سبعة أسهم للابن أربعة وللخنثى ثلاثة أرباع، وليس للمال ثلاثة أرباع وأربعة أرباع فيضرب كل واحد منهم بجميع حقه اعتباراً بطريق العول والمضاربة. وقال محمد رحمه الله : المال بينهما على اثني عشر سهماً سبعة للابن أيضاً وخمسة للخنثى ويعتبر هو نصيب كل واحد منهما في حالة الاجتماع فيقول : لو كان الخنثى ذكراً كان المال بينهما نصفين، ولو كان أنثى كان أثلاثاً فالقسمة على تقدير ذكورته من اثنين، وعلى تقدير أنوثته من ثلاثة وليس بينهما موافقة فيضرب إحداهما في الأخرى تبلغ ستة للخنثى على تقدير أنه أنثى سهمان، وعلى تقدير أنه ذكر ثلاثة فله نصف النصيبين وليس للثلاثة نصف صحيح فيضرب الستة في اثنين تبلع اثني عشر فيكون للخنثى ستة على تقدير أنه ذكر، وله أربعة على تقدير أنه أنثى فيأخذ نصف النصيبين خمسة لأن نصف الستة ثلاثة ونصف الأربعة اثنان ألا ترى أن الابن يأخذ في هذه المسألة سبعة لأن نصيب الابن على تقدير أن الخنثى ذكر ستة، وعلى أنه أنثى ثمانية فنصف النصيبين سبعة، ولو كان معها بنت فعند أبي يوسف تكون من تسعة لأن نصيب البنت النصف حالة انفرادها وللابن الكل وللخنثى ثلاثة أرباع حال انفراد كل منهما فيجعل كل ربع سهماً تبلغ تسعة وعند محمد له خمس وثمن لأن على تقدير أنه ذكر كان له خمسان فله نصف وهو الخمس، وعلى تقدير أنه أنثى كل له ربع نصفه وهو الثمن فمخرج الخمس من خمسة ومخرج الثمن من ثمانية وليس بينهما موافقة فتضرب إحداهما في الأخرى تبلغ أربعين ومنها تصح المسألة للخنثى خمسها ثمانية وثمنها له ثلاثة عشر سهماً والبنت على تقدير أنه ذكر خمسان وهو ستة عشر، وعلى تقدير أنه أنثى ربع وهو عشرة فيكون له نصف النصيبين ثلاثة عشر والابن خمسان على تقدير ذكورته، ونصف على تقدير أنوثته فله نصف النصيبين ثمانية عشر وعلى هذا تخرج المسائل ولو كانوا أكثر من ذلك على المذهبين والله أعلم.
Chapter on the Hermaphrodite. ... And he said: (He has the lesser of the two shares) meaning if his father dies, he gets the lesser of the share of a male or female: then his share is considered as if he were a male and as if he were a female, and he is given the lesser of the two. If he would be excluded on one estimation, he gets nothing. Example: two brothers from father and mother, one of them an ambiguous hermaphrodite: the estate is divided into thirds, the brother gets two-thirds and the hermaphrodite gets one-third, estimating him as female because it is less; if estimated as male he would get half. And if a woman leaves a husband, a mother, and a full sister who is a hermaphrodite: the husband gets half, the mother gets one-third of the remaining half, and the hermaphrodite gets what remains, which is one-sixth as a residuary; if estimated as female, she gets half and the case becomes eight. And if a woman leaves a husband, a mother, two uterine brothers, and a full brother who is a hermaphrodite: the husband gets half, the mother gets one-sixth, the two uterine brothers get one-third, and the hermaphrodite gets nothing because he is a residuary and nothing remains; if estimated as female, she gets half and the case becomes nine. And if a man leaves a son of a brother who is the hermaphrodite and a paternal uncle: the estate goes to the uncle, and the hermaphrodite is estimated as female because the daughter of a brother does not inherit; if estimated as male, the estate would go to him because the son of a brother precedes the uncle. Al-Sha'bi said: The hermaphrodite gets half of a male's inheritance and half of a female's inheritance. And from Ibn Abbas similar, because he is unknown, and distribution according to states in case of ignorance is a familiar way in the law, as in ambiguous manumission and ambiguous divorce if clarification becomes impossible due to the death of the one who made the ambiguous statement before clarification. Our argument: the need to establish ownership initially, so it cannot be established with doubt, as if there is doubt in the obligation of wealth due to some other cause besides inheritance, unlike the analogy given where entitlement is certain due to a prior act and the ambiguity is in the specific entity, so each of the two slaves or the two manumitted persons is a cause equally without preferring one over the other due to doubt. He said: So if his father dies and leaves a son, he gets two shares, and the hermaphrodite gets one share because it is the lesser and is certain, so he deserves it. According to al-Sha'bi, half of a male's inheritance and half of a female's inheritance. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differed in extracting al-Sha'bi's statement. Abu Yusuf said: The estate between them is into seven shares: four for the male and three for the hermaphrodite. He considered the share of each one of them in the case of isolation: the male if alone would have all the wealth, and the hermaphrodite if male would have all, if female would have half, so he takes half of the two shares: half of all and half of half, which is three-quarters of the estate. The son gets all the estate. Then each share is made a unit, thus reaching seven shares: for the son four, for the hermaphrodite three-quarters. But the estate does not actually have three-quarters and four-quarters, so each one is given his entire right by way of 'awl and mudaraba. Muhammad said: The estate between them is into twelve shares: seven for the son and five for the hermaphrodite. He considers the share of each one of them in the state of co-presence. He says: If the hermaphrodite were male, the estate would be between them half and half; if female, it would be into thirds. So division on estimate of masculinity from two, on estimate of femininity from three. There is no agreement between them, so multiply one by the other to reach six. For the hermaphrodite on estimate of being female: two shares; on estimate of being male: three. So he takes half of the two shares. For three, half is not an integer, so multiply six by two to reach twelve. Thus for the hermaphrodite: six on estimate of male, four on estimate of female. He takes half of the two shares, five, because half of six is three and half of four is two. Do you not see that the son takes seven because his share on estimate of hermaphrodite being male is six, and on estimate of female is eight, so half of the two shares is seven. And if there were a daughter with them, according to Abu Yusuf it would be from nine because the daughter's share in isolation is half, the son's is all, and the hermaphrodite's is three-quarters, so each quarter is made a unit, totaling nine. According to Muhammad, he gets one-fifth and one-eighth because on estimate of being male he gets two-fifths, so half is one-fifth; on estimate of being female he gets one-fourth, half of which is one-eighth. The denominator of one-fifth is five, of one-eighth is eight; no agreement, multiply one by the other to reach forty, and from it the case is corrected: for the hermaphrodite one-fifth is eight and one-eighth is five? Actually from context: for the hermaphrodite one-fifth of forty is eight and one-eighth is five, total thirteen? Wait text says: 'للخنثى خمسها ثمانية وثمنها له ثلاثة عشر سهماً' - that seems inconsistent: one-fifth of forty is eight, one-eighth of forty is five, total thirteen, but says 'وثمنها له ثلاثة عشر سهما' which likely means he gets eight (from one-fifth) and from one-eighth he gets five? Actually it says 'خمسها ثمانية وثمنها له ثلاثة عشر سهما' - perhaps 'وثمنها له' means his one-eighth share is five? No, it says 'ثلاثة عشر' which is 13. Possibly a scribal error. We'll reflect the text as is. The daughter on estimate of male gets two-fifths: sixteen; on estimate of female gets one quarter: ten. So half of the two shares is thirteen. The son gets two-fifths on estimate of masculinity, and half on estimate of femininity, so half of the two shares is eighteen. And upon this all cases are derived, even if more than that according to the two opinions. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the method of calculating the inheritance of a hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil) when applying the view of al-Sha'bi, who held that the khuntha takes half of the male's share and half of the female's share. The author first establishes the preferred Hanafi position: the khuntha takes the lesser of the two possible shares (aqall al-nasibayn). This is because certainty (yaqin) requires giving only what is definitely due, and doubt prevents giving more. Various examples illustrate: with a brother, the khuntha gets 1/3 (as female) rather than 1/2; with a husband, mother, and khuntha sister, the khuntha gets the residue as a male (1/6) rather than the half as female which would cause 'awl. Then al-Sha'bi's view is presented, and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ on how to implement it. Abu Yusuf's method considers each heir's share if they were alone (case of isolation) and then averages via 'awl. Muhammad's method considers the shares in the state of co-presence (social state) and averages the halves of the two estimates. The author includes examples with a son, and with a daughter, showing the resulting fractions. The accepted position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated, but the detailed analysis suggests Muhammad's method is more refined. The passage concludes that all cases follow these two methods.

Key Terms
خنثى مشكل (khuntha mushkil): A person with both male and female genitalia whose sex cannot be determined after maturation
أقل النصيبين (aqall al-nasibayn): The lesser of the two possible shares (male vs. female) that the khuntha is entitled to
عول ('awl): Proportional reduction of shares when the total of prescribed shares exceeds the estate

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the basic rule for a hermaphrodite's inheritance?
A) He gets half of a male's share and half of a female's share.
B) He gets the lesser of the two possible shares (male or female).
C) He is treated as a male unless proven otherwise.
D) He gets nothing until his sex is determined.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school gives the khuntha the lesser of the two shares (male/female) based on the principle of certainty (yaqin).

Implementing al-Sha'bi's View: The Dispute Between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the method of implementing al-Sha'bi's half-and-half rule.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two methods of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad for calculating the hermaphrodite's share under al-Sha'bi's rule and apply them to simple cases.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ on how to average the two estimates: isolation vs. co-presence.

While the Hanafi school rejects al-Sha'bi's half-and-half method, if one were to apply it, how exactly should it be calculated? Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, two pillars of the Hanafi school, proposed different mathematical methods. This lesson dissects their approaches.

Guided Path
1
State the context
Al-Sha'bi's rule: khuntha gets half of the male share and half of the female share. But when there are multiple heirs, how do we compute these halves?
The khuntha's share depends on the other heirs present.
2
Abu Yusuf's method
Abu Yusuf considers each heir's hypothetical share if they were alone (isolation), then uses 'awl to combine. For example, with a son and khuntha: son alone gets whole, khuntha if male gets whole, if female gets half. The three hypothetical shares (1, 1, 0.5) are made into shares of 7: son 4, khuntha 3.
This method is called 'isolation' (infirad).
3
Muhammad's method
Muhammad considers the shares in the actual state of co-presence (ijtima'). He first estimates the split if the khuntha were male, then if female. Then he averages half of each estimate. For the same example: if male, each gets 1/2; if female, son 2/3, khuntha 1/3. Half of 1/2=1/4, half of 1/3=1/6. Sum for khuntha = 1/4+1/6=5/12. The son gets 7/12.
This method averages the two hypothetical distributions.
4
Work through the example with a daughter
Another example with a daughter, son, and khuntha shows the same pattern: Abu Yusuf's method uses isolation (daughter alone 1/2, son 1, khuntha 3/4) leading to 9 shares; Muhammad's method uses co-presence estimates.
The fractions differ.
5
Understand the significance
Both methods are attempts to implement al-Sha'bi's rule, but the Hanafi school does not adopt either as mufta bihi because it rejects the rule itself. The dispute shows the nuanced reasoning within the school.
The practical difference is in the final shares, e.g., 3/7 vs 5/12 in the son-khuntha case.

كان كل المال له والخنثى إن كان ذكراً كان له كل المال، وإذا كان أنثى كان له نصف المال فيأخذ نصف النصيبين نصف الكل ونصف النصف وذلك ثلاثة أرباع المال وللابن كل المال فيجعل كل ربح سهماً فبلغ سبعة أسهم للابن أربعة وللخنثى ثلاثة أرباع، وليس للمال ثلاثة أرباع وأربعة أرباع فيضرب كل واحد منهم بجميع حقه اعتباراً بطريق العول والمضاربة. وقال محمد رحمه الله : المال بينهما على اثني عشر سهماً سبعة للابن أيضاً وخمسة للخنثى ويعتبر هو نصيب كل واحد منهما في حالة الاجتماع فيقول : لو كان الخنثى ذكراً كان المال بينهما نصفين، ولو كان أنثى كان أثلاثاً فالقسمة على تقدير ذكورته من اثنين، وعلى تقدير أنوثته من ثلاثة وليس بينهما موافقة فيضرب إحداهما في الأخرى تبلغ ستة للخنثى على تقدير أنه أنثى سهمان، وعلى تقدير أنه ذكر ثلاثة فله نصف النصيبين وليس للثلاثة نصف صحيح فيضرب الستة في اثنين تبلع اثني عشر فيكون للخنثى ستة على تقدير أنه ذكر، وله أربعة على تقدير أنه أنثى فيأخذ نصف النصيبين خمسة لأن نصف الستة ثلاثة ونصف الأربعة اثنان ألا ترى أن الابن يأخذ في هذه المسألة سبعة لأن نصيب الابن على تقدير أن الخنثى ذكر ستة، وعلى أنه أنثى ثمانية فنصف النصيبين سبعة، ولو كان معها بنت فعند أبي يوسف تكون من تسعة لأن نصيب البنت النصف حالة انفرادها وللابن الكل وللخنثى ثلاثة أرباع حال انفراد كل منهما فيجعل كل ربع سهماً تبلغ تسعة وعند محمد له خمس وثمن لأن على تقدير أنه ذكر كان له خمسان فله نصف وهو الخمس، وعلى تقدير أنه أنثى كل له ربع نصفه وهو الثمن فمخرج الخمس من خمسة ومخرج الثمن من ثمانية وليس بينهما موافقة فتضرب إحداهما في الأخرى تبلغ أربعين ومنها تصح المسألة للخنثى خمسها ثمانية وثمنها له ثلاثة عشر سهماً والبنت على تقدير أنه ذكر خمسان وهو ستة عشر، وعلى تقدير أنه أنثى ربع وهو عشرة فيكون له نصف النصيبين ثلاثة عشر والابن خمسان على تقدير ذكورته، ونصف على تقدير أنوثته فله نصف النصيبين ثمانية عشر وعلى هذا تخرج المسائل ولو كانوا أكثر من ذلك على المذهبين والله أعلم.
Chapter on the Hermaphrodite. ... And he said: (He has the lesser of the two shares) meaning if his father dies, he gets the lesser of the share of a male or female: then his share is considered as if he were a male and as if he were a female, and he is given the lesser of the two. If he would be excluded on one estimation, he gets nothing. Example: two brothers from father and mother, one of them an ambiguous hermaphrodite: the estate is divided into thirds, the brother gets two-thirds and the hermaphrodite gets one-third, estimating him as female because it is less; if estimated as male he would get half. And if a woman leaves a husband, a mother, and a full sister who is a hermaphrodite: the husband gets half, the mother gets one-third of the remaining half, and the hermaphrodite gets what remains, which is one-sixth as a residuary; if estimated as female, she gets half and the case becomes eight. And if a woman leaves a husband, a mother, two uterine brothers, and a full brother who is a hermaphrodite: the husband gets half, the mother gets one-sixth, the two uterine brothers get one-third, and the hermaphrodite gets nothing because he is a residuary and nothing remains; if estimated as female, she gets half and the case becomes nine. And if a man leaves a son of a brother who is the hermaphrodite and a paternal uncle: the estate goes to the uncle, and the hermaphrodite is estimated as female because the daughter of a brother does not inherit; if estimated as male, the estate would go to him because the son of a brother precedes the uncle. Al-Sha'bi said: The hermaphrodite gets half of a male's inheritance and half of a female's inheritance. And from Ibn Abbas similar, because he is unknown, and distribution according to states in case of ignorance is a familiar way in the law, as in ambiguous manumission and ambiguous divorce if clarification becomes impossible due to the death of the one who made the ambiguous statement before clarification. Our argument: the need to establish ownership initially, so it cannot be established with doubt, as if there is doubt in the obligation of wealth due to some other cause besides inheritance, unlike the analogy given where entitlement is certain due to a prior act and the ambiguity is in the specific entity, so each of the two slaves or the two manumitted persons is a cause equally without preferring one over the other due to doubt. He said: So if his father dies and leaves a son, he gets two shares, and the hermaphrodite gets one share because it is the lesser and is certain, so he deserves it. According to al-Sha'bi, half of a male's inheritance and half of a female's inheritance. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differed in extracting al-Sha'bi's statement. Abu Yusuf said: The estate between them is into seven shares: four for the male and three for the hermaphrodite. He considered the share of each one of them in the case of isolation: the male if alone would have all the wealth, and the hermaphrodite if male would have all, if female would have half, so he takes half of the two shares: half of all and half of half, which is three-quarters of the estate. The son gets all the estate. Then each share is made a unit, thus reaching seven shares: for the son four, for the hermaphrodite three-quarters. But the estate does not actually have three-quarters and four-quarters, so each one is given his entire right by way of 'awl and mudaraba. Muhammad said: The estate between them is into twelve shares: seven for the son and five for the hermaphrodite. He considers the share of each one of them in the state of co-presence. He says: If the hermaphrodite were male, the estate would be between them half and half; if female, it would be into thirds. So division on estimate of masculinity from two, on estimate of femininity from three. There is no agreement between them, so multiply one by the other to reach six. For the hermaphrodite on estimate of being female: two shares; on estimate of being male: three. So he takes half of the two shares. For three, half is not an integer, so multiply six by two to reach twelve. Thus for the hermaphrodite: six on estimate of male, four on estimate of female. He takes half of the two shares, five, because half of six is three and half of four is two. Do you not see that the son takes seven because his share on estimate of hermaphrodite being male is six, and on estimate of female is eight, so half of the two shares is seven. And if there were a daughter with them, according to Abu Yusuf it would be from nine because the daughter's share in isolation is half, the son's is all, and the hermaphrodite's is three-quarters, so each quarter is made a unit, totaling nine. According to Muhammad, he gets one-fifth and one-eighth because on estimate of being male he gets two-fifths, so half is one-fifth; on estimate of being female he gets one-fourth, half of which is one-eighth. The denominator of one-fifth is five, of one-eighth is eight; no agreement, multiply one by the other to reach forty, and from it the case is corrected: for the hermaphrodite one-fifth is eight and one-eighth is five? Actually from context: for the hermaphrodite one-fifth of forty is eight and one-eighth is five, total thirteen? Wait text says: 'للخنثى خمسها ثمانية وثمنها له ثلاثة عشر سهماً' - that seems inconsistent: one-fifth of forty is eight, one-eighth of forty is five, total thirteen, but says 'وثمنها له ثلاثة عشر سهما' which likely means he gets eight (from one-fifth) and from one-eighth he gets five? Actually it says 'خمسها ثمانية وثمنها له ثلاثة عشر سهما' - perhaps 'وثمنها له' means his one-eighth share is five? No, it says 'ثلاثة عشر' which is 13. Possibly a scribal error. We'll reflect the text as is. The daughter on estimate of male gets two-fifths: sixteen; on estimate of female gets one quarter: ten. So half of the two shares is thirteen. The son gets two-fifths on estimate of masculinity, and half on estimate of femininity, so half of the two shares is eighteen. And upon this all cases are derived, even if more than that according to the two opinions. And Allah knows best.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the method of calculating the inheritance of a hermaphrodite (khuntha mushkil) when applying the view of al-Sha'bi, who held that the khuntha takes half of the male's share and half of the female's share. The author first establishes the preferred Hanafi position: the khuntha takes the lesser of the two possible shares (aqall al-nasibayn). Then al-Sha'bi's view is presented, and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ on how to implement it. Muhammad's method considers the shares in the state of co-presence (social state) and averages the halves of the two estimates. The author includes examples with a son, and with a daughter, showing the resulting fractions. The accepted position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly stated, but the detailed analysis suggests Muhammad's method is more refined. The passage concludes that all cases follow these two methods.

Inheritance of the Khuntha with a Son and Daughter
Calculating shares for khuntha with son, and with son and daughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares of a khuntha when present with a son and a daughter, applying the method of averaging the two possible gender assumptions and using the base numbers determined by Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
The khuntha takes the minimum of his possible male and female shares, using the 'half of two portions' method.

When an heir is a hermaphrodite (khuntha) whose sex is uncertain, the Hanafi school resolves the ambiguity by calculating what the khuntha would receive under both male and female assumptions, then giving him the minimum of the two. This lesson walks through the calculation for two scenarios: khuntha with a son alone, and khuntha with a son and daughter. We will examine the methods of Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, which differ in finding the common base for shares.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of half of two portions
For any khuntha, first determine the shares if the khuntha were male and if female. Then the khuntha takes the lower of the two possible shares (or half the sum if both have the same base). This is called taking 'half of the two portions'.
2
Calculate the case of khuntha with a son alone
Assume khuntha is male: male khuntha and son split equally (1/2 each). Assume khuntha is female: son inherits all (since a female khuntha would not be a son's heir? The guided steps can simply present the two methods.
The calculation is the same for the case with only son: under male assumption, shares are half-half; under female, son gets 2/3, khuntha gets 1/3. Hence the half-of-two-portions gives 5/12 for khuntha (Muhammad) or 3/7 (Abu Yusuf).
3
Add a daughter to the scenario
With a daughter present, the shares change. Under male khuntha: two sons? Actually the khuntha as male is a son, so there are two sons and one daughter -> shares: each son gets 2/5? Not exactly. The text says for Muhammad: 'on the assumption that it is male, he had two-fifths' means khuntha as male gets 2/5? Actually from the calculation: Muhammad's base 40, female khuntha gets 1/4? Let's derive: If khuntha male (so a son), then there are two sons and one daughter. The estate is divided into 5 shares: each son gets 2, daughter gets 1 (male gets twice female). So khuntha (as son) gets 2/5? No, 2/5 = 8/20, but the text says the daughter under male assumption gets two-fifths? It says: 'the daughter, on the assumption that it is male, has two-fifths' Actually it says: 'the daughter, on the assumption that it is male, has two-fifths, which is sixteen' in base 40. Two-fifths of 40 is 16. So if khuntha male, daughter gets 2/5? But daughter normally gets half of son, so if two sons and one daughter, shares: son1:2, son2:2, daughter:1, total 5, so daughter gets 1/5, not 2/5. Something is off. Possibly the 'two-fifths' refers to something else. Let's trust the numbers given: in Muhammad's method for case with daughter, khuntha gets 13, daughter 13, son 18. So the method is: under male assumption, khuntha gets 2/5? That would be 16, half gives 8; under female, khuntha gets 1/4 = 10, half gives 5; average gives 6.5? Not 13. Actually I think the text's numbers are correct if we follow the derivation: khuntha under male assumption gets 2/5? But then half is 1/5 = 8/40; under female, khuntha gets 1/4 = 10/40; half of each gives 4/40 and 5/40? No, half of 2/5 is 1/5 = 8/40; half of 1/4 is 1/8 = 5/40; so khuntha would get 13/40? Actually 8+5? That would be sum, not half of sum. The principle is 'half of the two portions', not sum. It should be half of each possibility? The text says 'half of the two portions' meaning half of the sum? Usually it means the arithmetical mean of the two possible shares. So if male share = 2/5 = 16/40, female share = 1/4 = 10/40, mean = (16+10)/2 = 26/2 = 13/40. That matches khuntha gets 13. Daughter's share: under male assumption (khuntha male), daughter gets 1/5? But text says 2/5? Actually the text says: 'the daughter, on the assumption that it is male, has two-fifths, which is sixteen' so daughter gets 2/5 = 16/40? That would mean under male assumption, daughter gets 2/5, son gets? Not consistent. I think the text may have miswritten or the numbers are given in a specific way. Given the complexity, we will follow the actual numbers from the source: Abu Yusuf: base 9, shares? Not given for daughter+son+khuntha, only for son alone. For the case with daughter, only Muhammad's base 40 is given: khuntha 13, daughter 13, son 18. So we can present that as the method.
The guided step should simply explain that we determine shares under two gender assumptions and then average them, using the base number that accommodates both fractions.
4
Compare the methods of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
For the case of khuntha with son only, Abu Yusuf uses base 7, giving son 4 and khuntha 3. Muhammad uses base 12, giving son 7 and khuntha 5. For the case with a daughter added, Abu Yusuf uses base 9 (though the text does not give the individual shares, it says 'from nine') and Muhammad uses base 40 giving son 18, daughter 13, khuntha 13.
Both methods are valid within the Hanafi school; the difference is in how the base is derived.
5
Apply the principle to any set of heirs
The method generalizes: for any situation with a khuntha, calculate the shares under male and female assumptions, then assign the khuntha the arithmetic mean of the two possible shares (or the minimum to avoid exceeding the estate). The other heirs receive the mean of their two possible shares as well.
The text ends with 'On this all cases are derived, and Allah knows best.'

All the wealth belonged to him [the son?]. And if the khuntha was male, all the wealth belonged to him; and if female, half the wealth belonged to him. So he takes half of the two portions: half of the whole and half of half, which is three-quarters of the wealth. And to the son belongs all the wealth. So each profit is made a share, so it reached seven shares: for the son four, and for the khuntha three-quarters. And the wealth does not have three-quarters and four-quarters, so each one of them multiplies by all his right considering the method of 'awl and mudarabah. Muhammad said: the wealth between them on twelve shares: seven for the son also, and five for the khuntha. And he considers the share of each one in the state of meeting. He says: if the khuntha were male, the wealth would be half and half between them; if female, it would be thirds. So the division on the assumption of his masculinity is from two, and on the assumption of his femininity from three. There is no common factor between them, so multiply one by the other, it reaches six. For the khuntha, on the assumption that it is female, two shares; on the assumption that it is male, three. So he takes half of the two portions, and three does not have a half integer, so multiply the six by two, it becomes twelve. So the khuntha has six on the assumption that it is male, and four on the assumption that it is female. He takes half of the two portions, which is five, because half of six is three and half of four is two. Do you not see that the son takes in this case seven? Because the son's share on the assumption that the khuntha is male is six, and on the assumption that it is female is eight, so half of the two portions is seven. And if there was a daughter with her, then according to Abu Yusuf it would be from nine, because the daughter's share is half when she is alone, the son gets all, and the khuntha gets three-quarters when each is alone. So make each quarter a share, it reaches nine. According to Muhammad, he has one-fifth and one-eighth, because on the assumption that it is male, he had two-fifths, so his half is one-fifth; on the assumption that it is female, he had one-quarter, half of it is one-eighth. The denominator of one-fifth is five, and of one-eighth is eight, no common factor, so multiply one by the other, it reaches forty. From it the case is solved: for the khuntha one-fifth of it is eight, and one-eighth of it is thirteen shares. The daughter, on the assumption that it is male, has two-fifths, which is sixteen; on the assumption that it is female, one-quarter, which is ten, so her half of the two portions is thirteen. The son, on the assumption of his masculinity, has two-fifths, and on the assumption of his femininity, half, so his half of the two portions is eighteen. And on this all cases are derived, even if there are more than that, according to the two schools. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage presents faraid calculations for an hermaphrodite (khuntha) whose sex is unknown. The ruling: the khuntha takes the minimum of what it would receive as male or female. The text first considers a case with only the khuntha and a son. According to Abu Yusuf, the base is 7 shares: son gets 4, khuntha gets 3. Imam Muhammad disagrees and uses a base of 12, giving the son 7 and the khuntha 5. The method: assume khuntha is male (half and half = 6 shares each) or female (son two-thirds, khuntha one-third = 8 for son, 4 for khuntha); average the two possibilities: khuntha (6+4)/2=5, son (6+8)/2=7. Then the text adds a daughter. For this scenario, Abu Yusuf uses base 9: daughter gets 4.5? Actually, the text says 'from nine' and the son gets? More precisely, Abu Yusuf makes each quarter a share, yielding 9 shares total. Muhammad uses a base of 40: khuntha gets 13, daughter 13, son 18. The principle: the khuntha always takes the lower of the two possible shares to avoid depriving qualified heirs.

Key Terms
خنثى (khuntha): An hermaphrodite whose sex is uncertain
نصيبين (nasibayn): Two portions corresponding to the two possible genders
عول (awl): Proportional reduction of shares when sum exceeds base
مضاربة (mudarabah): Literal meaning 'profit-sharing'; used here symbolically to describe the multiplication method

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what is the base number for the case of a khuntha with a son and a daughter?
A) 9
B) 12
C) 40
D) 44

Key Takeaway
For a khuntha, shares are calculated by averaging the two possible gender scenarios; the method of Imam Muhammad using base 40 for the case with son and daughter is widely relied upon.
