Faraid — Inheritance
beginner
6 min
Defining Faraid and Its Causes
Defining the science and its causes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic meaning of 'fard', identify the three causes of inheritance in the Hanafi school, and explain why learning faraid is a communal obligation.

Core Idea
Inheritance is based on three causes: blood, marriage, and wala—all fixed by Allah and His Messenger.

This passage opens the Book of Inheritance. It does not yet teach you how to calculate shares, but it lays the foundation: what inheritance is, why it matters, and who qualifies. The author stresses that this knowledge is so essential that the Prophet warned it would be among the first to be taken from his community.

Guided Path
1
Define 'fard' linguistically
Look at the Arabic text: the author gives two meanings—estimation (تقدير) and cutting (قطع). Find the Quranic verse and the mouse example that illustrate each.
These are not legal definitions yet; they set up why the shares are called 'farā’iḍ'.
2
Identify the ruling on learning faraid
From the hadith, note the Prophet's command 'Learn inheritance'. In Hanafi usul, the imperative form (amr) suggests obligation, but context of communal need makes it fard kifayah.
Also note that the hadith warns of the loss of this knowledge.
3
List the three causes of inheritance
Three are mentioned: blood relation (qarābah rahm), marriage (zawjiyyah), and patronage through emancipation (walā’ al-‘itq). Trace each cause back to its evidence—Quran for the first two, hadith for wala.
Marriage is called 'aṣl al-qarābah' because it generates blood relations.
4
Understand the rationale for each cause
The text provides reasoning: the deceased's wealth should not go to waste, and the nearest relative deserves it as a continuation of the support they received during life. Wala is a fictitious kinship from emancipation.
This is a teleological argument (maqāṣid) for the law.
5
Memorize the key terms and their definitions
Focus on 'al-farā’iḍ', 'al-qarābah', 'al-walā’'. Use the key_terms section to solidify them. This is foundation for the entire book.
You will encounter these terms repeatedly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الفرائض اعلم أن علم الفرائض هو علم المواريث يحتاج إليه لكثرة ما تعم به البلوى ويكون فيه من النوازل والفتوى ولهذا حث الشارع على تعلمه ورغب فيه مخافة اندراسه فقال «تعلموا الفرائض وعلموها للناس فإني أمرؤ مقيوض وسيقبض هذا العلم بقبض العلماء وتظهر الفتن حتى يتنازع الاثنان في الفريضة فلا يجدان أحداً يفصل بينهما » (۱) وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام تعلموا الفرائض وعلموها الناس فإنه أول ما ينزع من أمتي (۲) ثم يحتاج إلى معرفة تفسير الفرائض وسبب استحقاق الميراث وسبب حرمانه والحقوق المتعلقة بالتركة وأصناف الوارثين . أما تفسيرها فالفرض في اللغة عبارة عن التقديرة قال الله تعالى فنصف ما فرضتم [البقرة : ٢٣٧] أي قدرتم ويقال فرض القاضي النفقة إذا قدرها ، وكذا يستعمل للقطع يقال قرضت الفأرة الثوب أي قطعته فسمي كتاب الفرائض لأن سهام المواريث كلها مقدرة مقطوعة، ولأن سبب استحقاق الإرث القرابة وما هو ملحق بها كالولاء. أما القرابة فنوعان : رحم وزوجية، ونص الكتاب ناطق بهما وهو قوله تعالى يوصيكم الله في أولادكم [النساء : ۱۱] الآية. ولأن الميت لما استغنى عن ماله ولم يستحقه أحد يبقى عاطلاً سائباً والقريب أولى الناس به فيستحقه بالقرابة صلة كما يستحق النفقة حال حياة مورثه صلة. والزوجية أصل القرابة وأساسها لأن القرابات تفرعت وتشعبت منها فالتحق قرابة السبب بقرابة النسب في حق استحقاق الإرث وأما الولاء فلقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «الولاء لحمة كلحمة النسب يعني في حق استحقاق الميراث فقد التحق الولاء بالنسب، ولأنه بالإعتاق تسببب إلى احيائه حكماً حين أزال عنه المالكية والولاية التي هي من خاصة
Book of Inheritance. Know that the science of inheritance is the knowledge of inheritance portions. It is needed due to the frequency of common affliction, and it contains many legal issues and verdicts. Therefore, the Lawgiver urged its learning and desired it for fear that it would become extinct. He said: 'Learn inheritance and teach it to the people, for I am a mortal and this knowledge will be taken away by the taking away of scholars, and tribulations will appear until two people dispute about an inheritance and cannot find anyone to decide between them.' And he, peace be upon him, said: 'Learn inheritance and teach it to the people, for it is the first thing that will be taken away from my nation.' Then one needs to know the interpretation of faraid, the causes of entitlement to inheritance, the causes of deprivation, the rights relating to the estate, and the categories of heirs. As for its interpretation: fard in language means estimation. Allah the Exalted said: 'So half of what you have fixed' [al-Baqara:237], meaning estimated. And it is said: the judge fixed the maintenance when he estimated it. Similarly it is used for cutting: it is said: the mouse cut the garment, i.e., tore it. So the book of faraid is named because the shares of inheritance are all estimated and cut. And because the cause of entitlement to inheritance is kinship and what is attached to it like wala. As for kinship, it is of two types: blood relation and marital relation, and the text of the Book speaks of both, namely His saying: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children' [an-Nisa:11] etc. And because the deceased no longer needs his wealth and no one deserves it to be left idle and wasted, the relative is the most entitled person, so he deserves it by kinship as a connection, just as he deserved maintenance during the life of his predecessor as a connection. And marriage is the origin and foundation of kinship because kinship branched out and spread from it, so the kinship of cause (marriage) is annexed to the kinship of blood in the right of inheritance. And as for wala, because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Wala is a kinship like the kinship of lineage,' meaning in the right of inheritance, so wala is annexed to lineage. And because through emancipation, he was a cause for his (the slave's) life in a legal sense when he removed from him ownership and guardianship, which are from the particular...
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This is the opening of the Book of Faraid. The author begins by stressing the importance of learning inheritance, citing hadith that it will be taken away. He then defines the term fard (farida) linguistically as estimation or cutting, and explains that the shares are fixed amounts. He then lists the causes of inheritance: kinship (blood and marriage) and wala (patronage). He supports each with Quran and Sunnah. He explains that relatives deserve the wealth as a connection, similar to maintenance during life. Marriage is presented as the origin of kinship, and wala is annexed to lineage via the hadith. The passage sets the foundation for the detailed rules to come.

Key Terms
الفرائض (al-farā'iḍ): The shares of inheritance fixed by Allah; the science of inheritance.
القرابة (al-qarābah): Kinship, which is a cause of inheritance; two types: blood (rahm) and marriage (zawjiyyah).
الولاء (al-walā'): Patronage resulting from emancipation (walā' al-‘itq), a secondary cause of inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the linguistic meaning of 'fard' (فرض)?
A) Obligation
B) Estimation and cutting
C) Giving
D) Division

Key Takeaway
Inheritance is based on three causes: blood, marriage, and emancipation patronage; learning this science is a communal obligation.

Faraid — Inheritance
beginner
8 min
The Science of Inheritance: Importance, Causes, and Impediments
Foundational definitions and causes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic meaning of 'fard', identify the two causes of inheritance (kinship and wala'), and list the three impediments with their Qur'anic and Hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Inheritance is based on kinship and wala'; it is blocked by slavery, disbelief, and unjust killing.

This lesson opens the Hanafi study of inheritance (fara'id) by establishing its supreme importance in the Shari'ah. The Prophet ﷺ urged learning and teaching it, warning that its loss would bring confusion. We begin with the linguistic root of 'fard', then explore the causes that entitle a person to inherit and the impediments that strip that entitlement.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the urgency of learning fara'id
Read the two hadiths cited by the author. Note that the Prophet ﷺ feared the extinction of this knowledge and linked it to the appearance of trials.
The hadiths underscore that inheritance knowledge is fard kifayah (communal obligation).
2
Define 'fard' linguistically and technically
Understand that 'fard' means 'estimation' (from Q. 2:237) and 'cutting'. The Book of Fara'id is so named because shares are precisely estimated and cut off for heirs.
This dual meaning reinforces the exact nature of inheritance shares.
3
Identify the two causes of inheritance
The passage gives two causes: kinship (qarabah) – both blood (rahm) and marriage (zawjiyyah) – and wala' (patronage). The Qur'anic proof (4:11) is cited for kinship, and a hadith for wala'.
Marriage is the origin of kinship because it produces offspring. Wala' is attached to lineage by the Prophet's saying: 'al-wala' luhmah ka-luhmah al-nasab'.
4
List the three impediments to inheritance
The text states three impediments: slavery (negates capacity to own), disbelief (different religions), and killing (unjust direct killing). For each, a brief proof is provided.
Disbelief and killing are major topics with detailed rules; the killing impediment will be elaborated in its own chapter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الفرائض
اعلم أن علم الفرائض هو علم المواريث يحتاج إليه لكثرة ما تعم به البلوى ويكون فيه من النوازل والفتوى ولهذا حث الشارع على تعلمه ورغب فيه مخافة اندراسه فقال «تعلموا الفرائض وعلموها للناس فإني أمرؤ مقبوض وسيقبض هذا العلم بقبض العلماء وتظهر الفتن حتى يتنازع الاثنان في الفريضة فلا يجدان أحداً يفصل بينهما» وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام تعلموا الفرائض وعلموها الناس فإنه أول ما ينزع من أمتي ثم يحتاج إلى معرفة تفسير الفرائض وسبب استحقاق الميراث وسبب حرمانه والحقوق المتعلقة بالتركة وأصناف الوارثين . أما تفسيرها فالفرض في اللغة عبارة عن التقدير قال الله تعالى فنصف ما فرضتم [البقرة : ٢٣٧] أي قدرتم ويقال فرض القاضي النفقة إذا قدرها ، وكذا يستعمل للقطع يقال قرضت الفأرة الثوب أي قطعته فسمي كتاب الفرائض لأن سهام المواريث كلها مقدرة مقطوعة، ولأن سبب استحقاق الإرث القرابة وما هو ملحق بها كالولاء. أما القرابة فنوعان : رحم وزوجية، ونص الكتاب ناطق بهما وهو قوله تعالى يوصيكم الله في أولادكم [النساء : ۱۱] الآية. ولأن الميت لما استغنى عن ماله ولم يستحقه أحد يبقى عاطلاً سائباً والقريب أولى الناس به فيستحقه بالقرابة صلة كما يستحق النفقة حال حياة مورثه صلة. والزوجية أصل القرابة وأساسها لأن القرابات تفرعت وتشعبت منها فالتحق قرابة السبب بقرابة النسب في حق استحقاق الإرث وأما الولاء فلقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «الولاء لحمة كلحمة النسب يعني في حق استحقاق الميراث فقد التحق الولاء بالنسب، ولأنه بالإعتاق تسبب إلى إحيائه حكماً حين أزال عنه المالكية والولاية التي هي خاصة الإنسانية وكان السبب إلى الإحياء يعني بالاعتاق وكذا ولاء الموالاة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لمن سأله عمن أسلم على يد رجل هو أحق الناس به محياه أو مماته. وأما ما يحرم به الميراث فأنواع ثلاثة : الرق والكفر والقتل مباشرة بغير حق. أما الرق فلأنه سلب أهلية الملك، وأما الكفر فلقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لا يتوارث أهل ملتين لا كافر مسلماً ولا مسلم كافراً وأما القتل فلما يأتي في بابه وأما الحقوق المتعلقة بالتركة فأربعة : الكفن والدفن والوصية والدين والميراث فأول ما يبدأ منها بكفن الميت ودفنه لأن ستر عورته ومواراة سواته من أهم حوائجه، واستغرق الدين بماله لم يمنعه من ذلك حال حياته فكذلك بعد وفاته ثم تقضى ديونه لأنها أهم من قضاء ديون الله لاستغناء الله تعالى، وافتقار العبد لدي خصومة الله تعالى في حقوق العباد ولكثرة تجاوز الله تعالى وعفوه وتفضله وكرمه، ثم تنفذ وصيته من الثلث لأنها من حوائج الميت. والوارث إنما يستحق الميراث إذا استغنى المورث . وهذا إذا كانت الوصية بشيء بعينه، فإن كانت الوصية بثلث ماله أو ربعه فالموصى له شريك الورثة لأنها بمعنى الميراث لأنه ثبت حقه في جميع التركة شائعاً كحق سائر الورثة. ثم يقسم الباقي بين ورثته على فرائض الله تعالى وسنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. وأما أصناف الوارثين فثلاثة أصحاب الفرائض الذين لهم سهام مقدرة وعصبة وهم الذين يأخذون ما فضل من أصحاب الفروض وذوو الأرحام وهم الذين ليس لهم فروض مقدرة ولا لهم حقيقة تعصيب وإنما لهم مجرد قرابة. ولم يتعرض المؤلف لبيان ما يجري فيه الإرث وما لا يجري فيه الإرث فنقول : لا شك أن أعيان الأموال يجري فيها الإرث، وأما الحقوق فمنها ما يجري فيه الإرث حق الشفعة وخيار الشرط وحد القذف عندنا والنكاح لا يورث بلا خلاف وحبس المبيع وحبس الرهن يورث والوكالات والعواري والودائع لا تورث واختلف المشايخ في خيار العيب فمنهم من قال يورث، ومنهم من قال لا يورث ولكن لا يثبت للورثة ابتداء، والدية تورث بلا خلاف، وأما القصاص في الأصل أنه يورث ويثبت للورثة ابتداء ويجوز أن يقال القصاص لا يورث عند أبي حنيفة، ويورث عندهما والولاء لا يورث بلا خلاف وأما بيان الوقت الذي يجري فيه الإرث فنقول : هذا فصل اختلف المشايخ فيه ؛ قال مشايخ العراق : الإرث يثبت في آخر جزء من أجزاء حياة المورث. وقال مشايخ بلخ: الإرث يثبت بعد موت المورث. وفائدة هذا الاختلاف إنما تظهر في رجل تزوج بأمة الغير ثم قال لها إذا مات مولاك فأنت حرة فمات المولى والزوج وارثه هل تعتق؟ فعلى قول من يقول بأن الأرث يجري في آخر جزء
Book of Fara'id. Know that the science of fara'id is the science of inheritances; it is needed due to the prevalence of need for it and it contains many incidents and fatwas. Therefore, the Lawgiver encouraged learning it and desired it for fear of its extinction, saying: 'Learn the fara'id and teach them to the people, for I am a mortal and this knowledge will be taken away with the passing of the scholars, and trials will appear until two people will dispute over an inheritance and find no one to decide between them.' And he (peace be upon him) said: 'Learn the fara'id and teach them to the people, for it is the first thing that will be withdrawn from my community.' Then there is need to know the interpretation of fara'id, the cause of entitlement to inheritance, the cause of deprivation, the rights connected to the estate, and the categories of heirs. As for its interpretation, fard in language means estimation. Allah said: 'half of what you have fixed [al-Baqarah 2:237]' i.e., determined. And it is said: 'the judge fixed the maintenance' when he determined it. Similarly, it is used for cutting; it is said: 'the mouse cut the garment' i.e., it cut it. So the book of fara'id is so named because the shares of inheritances are all determined and cut. And because the cause of entitlement to inheritance is kinship and what is joined to it like wala'. As for kinship, there are two types: blood relationship and marital relationship, and the text of the Book (Qur'an) speaks of them: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children [al-Nisa' 4:11]' So named because the shares of inheritances are all determined and cut. And because the cause of entitlement to inheritance is kinship and what is joined to it like wala'. As for kinship, there are two types: blood relationship and marital relationship, and the text of the Book (Qur'an) speaks of them: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children [al-Nisa' 4:11]' So named... And because the deceased, when he becomes free from need of his wealth and no one deserves it, it would remain idle and unclaimed, and the relative is the most entitled to him, so he deserves it through kinship as a connection, just as he deserves maintenance during the life of his inheritor as a connection. And marital relationship is the origin and basis of kinship because kinships have branched and spread from it, so the kinship of cause (marriage) is joined to kinship of lineage in terms of entitlement to inheritance. As for wala', because he (peace be upon him) said: 'Wala' is a bond like the bond of lineage', meaning in terms of entitlement to inheritance, so wala' is joined to lineage. And also because by emancipation one becomes the cause of giving him life legally by removing ownership and authority which are specific to humanity, and it is the cause to life i.e., by emancipation. Similarly, wala' of alliance (mawalat) due to his (peace be upon him) statement to the one who asked him about the one who accepted Islam at the hands of a man: 'He is the most entitled of people to him in his life and death.' As for what prevents inheritance, there are three types: slavery, disbelief, and killing directly without right. As for slavery, because it negates the capacity for ownership. As for disbelief, because of his (peace be upon him) statement: 'People of two different religions do not inherit from each other'; a disbeliever does not inherit from a Muslim nor a Muslim from a disbeliever. As for killing, it will come in its chapter. As for the rights attached to the estate, there are four: the shroud and burial, the legacy (wasiyyah), debt, and inheritance. The first of these that is begun with is the shroud and burial of the deceased because covering his ‘awrah and veiling his nudity is among his most important needs; and if his wealth is consumed by debt, it does not prevent that during his life, so likewise after his death. Then his debts are paid because they are more important than paying the debts of Allah (swt), due to Allah's self-sufficiency and the slave's need for the dispute of Allah (swt) concerning the rights of the servants, and due to the abundance of Allah's indulgence, pardon, favor and generosity. Then his will (wasiyyah) is executed from one-third because it is among the needs of the deceased. And the heir only deserves inheritance when the deceased is free from need. This is when the will is for a specific thing; if the will is for one-third or one-quarter of his wealth, then the legatee is a partner with the heirs because it is in the nature of inheritance, since his right is established in the entire estate as a shared portion like the rights of the other heirs. Then the remainder is divided among his heirs according to the fara'id of Allah and the Sunnah of His Messenger (peace be upon him). As for the categories of heirs, they are three: the people of prescribed shares (ashab al-fara'id) who have fixed shares; the 'asabah (residuaries) who take what remains after the prescribed shares; and dhawu al-arham (uterine relatives) who have no fixed shares nor any true 'asabah, but merely kinship. The author did not address what is inherited and what is not inherited, so we say: there is no doubt that physical property (a'yan al-amwal) is inherited. As for rights, some of them are inherited: the right of pre-emption (shuf‘ah), the right of option (khiyar al-shart), and the hadd of qadhf (false accusation of adultery) in our school; marriage is not inherited without dispute; the right to detain the sold item and the right to detain the pawn (rahn) are inherited; agencies (wakalat), loans (‘ariyah), and deposits (wadi‘ah) are not inherited; the mashayikh (scholars) differed regarding the option of defect (khiyar al-‘ayb): some said it is inherited, others said it is not, but it is not established for the heirs initially; blood money (diyah) is inherited without dispute; as for qisas (retaliation), in principle it is inherited and established for the heirs initially, and it may be said that qisas is not inherited according to Abu Hanifah, but it is inherited according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad); wala' is not inherited without dispute. As for clarifying the time at which inheritance operates, we say: this is a chapter in which the scholars differed; the scholars of Iraq said: inheritance is established in the last part of the parts of the life of the deceased. The scholars of Balkh said: inheritance is established after the death of the deceased. The benefit of this difference appears in the case of a man who marries a slave woman belonging to someone else and then says to her: 'When your master dies, you are free'; then the master dies and the slave woman's husband is his heir; will she become free? According to the view that inheritance runs in the last part...
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the Book of Fara'id (Inheritance) from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a Hanafi commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author begins by emphasizing the importance of learning the science of inheritance, citing two prophetic hadiths that urge its study and warn of its loss. He then explains the linguistic meaning of 'fard' (الفرض) as 'estimation' or 'cutting', and notes that the book is so named because all inheritance shares are precisely determined and 'cut off' for the heirs. 

The causes of entitlement to inheritance are then discussed: kinship (qarabah) – both blood relation (rahm) and marital relation (zawjiyyah) – and wala' (patronage) arising from emancipation or alliance. The Qur'anic verse (al-Nisa' 4:11) is cited as the primary proof for inheritance through kinship. The author explains that marriage is the root of all kinship ties because it produces offspring and thus creates further relationships. Wala' is attached to lineage via a hadith that calls it a 'bond like the bond of lineage'. 

Three impediments to inheritance are listed: slavery (salahiyyat al-milk, capacity for ownership), disbelief (difference of religion), and intentional unjust killing. The order of payment from the estate is then explained: first the shroud and burial expenses, then debts, then the will (from one-third), and finally distribution among heirs. 

The heirs are categorized into three groups: ashab al-fara'id (Qur'anic share heirs), 'asabah (residuaries who take the remainder), and dhawu al-arham (uterine relatives who inherit only in the absence of others). 

The passage then discusses what rights can be inherited: physical property is clearly inherited, but certain rights (like pre-emption, option of condition, hadd of qadhf, detention of sold item and pawn) are inherited, while others (marriage, agencies, loans, deposits) are not. Blood money is inherited by consensus. Qisas (retaliation) is subject to disagreement between Abu Hanifah and his two companions. 

Finally, a significant intra-Hanafi dispute is presented: whether inheritance is established in the last moment of the deceased's life (Iraqi school) or after death (Balkh school). The practical difference appears in a scenario involving a slave woman's conditional emancipation: if her master dies and her husband (who inherits from the master) dies simultaneously, the outcome depends on when the inheritance is deemed to have vested.

Key Terms
الفرائض (al-fara'id): The science of inheritance shares from the estate of the deceased.
القرابة (al-qarabah): Kinship, which includes both blood relationship (rahm) and marital relationship (zawjiyyah).
الولاء (al-wala'): Patronage, the bond created by emancipation (wala' al-'itaqah) or by alliance (wala' al-muwalat), which entitles the patron to inherit from the freed slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT an impediment to inheritance?
A) Slavery
B) Disbelief
C) Manslaughter (unintentional killing)
D) Direct killing without right

Key Takeaway
Inheritance is a precise science; its causes are kinship and wala', and its impediments are slavery, disbelief, and unjust direct killing.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
10 min
Estate Rights, Heir Categories, and the Vesting Dispute
Estate rights, heir classification, and a scholarly dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to order the four rights attached to the estate, distinguish the three categories of heirs, and explain the practical consequence of the intra-Hanafi dispute on when inheritance vests.

Core Idea
The estate is settled in a fixed order: shroud, debt, will, then inheritance; heirs are of three classes, and when inheritance vests matters in overlapping events.

This lesson completes the introductory framework of fara'id by detailing the priority of claims against the estate, the classification of heirs into prescribed share-holders, residuaries, and uterine relatives, and the rights that can be inherited. It concludes with an intra-Hanafi debate on the exact moment inheritance vests, with a concrete case showing its practical impact.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the order of rights on the estate
The text lists four rights: (1) shroud and burial, (2) debts, (3) will (from one-third), (4) inheritance. Understand the rationale for this order.
Burial is first because it is a human dignity need; debts precede will because of creditor rights.
2
Identify the three categories of heirs
The heirs are: ashab al-fara'id (Qur'anic share heirs with fixed fractions), 'asabah (residuary male agnates), and dhawu al-arham (uterine relatives who inherit only when no other heirs exist).
Dhawu al-arham are recognized in Hanafi school; other madhahib differ.
3
Distinguish inheritable and non-inheritable rights
The passage lists rights that are inherited (e.g., pre-emption, option of condition, hadd of qadhf) and those that are not (e.g., marriage, agency, deposits). Note the intra-Hanafi differences on khiyar al-'ayb and qisas.
Qisas is not inherited according to Abu Hanifah but is inherited according to the two companions.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on vesting time
Iraqi scholars say inheritance vests in the last part of the deceased's life; Balkh scholars say it vests after death. Apply this to the case of a husband marrying a slave woman and promising her freedom on her master's death.
The practical difference: if inheritance vests before freedom, the husband inherits first and then frees her; if after, she is free first.

Source Text

كتاب الفرائض
اعلم أن علم الفرائض هو علم المواريث يحتاج إليه لكثرة ما تعم به البلوى ويكون فيه من النوازل والفتوى ولهذا حث الشارع على تعلمه ورغب فيه مخافة اندراسه فقال «تعلموا الفرائض وعلموها للناس فإني أمرؤ مقبوض وسيقبض هذا العلم بقبض العلماء وتظهر الفتن حتى يتنازع الاثنان في الفريضة فلا يجدان أحداً يفصل بينهما» وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام تعلموا الفرائض وعلموها الناس فإنه أول ما ينزع من أمتي ثم يحتاج إلى معرفة تفسير الفرائض وسبب استحقاق الميراث وسبب حرمانه والحقوق المتعلقة بالتركة وأصناف الوارثين . أما تفسيرها فالفرض في اللغة عبارة عن التقدير قال الله تعالى فنصف ما فرضتم [البقرة : ٢٣٧] أي قدرتم ويقال فرض القاضي النفقة إذا قدرها ، وكذا يستعمل للقطع يقال قرضت الفأرة الثوب أي قطعته فسمي كتاب الفرائض لأن سهام المواريث كلها مقدرة مقطوعة، ولأن سبب استحقاق الإرث القرابة وما هو ملحق بها كالولاء. أما القرابة فنوعان : رحم وزوجية، ونص الكتاب ناطق بهما وهو قوله تعالى يوصيكم الله في أولادكم [النساء : ۱۱] الآية. ولأن الميت لما استغنى عن ماله ولم يستحقه أحد يبقى عاطلاً سائباً والقريب أولى الناس به فيستحقه بالقرابة صلة كما يستحق النفقة حال حياة مورثه صلة. والزوجية أصل القرابة وأساسها لأن القرابات تفرعت وتشعبت منها فالتحق قرابة السبب بقرابة النسب في حق استحقاق الإرث وأما الولاء فلقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «الولاء لحمة كلحمة النسب يعني في حق استحقاق الميراث فقد التحق الولاء بالنسب، ولأنه بالإعتاق تسبب إلى إحيائه حكماً حين أزال عنه المالكية والولاية التي هي خاصة الإنسانية وكان السبب إلى الإحياء يعني بالاعتاق وكذا ولاء الموالاة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لمن سأله عمن أسلم على يد رجل هو أحق الناس به محياه أو مماته. وأما ما يحرم به الميراث فأنواع ثلاثة : الرق والكفر والقتل مباشرة بغير حق. أما الرق فلأنه سلب أهلية الملك، وأما الكفر فلقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لا يتوارث أهل ملتين لا كافر مسلماً ولا مسلم كافراً وأما القتل فلما يأتي في بابه وأما الحقوق المتعلقة بالتركة فأربعة : الكفن والدفن والوصية والدين والميراث فأول ما يبدأ منها بكفن الميت ودفنه لأن ستر عورته ومواراة سواته من أهم حوائجه، واستغرق الدين بماله لم يمنعه من ذلك حال حياته فكذلك بعد وفاته ثم تقضى ديونه لأنها أهم من قضاء ديون الله لاستغناء الله تعالى، وافتقار العبد لدي خصومة الله تعالى في حقوق العباد ولكثرة تجاوز الله تعالى وعفوه وتفضله وكرمه، ثم تنفذ وصيته من الثلث لأنها من حوائج الميت. والوارث إنما يستحق الميراث إذا استغنى المورث . وهذا إذا كانت الوصية بشيء بعينه، فإن كانت الوصية بثلث ماله أو ربعه فالموصى له شريك الورثة لأنها بمعنى الميراث لأنه ثبت حقه في جميع التركة شائعاً كحق سائر الورثة. ثم يقسم الباقي بين ورثته على فرائض الله تعالى وسنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. وأما أصناف الوارثين فثلاثة أصحاب الفرائض الذين لهم سهام مقدرة وعصبة وهم الذين يأخذون ما فضل من أصحاب الفروض وذوو الأرحام وهم الذين ليس لهم فروض مقدرة ولا لهم حقيقة تعصيب وإنما لهم مجرد قرابة. ولم يتعرض المؤلف لبيان ما يجري فيه الإرث وما لا يجري فيه الإرث فنقول : لا شك أن أعيان الأموال يجري فيها الإرث، وأما الحقوق فمنها ما يجري فيه الإرث حق الشفعة وخيار الشرط وحد القذف عندنا والنكاح لا يورث بلا خلاف وحبس المبيع وحبس الرهن يورث والوكالات والعواري والودائع لا تورث واختلف المشايخ في خيار العيب فمنهم من قال يورث، ومنهم من قال لا يورث ولكن لا يثبت للورثة ابتداء، والدية تورث بلا خلاف، وأما القصاص في الأصل أنه يورث ويثبت للورثة ابتداء ويجوز أن يقال القصاص لا يورث عند أبي حنيفة، ويورث عندهما والولاء لا يورث بلا خلاف وأما بيان الوقت الذي يجري فيه الإرث فنقول : هذا فصل اختلف المشايخ فيه ؛ قال مشايخ العراق : الإرث يثبت في آخر جزء من أجزاء حياة المورث. وقال مشايخ بلخ: الإرث يثبت بعد موت المورث. وفائدة هذا الاختلاف إنما تظهر في رجل تزوج بأمة الغير ثم قال لها إذا مات مولاك فأنت حرة فمات المولى والزوج وارثه هل تعتق؟ فعلى قول من يقول بأن الأرث يجري في آخر جزء

The first of these that is begun with is the shroud and burial of the deceased because covering his ‘awrah and veiling his nudity is among his most important needs; and if his wealth is consumed by debt, it does not prevent that during his life, so likewise after his death. Then his debts are paid because they are more important than paying the debts of Allah (swt), due to Allah's self-sufficiency and the slave's need for the dispute of Allah (swt) concerning the rights of the servants, and due to the abundance of Allah's indulgence, pardon, favor and generosity. Then his will (wasiyyah) is executed from one-third because it is among the needs of the deceased. And the heir only deserves inheritance when the deceased is free from need. This is when the will is for a specific thing; if the will is for one-third or one-quarter of his wealth, then the legatee is a partner with the heirs because it is in the nature of inheritance, since his right is established in the entire estate as a shared portion like the rights of the other heirs. Then the remainder is divided among his heirs according to the fara'id of Allah and the Sunnah of His Messenger (peace be upon him). As for the categories of heirs, they are three: the people of prescribed shares (ashab al-fara'id) who have fixed shares; the 'asabah (residuaries) who take what remains after the prescribed shares; and dhawu al-arham (uterine relatives) who have no fixed shares nor any true 'asabah, but merely kinship. The author did not address what is inherited and what is not inherited, so we say: there is no doubt that physical property (a'yan al-amwal) is inherited. As for rights, some of them are inherited: the right of pre-emption (shuf‘ah), the right of option (khiyar al-shart), and the hadd of qadhf (false accusation of adultery) in our school; marriage is not inherited without dispute; the right to detain the sold item and the right to detain the pawn (rahn) are inherited; agencies (wakalat), loans (‘ariyah), and deposits (wadi‘ah) are not inherited; the mashayikh (scholars) differed regarding the option of defect (khiyar al-‘ayb): some said it is inherited, others said it is not, but it is not established for the heirs initially; blood money (diyah) is inherited without dispute; as for qisas (retaliation), in principle it is inherited and established for the heirs initially, and it may be said that qisas is not inherited according to Abu Hanifah, but it is inherited according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad); wala' is not inherited without dispute. As for clarifying the time at which inheritance operates, we say: this is a chapter in which the scholars differed; the scholars of Iraq said: inheritance is established in the last part of the parts of the life of the deceased. The scholars of Balkh said: inheritance is established after the death of the deceased. The benefit of this difference appears in the case of a man who marries a slave woman belonging to someone else and then says to her: 'When your master dies, you are free'; then the master dies and the slave woman's husband is his heir; will she become free? According to the view that inheritance runs in the last part...
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the Book of Fara'id (Inheritance) from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a Hanafi commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author begins by emphasizing the importance of learning the science of inheritance, citing two prophetic hadiths that urge its study and warn of its loss. He then explains the linguistic meaning of 'fard' (الفرض) as 'estimation' or 'cutting', and notes that the book is so named because all inheritance shares are precisely determined and 'cut off' for the heirs. 

The causes of entitlement to inheritance are then discussed: kinship (qarabah) – both blood relation (rahm) and marital relation (zawjiyyah) – and wala' (patronage) arising from emancipation or alliance. The Qur'anic verse (al-Nisa' 4:11) is cited as the primary proof for inheritance through kinship. The author explains that marriage is the root of all kinship ties because it produces offspring and thus creates further relationships. Wala' is attached to lineage via a hadith that calls it a 'bond like the bond of lineage'. 

Three impediments to inheritance are listed: slavery (salahiyyat al-milk, capacity for ownership), disbelief (difference of religion), and intentional unjust killing. The order of payment from the estate is then explained: first the shroud and burial expenses, then debts, then the will (from one-third), and finally distribution among heirs. 

The heirs are categorized into three groups: ashab al-fara'id (Qur'anic share heirs), 'asabah (residuaries who take the remainder), and dhawu al-arham (uterine relatives who inherit only in the absence of others). 

The passage then discusses what rights can be inherited: physical property is clearly inherited, but certain rights (like pre-emption, option of condition, hadd of qadhf, detention of sold item and pawn) are inherited, while others (marriage, agencies, loans, deposits) are not. Blood money is inherited by consensus. Qisas (retaliation) is subject to disagreement between Abu Hanifah and his two companions. 

Finally, a significant intra-Hanafi dispute is presented: whether inheritance is established in the last moment of the deceased's life (Iraqi school) or after death (Balkh school). The practical difference appears in a scenario involving a slave woman's conditional emancipation: if her master dies and her husband (who inherits from the master) dies simultaneously, the outcome depends on when the inheritance is deemed to have vested.

Key Terms
العصبة (al-'asabah): Residuary heirs who inherit the surplus after the prescribed shares are taken.
ذوو الأرحام (dhawu al-arham): Uterine relatives who have no fixed share and are not residuaries; they inherit only in the absence of other heirs.
القصاص (al-qisas): Retaliation – the right to exact equivalent punishment for murder or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the intra-Hanafi dispute, what practical case illustrates the difference between inheritance vesting in the last part of life versus after death?
A) A man who marries a slave woman and promises her freedom upon her master's death
B) A woman who divorces her husband before he dies
C) A child born after the father's death
D) A will that exceeds one-third of the estate

Key Takeaway
The estate is settled in a fixed order; heirs are of three types; and the timing inheritance vests affects overlapping rights.

Causes and Impediments of Inheritance in Hanafi Fiqh
Ruling foundation for faraid: causes and impediments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two causes of inheritance (nasab and sabab) and identify the three impediments (riqq, kufr, qatl) with their respective proofs from the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Inheritance requires either lineage or legal bond; slavery, difference of religion, and direct killing block it.

Inheritance law (faraid) begins by defining what establishes a right to inherit and what prevents it. This passage from a classical Hanafi commentary presents the foundational causes and impediments, supported by Quranic and hadith proofs. Understanding these basics is essential before delving into share calculations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the positive causes
The passage states that inheritance is established through nasab (lineage) or sabab (legal cause). Sabab includes 'itq (manumission) and the wala' bond that follows, as well as wala' al-muwalah (alliance by contract).
Wala' al-muwalah is a unique Hanafi concept; other schools may not recognize it.
2
Connect the proof for sabab
The Prophet ﷺ said to a man who asked about someone who embraced Islam on his hands: 'He is the most entitled of people to him in life and death.' This hadith underpins the inheritance right via wala'.
The hadith is cited in the commentary as a direct proof.
3
List the three impediments
Three things prevent inheritance: riqq (slavery), kufr (difference of religion), and qatl (direct killing without right). Each is explained in the passage.
The impediments are mutually exclusive conditions that block inheritance entirely.
4
Understand the reasoning for each impediment
Slavery prevents because a slave lacks full ownership capacity. Kufr is based on the hadith 'People of two religions do not inherit from each other.' Qatl is deferred to its own chapter; the key condition is mubasharah (direct act) without right.
The Hanafi school requires direct physical causation for the killing to be an impediment.
5
Appreciate the cross-madhhab dimension
All schools agree on the basic impediments but differ on details. For example, the Shafi'i school holds that any killing (even accidental) prevents inheritance, while Hanafi restricts it to direct killing without right.
This ikhtilaf has practical consequences in estate distribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الفرائض
يعني يرث الإنسانية وكان السبب إلى الإحياء يعني بالاعتاق وكذا ولاء الموالاة لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لمن سأله عمن أسلم على يد رجل هو أحق الناس به محياه أو مماته. وأما ما يحرم به الميراث فأنواع ثلاثة : الرق والكفر والقتل مباشرة بغير حق. أما الرق فلأنه سلب أهلية الملك، وأما الكفر فلقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لا يتوارث أهل ملتين لا كافر مسلماً ولا مسلم كافراً وأما القتل فلما يأتي في بابه.
The Book of Faraid: He means that he inherits through human connection, and the cause is through freeing (i.e., by manumission) as well as through wala' of mawalat, due to his statement (peace be upon him) to the one who asked him about a person who embraced Islam on the hands of another: 'He is the most entitled of people to him in life and death.' As for what prevents inheritance, there are three types: slavery, disbelief, and direct killing without right. As for slavery, because it strips legal capacity (ahliyyat al-milk). As for disbelief, because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'People of two different religions do not inherit from each other' – neither a disbeliever inherits from a Muslim nor a Muslim from a disbeliever. As for killing, it will come in its proper chapter.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage from the commentary opens the chapter on inheritance (faraid) by stating the fundamental principle: inheritance is established through either lineage (nasab) or a legal cause (sabab). The cause includes both 'itq (manumission) and wala' al-muwalah (alliance by contract). The Prophet ﷺ said that whoever embraces Islam on the hands of another, that other is most entitled to his inheritance in life and death. The passage then lists three impediments: slavery (since a slave lacks full ownership capacity), difference of religion (based on the sahih hadith that people of two religions do not inherit from each other), and direct killing without right. Each is explained briefly. The commentary follows the author's order: first the positive causes, then the negative impediments.

Key Terms
الولاء (al-walā'): Legal bond of patronage that creates inheritance rights between freed slave and former master.
المباشرة (al-mubāsharah): Direct act causing death, as opposed to tashabbub (indirect causation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Slavery
B) Difference of religion
C) Direct killing without right
D) Physical distance

Key Takeaway
Inheritance is based on lineage or legal bond, and is blocked by slavery, difference of religion, and direct killing without right.

Order of Rights on the Estate
Describes the four rights (kafn, dayn, wasiyyah, mīrāth) and their order of priority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct order of the four rights on the estate and explain the rationale for each priority.

Core Idea
Shrouding and burial come before debts; debts before bequests; bequests before inheritance.

The estate of a deceased Muslim is not simply divided among heirs; there are prior rights that must be fulfilled. This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq lays out the compulsory order: first the funeral expenses, then debts, then bequests (from up to one-third), and finally inheritance. Understanding this sequence is essential for proper estate administration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four rights
List the four rights that attach to the estate: kafn (shroud and burial), dayn (debts), wasiyyah (bequest), and mīrāth (inheritance).
The text enumerates them as 'الكفن والدفن والوصية والدين والميراث' — note that burial is included with the shroud.
2
Determine the first priority
The passage states that shrouding and burial come first because covering the deceased's body is an immediate necessity, even if debts exist. Just as during life, basic needs precede debt repayment.
The analogy: 'استغرق الدين بماله لم يمنعه من ذلك حال حياته' — even if debt consumed his wealth, it didn't prevent covering his needs during life.
3
Explain why debts come second
After funeral expenses, debts to people are repaid because they are obligations to fellow humans, which are more stringent than obligations to Allah (like unpaid zakah). Allah is self-sufficient and forgiving, while people are not assumed to forgive.
The text says: 'لأنها أهم من قضاء ديون الله' — debts to people are more important than debts to Allah.
4
Position of bequests
Bequests (wasiyyah) are executed from one-third of the remaining estate after debts. They are a need of the deceased, but limited to protect heirs' rights. Note the distinction: if the bequest is a specific item, it is taken outright; if a fraction (like one-third), the legatee becomes a partner with the heirs.
The text explains: 'فإن كانت الوصية بشيء بعينه... فإن كانت الوصية بثلث ماله...'
5
Final step: inheritance
After all prior rights are fulfilled, the remainder is divided among the legal heirs according to the fixed shares prescribed in the Quran and Sunnah.
The passage concludes: 'ثم يقسم الباقي بين ورثته على فرائض الله تعالى'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الحقوق المتعلقة بالتركة فأربعة : الكفن والدفن والوصية والدين والميراث فأول ما يبدأ منها بكفن الميت ودفنه لأن ستر عورته ومواراة سواته من أهم حوائجه، واستغرق الدين بماله لم يمنعه من ذلك حال حياته فكذلك بعد وفاته ثم تقضى ديونه لأنها أهم من قضاء ديون الله لاستغناء الله تعالى، وافتقار العبد لدة خصومة الله تعالى في حقوق العباد ولكثرة تجاوز الله تعالى وعفوه وتفضله وكرمه، ثم تنفذ وصيته من الثلث لأنها من حوائج الميت. والوارث إنما يستحق الميراث إذا استغنى المورث . وهذا إذا كانت الوصية بشيء بعينه، فإن كانت الوصية بثلث ماله أو ربعه فالموصى له شريك الورثة لأنها بمعنى الميراث لأنه ثبت حقه في جميع التركة شائعاً كحق سائر الورثة. ثم يقسم الباقي بين ورثته على فرائض الله تعالى وسنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم.
As for the rights related to the estate, they are four: the shroud, burial, bequest, debt, and inheritance. The first to begin with is the shroud of the deceased and his burial, because covering his private parts and concealing his flaw is among his most important needs. Even if the debt encompasses his wealth, it does not prevent that during his life, so likewise after his death. Then his debts are repaid because they are more important than fulfilling debts owed to Allah; Allah is self-sufficient, while the slave is in need due to adversary with Allah in terms of rights of people, and due to Allah's abundant pardoning and forgiveness and grace. Then his bequest is executed from one-third because it is among the needs of the deceased. The heir only deserves inheritance if the testator has no need. This is if the bequest is for a specific thing; if the bequest is for one-third or one-fourth of his wealth, then the legatee is a partner with the heirs because it is like inheritance, as his right is established in the entire estate as a share like the right of the other heirs. Then the remainder is divided among his heirs according to the obligations of Allah and the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage explains the four rights that attach to the deceased's estate and their order of priority. First, the expenses of shrouding and burial are taken from the estate, even if the deceased owes debts, because covering the body is a pressing need. Second, monetary debts owed by the deceased are repaid, because they are obligations to fellow humans, which are more stringent than obligations to Allah (such as missed zakah) since Allah is forgiving and people are not presumed to forgive. Third, bequests (wasiyyah) are executed up to one-third of the estate, because the deceased's will is a form of charity from his wealth, but limited to a third to protect the heirs' rights. The author notes that if the bequest is of a specific item, it is taken from the estate before division; but if it is of a fraction (like one-third), the legatee becomes a partner with the heirs, taking a share from the entire estate proportionally. Finally, the remaining wealth is divided among the heirs according to the fixed shares in the Quran and Sunnah.

Key Terms
التركة (al-tarikah): The estate left by the deceased, comprising all assets after deducting rights of others (like mortgaged property).
الكفن (al-kafan): The shroud used to cover the deceased; its expense is the first priority from the estate.
الدين (al-dayn): Debts owed by the deceased to other people; repaid as the second priority.
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): Bequest made by the deceased; executed from up to one-third of the estate after debts.
الميراث (al-mīrāth): Inheritance; the remaining estate distributed among legal heirs after prior rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Execute bequests

D) Distribute inheritance

Key Takeaway
The estate must be administered in this order: funeral expenses, then debts, then bequests (from one-third), then inheritance to heirs.

Categories of Heirs and Inheritable Rights
Classification of heirs and inheritable rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify heirs into the three Hanafi categories (ashab al-fara'id, asaba, dhawi al-arham) and identify which rights are inheritable, including the intra-Hanafi dispute on qisas.

Core Idea
Not all rights pass by inheritance; tangible assets always do, but personal rights like marriage and agency do not.

This lesson introduces the foundational classification of heirs in Hanafi faraid and then explores the critical question: which legal rights can be inherited? Understanding both is essential for proper estate distribution. The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the categories and provides a detailed enumeration of inheritable and non-inheritable rights, including a significant intra-Hanafi difference on qisas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of heirs
Read the first part of the passage and list the three types: ashab al-fara'id (fixed-share heirs), asaba (residuaries), and dhawu al-arham (distant kindred). Note the defining characteristic of each.
Ashab al-fara'id have prescribed shares; asaba take the remainder; dhawu al-arham inherit only when no ashab or asaba exist.
2
Distinguish tangible assets from rights
The passage states that tangible assets (a'yan al-amwal) are always inherited. Rights are further divided. Make a mental table: inherited vs. not inherited vs. disputed.
This distinction is crucial because some rights are personal and do not transfer.
3
Enumerate inherited and non-inherited rights
From the passage, list rights that are inherited (shuf'a, khiyar al-shart, hadd al-qadhf, habs al-mabī', habs al-rahn, diyah), those not inherited (marriage, wakalah, a'ariyah, wadi'ah, wala'), and the disputed ones (khiyar al-'ayb, qisas).
Note that the listing is authoritative for the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the dispute on qisas
The passage reports that Abu Hanifa holds qisas is not inherited, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it is inherited. Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) and the mufta bihi position.
The mufta bihi is the view of the Sahibayn, so qisas is inherited in practice.
5
Apply the classification to a scenario
Given a deceased person's estate, classify heirs and determine which rights pass. For example, if the deceased had a pending option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb) and qisas claim, state whether heirs inherit them.
Khiyar al-'ayb is disputed; the passage says it does not initially vest in heirs but some say it is inherited. For fatwa, the relied-upon view should be consulted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما أصناف الوارثين فثلاثة أصحاب الفرائض الذين لهم سهام مقدرة وعصبة وهم الذين يأخذون ما فضل من أصحاب الفروض وذوو الأرحام وهم الذين ليس لهم فروض مقدرة ولا لهم حقيقة تعصيب وإنما لهم مجرد قرابة. ولم يتعرض المؤلف لبيان ما يجري فيه الإرث وما لا يجري فيه الإرث فنقول : لا شك أن أعيان الأموال يجري فيها الإرث، وأما الحقوق فمنها ما يجري فيه الإرث حق الشفعة وخيار الشرط وحد القذف عندنا والنكاح لا يورث بلا خلاف وحبس المبيع وحبس الرهن يورث والوكالات والعواري والودائع لا تورث واختلف المشايخ في خيار العيب فمنهم من قال يورث، ومنهم من قال لا يورث ولكن لا يثبت للورثة ابتداء، والدية تورث بلا خلاف، وأما القصاص في الأصل أنه يورث ويثبت للورثة ابتداء ويجوز أن يقال القصاص لا يورث عند أبي حنيفة، ويورث عندهما والولاء لا يورث بلا خلاف
As for the types of heirs, they are three: Ashab al-Fara'id (those who have fixed shares), Asaba (those who take what remains after the share holders), and Dhawu al-Arham (those who have no fixed share nor true asabiyya but merely blood relation). The author did not mention what is inherited and what is not inherited. So we say: There is no doubt that tangible assets are inherited. As for rights, some are inherited: the right of pre-emption (shuf'a), option of stipulation (khiyar al-shart), and the hadd of slander (qadhf) in our view. Marriage is not inherited without dispute. The right to retain the sold item (habs al-mabī') and the right to retain the pawn (habs al-rahn) are inherited. Agency (wakalah), loans (a'ariyah), and deposits (wadi'ah) are not inherited. The mashayikh differed regarding the option of defect (khiyar al-'ayb): some said it is inherited, some said it is not, but it does not initially vest in heirs. The blood money (diyah) is inherited without dispute. As for qisas (retaliation), in principle it is inherited and vests in heirs initially, but one may say qisas is not inherited according to Abu Hanifah, while it is inherited according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Walā' (patronage) is not inherited without dispute.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage first categorizes heirs into three groups: 1) Ashab al-Furud (Quranic share holders), 2) Asaba (residuaries who take leftover), and 3) Dhawu al-Arham (distant kindred who inherit only in the absence of the first two). Then it delves into which legal rights are transferable by inheritance. The general rule is that tangible assets (a'yan al-amwal) are always inherited. For intangible rights: some are inheritable (shuf'a, khiyar al-shart, hadd al-qadhf according to the Hanafi school, habs of sold item and pawn), some are not (marriage, agency, loans, deposits, walā'). Some are disputed: khiyar al-'ayb (option of defect) and qisas (retaliation). For qisas: Abu Hanifah says it does not pass by inheritance, while the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it does. The author notes that the relied-upon view is that qisas is inherited. The discussion concludes that walā' is never inherited.

Key Terms
أصحاب الفرائض (ashāb al-farāʼiḍ): Heirs entitled to fixed Quranic shares (e.g., 1/2, 1/4, 1/8, etc.)
العصبة (al-ʻaṣabah): Residuary heirs who take what remains after the Quranic share holders; typically male agnates.
ذوو الأرحام (dhawū al-arḥām): Distant kindred who are neither Quranic share holders nor residuaries; they inherit in the absence of the first two categories.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Heirs are classified into three groups, and inheritable rights include shuf'a, khiyar al-shart, and qisas (mufta bihi), but not marriage, agency, or deposits.

Timing of Inheritance: Iraq vs Balkh Scholars
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of inheritance with practical application

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on when inheritance vests and apply them to the scenario of a slave girl's conditional freedom.

Core Idea
Inheritance timing affects ownership; two Hanafi views yield opposite outcomes in the slave-girl example.

This passage presents a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute about the exact moment inheritance is established. While it may seem abstract, it has real-world consequences, as shown in the case of a man who promises freedom to a slave girl upon her master's death. Understanding this difference is key to grasping how inheritance and conditional rights interact in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify that the Iraq scholars say inheritance vests in the last moment of the deceased's life (ākhir juz'), while the Balkh scholars say it vests after death.
2
Understand the theoretical difference
Consider what each position implies: if inheritance vests before death, the heir owns the property during the last moment of the deceased's life; if after, ownership transfers only after death.
3
Apply to the slave-girl scenario
Work through the example: a man marries another's slave girl and says 'when your master dies you are free.' The master dies, and the husband is his heir. According to the Iraq view, the husband inherits her before death, so at the moment of the master's death he already owns her. Does the condition trigger? The passage notes that Abu Yusuf says she is not freed, while Zufar says she is freed. This shows a further ikhtilaf.
The passage does not give a final tarjih.
4
Note the further ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Zufar
Even among those who hold the Iraq view, there is disagreement on the outcome in the slave-girl case. This highlights the complexity of applying theoretical rules to concrete cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما بيان الوقت الذي يجري فيه الإرث فنقول : هذا فصل اختلف المشايخ فيه؛ قال مشايخ العراق : الإرث يثبت في آخر جزء من أجزاء حياة المورث. وقال مشايخ بلخ: الإرث يثبت بعد موت المورث. وفائدة هذا الاختلاف إنما تظهر في رجل تزوج بأمة الغير ثم قال لها إذا مات مولاك فأنت حرة فمات المولى والزوج وارثه هل تعتق؟ فعلى قول من يقول بأن الأرث يجري في آخر جزء من أجزاء حياة المورث تعتق بعد الموت، وذكر هذه المسألة في القدوري وذكر أنها على قول أبي يوسف لا تعتق، وعلى قول زفر تعتق .
As for the explanation of the time in which inheritance operates, we say: This is a chapter where the mashayikh differed. The scholars of Iraq said: Inheritance is established in the last part of the life of the deceased. The scholars of Balkh said: Inheritance is established after the death of the deceased. The benefit of this difference appears in a case of a man who married a slave girl belonging to another, then said to her: 'When your master dies, you are free.' Then the master dies, and the husband is his heir. Is she freed? According to the one who says inheritance operates in the last part of the life of the deceased, she becomes free after death. This matter is mentioned in al-Quduri, and it is stated that according to Abu Yusuf she is not freed, and according to Zufar she is freed.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage addresses a subtle issue: at what exact moment does the right of inheritance vest? The Iraq school holds that it vests in the last moment of the deceased's life (i.e., the moment before death). The Balkh school holds that it vests only after the actual death. The practical difference arises in a scenario: A man marries a slave girl belonging to another, and he tells her, 'When your master dies, you are free.' The master dies, and the husband (the slave girl's husband) is the master's heir. The question: Is she freed upon the master's death? If inheritance vests before death (Iraq view), then the husband inherits the master's property including the slave girl, and his ownership is established before death, so the condition 'when your master dies' triggers freedom, but since the husband owns her, does she become free? The example in al-Quduri states that according to Abu Yusuf, she is not freed (because he holds that inheritance vests after death, so the husband does not own her at the moment of the master's death, so the condition triggers, but the slave is still owned by the master's estate, and the husband inherits her later, but the freedom occurred? Actually the text says: according to Abu Yusuf she is not freed; according to Zufar she is freed. The passage leaves it at the level of ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
آخر جزء (ākhir juz'): The last moment of the deceased's life; the Iraq scholars say inheritance vests at this instant.
المشايخ (al-mashāyikh): Senior scholars of the Hanafi school; here, referring to the scholars of Iraq and Balkh as groups.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence of the disagreement between Iraq and Balkh scholars on timing of inheritance?
A) When to recite Quran for the deceased
B) Whether a slave woman becomes free upon her master's death if her husband inherits him
C) The amount of zakah on inherited wealth
D) The validity of wills made in the final illness

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two views on when inheritance vests (last moment of life vs after death), and this difference leads to opposite rulings in cases involving conditional freedom.

The Order of Estate Expenses: Tajhiz, Debt, Wasiyya, Inheritance
Establishes the order of expenses from the deceased's estate and details the treatment of debts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of priority for estate expenses and explain why debt takes precedence over bequest using the hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
Debt is paid before bequest because it is obligatory; burial comes first as a necessity.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq establishes the well-known Hanafi order of priority for spending from a deceased person's estate. Understanding this order is crucial for estate administrators and heirs. The passage also clarifies a key distinction between debts owed to people (dayn al-ibad) and debts owed to Allah (dayn Allah), which fall off at death unless bequeathed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four rights attached to the estate
List the four categories: tajhiz, debt, wasiyya, inheritance according to the Hanafi school.
Note the specific order given by the author.
2
Note the priority of tajhiz
Tajhiz (funeral preparation) is paid first from the estate, based on necessity and the Quranic principle of moderation.
The shroud should be moderate, neither extravagant nor stingy.
3
Locate the dalil for debt before bequest
The author cites the hadith of the Prophet (reported by Ali) giving debt precedence over bequest, and qiyas: debt is obligatory, bequest is voluntary.
The Quranic verse (4:12) mentions bequest before debt, but the hadith clarifies actual precedence.
4
Distinguish dayn al-ibad from dayn Allah
Debts owed to people must be paid; debts owed to Allah (like unpaid zakat) fall off at death because they require personal intention.
However, if the deceased bequeathed them or heirs volunteer, they may be paid.
5
Apply to an insufficient estate scenario
If the estate cannot cover both debt and bequest, debt is paid first, and the bequest is reduced or canceled.
This has practical implications for estate distribution.

الدين دين الصحة والبعض دين المرض ثبت بالبينة أو المعاينة فهو دين الصحة سواء. وفي المضمرات وسأل عمن مات وله مال في يد أجنبي وطلب منه الورثة تسليم ذلك وعلى الميت ديون والمدعي عليه يعلم بذلك وأنهم ورثته الابتلاء حتى يلزمه الفصل فيها، ولا العبادة حتى يجيز بفعل غيره من غير اختيار بخلاف دین العباد لأن فعله ليس بمقصود فيه ألا ترى أن صاحب الدين إذا ظفر بجنس حقه وأخذه يجتزئ بذلك ولا كذلك حق الله تعالى لأن Book of Faraid. From 'during his life'... So the gist is that what is considered is based on his life condition, because a person gives priority to himself during his life for what he needs of maintenance, clothing, and housing over creditors, as long as the right of others does not pertain to a specific asset of his. Similarly, after his death, his funeral preparation is given priority without extravagance or stinginess, and that is the amount of a sufficient shroud or the shroud of the Sunnah or the amount he used to wear during his life of the middle level or that which he used to adorn himself with on Eid and Friday gatherings and visits, according to their differences. Due to His statement: 'And those who, when they spend, are neither extravagant nor stingy, but are moderate between that' (al-Furqan: 67). He is honored alive and dead, so it is not permissible to uncover his private parts. In the athar: 'The bones of the dead have the same sanctity as the bones of the living.' So it must be known that four rights are attached to the estate: the preparation and burial of the deceased, debt, bequest, and inheritance. It begins with his preparation, shroud, and what is needed for his burial in a reasonable manner. In al-Kafi: without extravagance or stinginess. In al-Tahdhib: When a man dies, from his estate one begins with his shrouding and preparation in the manner (al-mithl), and al-mithl is what he wears when going out. It is said: on Eids. It is said: on Friday and congregations, and that is the most correct. Then debt. And it is not free from either being all debt of illness, or some debt of health and some debt of illness. If it is all, one is not given priority over another. If it is debt of health and some debt of illness established by evidence or inspection, then it is debt of health equally. In al-Mudmarat: He asked about one who died and had wealth in the hands of a stranger, and the heirs asked for its delivery, and the deceased had debts, and the defendant knew that and that they were his heirs. He made a settlement with the heirs regarding what he owed and the wealth in his hand, then he paid it from his own wealth to them. Is he liable to the creditors of the deceased? He said: Yes, and he is not absolved by this settlement. He asked: About one who died and had wealth in the hands of a stranger, and he has heirs who have nothing in their hands, and the deceased has debts. Who claims the creditor? And who establishes the evidence? He said: The one in possession (dhu al-yad) in the presence of the heirs. And his bequests are executed from one-third of his wealth. In al-Fara'id of al-Khasami: Then his bequests are executed from one-third of what remains after the shroud and debt, unless the heirs permit more than one-third. And the remainder is divided among the heirs according to the shares of inheritance. This is when the bequest is of a specific thing. As for when the bequest is undivided, such as a bequest of one-third or one-quarter, the bequest is not given priority over inheritance at all; rather, the legatee becomes a partner with the heirs in this case. His right increases with an increase in the estate of the deceased and decreases with a decrease in the estate of the deceased. He (the author) said: (Then his debt) due to His statement: 'After a bequest you make or a debt' (al-Nisa': 12). Ali, may Allah honor his face, said: You read the bequest as preceding the debt, but I witnessed the Prophet, peace be upon him, give debt precedence over the bequest. And because debt is obligatory from the start, while a bequest is voluntary, and beginning with the obligatory is better. The mention in order does not indicate actual precedence. What is meant is debt that has a claim from the side of people (rights of humans), not the debt of zakat, expiations, and the like, because these debts fall away with death, so the heirs are not required to pay them unless he bequeathed them or the heirs voluntarily pay them, because the pillar in acts of worship is the intention of the obligated person performing the act, and it has been lost with his death, so its continuation is inconceivable. Book of Faraid. 367. One with a prescribed share: for the father one-sixth with child and child's son, and the grandfather is like the father as long as there is no mother in his lineage, except in her rejection (radd) of one-third of what remains, and the exclusion of the mother of the father he excludes the siblings. For the mother one-third. The obligatory (al-wajib) without need because the Hereafter is not a realm of trial so that he would be obligated to act in it, nor is it worship so that it would be fulfilled by someone else's action without choice. Unlike the debt of people (rights of humans) because his action is not the purpose in it; do you not see that if the creditor gets hold of the equivalent of his right and takes it, he is satisfied with that? Not so with the right of Allah, because the purpose in it is his action and intention as a trial, and Allah is independent of his wealth and of all the worlds. However, Allah has given charity to the servant through one-third of his wealth at the end of his life to compensate for what he has neglected, as a favor to him. If he bequeaths it, the action of the heirs takes the place of his action due to the existence of his choice through the bequest; otherwise, no.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from al-Bahr al-Raiq, a Hanafi sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It establishes the order of priorities from the deceased's estate: 1) Tajhiz and takfin (preparation and shroud), 2) Debt (dayn), 3) Wasiyya (bequest) up to one-third, and 4) Inheritance among heirs. The author explains that the shroud should be moderate, based on the Quranic verse (al-Furqan 67) and the principle that the deceased's body is honored. Then, the debt of people (rights of humans) is given precedence over bequests, citing the hadith that the Prophet gave debt priority and the legal reasoning that debt is obligatory while bequest is voluntary. The Quranic verse (al-Nisa' 12) mentions bequest before debt, but this is not indicative of actual precedence; it is merely a mention. Then, the author distinguishes between debt owed to people and debt owed to Allah (such as zakat and expiation): the latter falls away upon death because it is an act of worship requiring intention, which cannot be completed after death; however, if the deceased bequeathed it or the heirs volunteer, it may be paid. The passage then transitions to inheritance, stating that the father's share is one-sixth when there is a child or son's child, and the grandfather is like the father under certain conditions.

Key Terms
تجهيز (tajhīz): The preparation of the deceased for burial, including washing, shrouding, and funeral expenses.
دين العباد (dayn al-ʿibād): Debts owed to human beings, such as loans or unpaid purchases.
دين الله (dayn Allāh): Obligations to Allah, such as unpaid zakat or expiations (kaffarat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Debt, bequest, burial, inheritance
B) Bequest, debt, burial, inheritance
C) Burial, debt, bequest, inheritance
D) Burial, bequest, debt, inheritance

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi order of estate expenses is: tajhiz, then debt of people, then bequest up to one-third, then inheritance.

The Father's Three States and the Grandfather's Position in Inheritance
Explains the three states of the father's share and the grandfather's analogous position in faraid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three states of the father's share in Hanafi inheritance and apply them to determine the shares of the father and grandfather in given scenarios.

Core Idea
The father inherits in three ways: prescribed one-sixth, both prescribed and residue, or pure residue.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the three distinct inheritance positions of the father, supported by Quranic evidence and consensus. It also introduces the grandfather's analogous role, with important exceptions. Understanding these states is fundamental to solving faraid problems involving the father or grandfather.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three states
Read the passage to find the three states: (1) absolute prescribed share (one-sixth) with a son or son's son, (2) prescribed share plus agnatic residue with a daughter or son's daughter, (3) absolute agnatic residue when no child exists.
Memorize these three cases as they are the foundation for father's share.
2
Examine the Quranic and Hadith evidence
Note the verse (4:11) for the one-sixth and the hadith about giving faraid to their owners. Understand how the father becomes asabah through the mother's third verse (4:11) implying the father takes the remainder.
The dalil for asabah is derived from the structure of the verse.
3
Understand why a grandson is considered a 'child'
The passage explains that a son's son is legally a child by consensus and custom, citing the Quranic address 'O children of Adam' and a poetic line. This is critical for applying the first state.
This is a ruling based on consensus, not qiyas alone.
4
Compare the grandfather to the father
The text states the grandfather is like the father except in three matters: (1) the return (radd) of one-third of what remains, (2) the exclusion of the mother of the father, (3) excluding siblings. These exceptions modify the grandfather's share in specific cases.
These exceptions will be detailed in later lessons; for now, note the similarity and differences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ثم يقسم بين ورثته وهم ذو فرض أي ذو سهم مقدر) لما تلونا ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام ألحقوا الفرائض بأهلها فما فضل فلذي عصبة ذكر»(۱) وفي رواية «فلأولى رجل ذكر وذلك على سبيل التأكيد كقوله تعالى تلك عشرة كاملة [البقرة : ١٩٦] ولا طائر يطير بجناحيه ﴾ [الأنعام: ٣٨] قال رحمه الله : فللأب السدس مع الولد وولد الابن لقوله تعالى ولأبويه لكل واحد منهما السدس مما ترك إن كان له ولد ﴾ [النساء: ١١] جعل له السدس مع الولد وولد الابن ولد شرعاً بالإجماع قال الله تعالى يا بني آدم ﴾ [الأعراف: ۳۱] وكذا عرفاً قال الشاعر : بنونا بنو أبنائنا وبناتنا أبناء الرجال الأباعد بنوهن وليس دخول ولد الابن في الولد من باب الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز بل من باب عموم المجاز أو عرف كون ولد ابن كحكم الولد بدليل آخر وهو الإجماع. وجميع أحوال الأب في الفرائض ثلاثة : أحدها الفرض المطلق وهو السدس وذلك مع الابن أو ابن الابن وإن سفل لما تلونا. والحالة الثانية الفرض والتعصيب وذلك مع البنت أو بنت الابن الفرض بما تلونا والتعصيب لما روينا والحالة الثالثة التعصيب المطلق وذلك إذا لم يكن للميت ولد ولا ولد ابن لقوله تعالى فإن لم يكن له ولد وورثه أبواه فلامه الثلث ﴾ [النساء : ١١] ذكر فرض الأم وجعل الباقي دليل على أنه عصبة . قال رحمه الله : (والجد كالأب إذا لم يتخلل في نسبته أم إلا في ردها في الثلث ما بقي وحجب أم الأب فيحجب الأخوة أي الجد كالأب إذا لم يتخلل
He (the author) said: (Then it is divided among his heirs, and they are people with prescribed shares, i.e., people with a fixed portion) - as we have recited, and due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Give the prescribed shares to their owners, and what remains is for the nearest male relative' (narrated by Bukhari, Muslim). In another narration: 'For the nearest male relative.' And that is by way of emphasis, like His saying: 'That is ten, complete' (al-Baqarah: 196) and 'There is no bird that flies with its wings' (al-An'am: 38). He (the author) said: For the father is one-sixth with the child and the son's child, due to His saying: 'And for his parents, each of them one-sixth of what he leaves if he has a child' (al-Nisa': 11). He made for him one-sixth with the child, and the son's child is legally a child by consensus. Allah said: 'O children of Adam' (al-A'raf: 31). Likewise customarily. The poet said: 'Our sons are the sons of our sons, and our daughters are the sons of distant men.' And the inclusion of the son's child in 'child' is not by way of combining literal and figurative meaning, but by way of general figurative meaning or custom, that the son's child is like the ruling of the child based on another evidence, which is consensus. And all the states of the father in inheritance are three: First, absolute prescribed share, which is one-sixth, and that is with the son or the son's son, however low, as we have recited. Second, prescription and agnatic succession (ta'sib), and that is with the daughter or the daughter's son: prescription as we have recited, and agnatic succession as we have narrated. Third, absolute agnatic succession, and that is when the deceased has no child and no son's child, due to His saying: 'But if he has no child and his parents inherit him, then for his mother is one-third' (al-Nisa': 11). He mentioned the mother's prescribed share and made the remainder indicate that he (the father) is an asabah. He (the author) said: (And the grandfather is like the father as long as there is no mother in his lineage, except in her rejection (radd) of one-third of what remains, and the exclusion of the mother of the father he excludes the siblings, i.e., the grandfather is like the father as long as there is no mother in his lineage.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage explains the division of the estate among heirs, focusing on the father's share. The author first cites the hadith 'Give the prescribed shares to their owners, and what remains is for the nearest male relative.' Then he explains the three states of the father: (1) When there is a son or son's son, the father gets one-sixth as a prescribed share (fard). (2) When there is a daughter or son's daughter, the father takes one-sixth as a prescribed share and also inherits the residue as an asabah (by ta'sib). (3) When there are no children at all, the father inherits the entire residue as an asabah (after the mother takes her third if present). The text also establishes that a son's son (grandson) is included in the meaning of 'child' by consensus. Finally, it states that the grandfather (father's father) is treated like the father in inheritance, with three exceptions: (a) regarding the return (radd) of one-third of what remains, (b) the exclusion of the mother of the father, and (c) excluding siblings. These exceptions require further elaboration.

Key Terms
فرض (farḍ): A prescribed share in inheritance, fixed by Quran or Sunnah.
تعصيب (taʿṣīb): Agnatic succession; inheriting the residue after prescribed shares are given.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the deceased leaves a daughter and no son, what is the father's share according to the Hanafi school?
A) One-sixth only
B) One-sixth plus the residue
C) The entire residue
D) No share

Key Takeaway
Master the three states of the father's inheritance: fard only with a son, fard+asabah with a daughter, and asabah only when no child.
