The Father's Share in Inheritance: Fixed Share and Residual
Ruling on the father's share with proof from Quran and Sunnah, enumerating three states.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three possible states of the father in inheritance and derive each from the Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
The father inherits either as a fixed-share holder (one-sixth) or as a residuary, depending on the presence of descendants.

This lesson examines the father's inheritance share in detail, based on Quran 4:11 and the Prophet's hadith. Understanding these rules is crucial for correct distribution of estates. The father's status shifts between fixed-share recipient and residuary heir, a distinction that often causes confusion.

Guided Path
1
Understand the division of heirs
Recognize that heirs are divided into fixed-share holders (ashab al-fara'id) and residuaries (asabah). The father can belong to either category.
2
Identify the proof for the father's one-sixth
Quran 4:11 assigns each parent one-sixth when the deceased has a child. This is the primary evidence for the father's fixed share.
The verse uses the term 'walad' (child), which by consensus includes grandchildren through sons.
3
Note the inclusion of the son's son as 'child'
The passage argues that a son's son is legally considered a child by consensus and custom, citing Quranic usage and poetry. This understanding is crucial for applying the one-sixth rule when a grandson exists.
This is a linguistic and legal expansion (majaz) rather than mixing literal and figurative.
4
Enumerate the three states of the father
State 1: Only fixed share (one-sixth) when there is a son or son's son. State 2: Fixed share plus residual when with a daughter or son's daughter. State 3: Only residual when no child or grandchild exists.
The hadith about assigning fixed shares and giving the remainder to the nearest male agnate supports the residual role.
5
Apply the evidence to each state
For state 1, cite Quran 4:11. For state 2, combine the verse for the one-sixth and the hadith for the residual. For state 3, the mother gets one-third, and the father takes the rest as asabah, as indicated by the same verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (ثم يقسم بين ورثته وهم ذو فرض أي ذو سهم مقدر) لما تلونا ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «ألحقوا الفرائض بأهلها فما فضل فلذي عصبة ذكر» وفي رواية «فلأولى رجل ذكر وذلك على سبيل التأكيد كقوله تعالى {تلك عشرة كاملة} ولا طائر يطير بجناحيه». قال رحمه الله : فللأب السدس مع الولد وولد الابن لقوله تعالى {ولأبويه لكل واحد منهما السدس مما ترك إن كان له ولد} جعل له السدس مع الولد وولد الابن ولد شرعاً بالإجماع قال الله تعالى {يا بني آدم} وكذا عرفاً قال الشاعر : بنونا بنو أبنائنا وبناتنا بنوهن أبناء الرجال الأباعد وليس دخول ولد الابن في الولد من باب الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز بل من باب عموم المجاز أو عرف كون ولد ابن كحكم الولد بدليل آخر وهو الإجماع. وجميع أحوال الأب في الفرائض ثلاثة : أحدها الفرض المطلق وهو السدس وذلك مع الابن أو ابن الابن وإن سفل لما تلونا. والحالة الثانية الفرض والتعصيب وذلك مع البنت أو بنت الابن الفرض بما تلونا والتعصيب لما روينا والحالة الثالثة التعصيب المطلق وذلك إذا لم يكن للميت ولد ولا ولد ابن لقوله تعالى {فإن لم يكن له ولد وورثه أبواه فلامه الثلث} ذكر فرض الأم وجعل الباقي دليل على أنه عصبة.
He (the author) said: Then he (the deceased) is divided among his heirs, and they are people of fixed share, meaning those with a prescribed portion. Due to what we recited and due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'Assign the fixed shares to their rightful recipients, and whatever remains goes to the closest male agnate.' In another narration: 'to the nearest male relative.' And that is by way of emphasis, like His saying: 'That is ten complete' and 'No bird flies with its two wings.' He (the author) said: For the father, the one-sixth with the child and the son's child, due to His saying: 'And for his parents, for each one of them, one-sixth of what he left, if he has a child.' He assigned him the sixth with the child and the son's child, and the son's child is considered a child legally by consensus. Allah said: 'O children of Adam' and likewise customarily. The poet said: 'Our sons are the sons of our sons, and our daughters are the sons of distant men.' And the inclusion of the son's child in the term 'child' is not from the combination of literal and figurative, but from the generality of the metaphor or custom that the son's child is like the child in ruling, based on another evidence which is consensus. And all the states of the father in inheritance are three: one: absolute fixed share, which is one-sixth, and that is with a son or a son's son, however low, due to what we recited. The second state: fixed share and agnation, and that is with a daughter or a son's daughter: the fixed share due to what we recited, and agnation due to what we narrated. The third state: absolute agnation, and that is when the deceased has no child nor son's child, due to His saying: 'But if he has no child and his parents inherit from him, then his mother gets one-third.' He mentioned the mother's fixed share and made the remainder evidence that he (the father) is an agnate.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on the father's share in inheritance with Quranic and Hadith evidence. The author first cites the general principle: heirs are either fixed-share holders (ashab al-fara'id) or residuaries (asabah). Then the father's share is detailed: he gets one-sixth (fard) when there is a child or grandchild (son's son) alive. The proof is Quran 4:11. The passage explains that a son's son is legally considered a 'child' by consensus and custom. Then it enumerates the three possible states for the father: (1) only a fixed share (one-sixth) when there is a son or son's son, (2) fixed share plus residual when with a daughter or son's daughter, (3) only residual when no child or grandchild. This classification is based on Quran and hadith.

Key Terms
ذو فرض (dhu fard): An heir entitled to a fixed Quranic share.
السدس (al-suds): One-sixth, the father's share in presence of child or grandchild.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One-sixth plus residual
B) One-sixth only
C) Residual only
D) One-third

Key Takeaway
The father's inheritance depends on the presence of descendants: with a child, he gets one-sixth; with a daughter, he gets one-sixth plus residual; with no descendant, he is the sole residuary.

The Grandfather's Inheritance: True vs False and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on the grandfather's inheritance with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the true and false grandfather in Hanafi inheritance law and explain the differences between Abu Hanifa and his two students regarding the grandfather's co-existence with siblings.

Core Idea
The grandfather inherits like the father, but only if his lineage is free of females; and whether he excludes siblings depends on which Hanafi authority you follow.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses the complex status of the grandfather in Hanafi faraid. While he is generally likened to the father, there are two important exceptions. More critically, within the Hanafi school itself, there is a well-known dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two major students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) over whether the grandfather excludes siblings or shares with them. Understanding this dispute is essential for correctly applying the rulings and for appreciating the later fatwa tradition that often recommended reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of grandfather
Distinguish al-jadd al-sahih (true, no female in lineage) from al-jadd al-fasid (false, female present). The false one inherits only as dhu arham.
The true grandfather's lineage must have only males between him and the deceased.
2
List the exceptions where grandfather differs from father
Two exceptions: (1) returning the mother's share from 1/3 of total to 1/3 of what remains, and (2) the grandfather does not prevent the mother of the father (whereas the father does).
In all other inheritance aspects, the true grandfather is treated like the father.
3
Understand the baseline ruling: grandfather like father in absence of father
In the absence of the father, the grandfather takes the same three states as the father: (a) one-sixth with a child heir, (b) remainder after Quranic shares if no child, (c) one-sixth if no other heir? Actually standard faraid: with son, grandfather is excluded; with daughter, 1/6; if no children, he may take the remainder by ta'sib.
The passage states 'he has the three states that we mentioned for the father' and adds a fourth state: falling from inheritance due to the father.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on grandfather vs siblings
Abu Hanifa: grandfather excludes siblings entirely (like father). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad: grandfather divides with siblings by muqasamah (treating grandfather as one of them) or takes one-third if more beneficial.
The thamarah al-khilaf is clear: siblings get nothing under Abu Hanifa; they share under the Sahibayn.
5
Consider the later fatwa recommendations
Some scholars (like al-Sarakhsi) preferred the Sahibayn's view; others refused to give a fixed fatwa and recommended reconciliation (sulh) between grandfather and siblings due to the strong disagreement among the Companions.
The passage quotes al-Nasafi advising against saying the entire wealth goes to the grandfather out of reverence for Abu Bakr.

وفاسد. فالفاسد من جملة ذوي الأرحام والصحيح له أحوال ثلاثة على ما نحو ما ذكرنا في الأب وحكمه حال عدم الأب في استحقاقه السهم والتعصيب حكم الأب وحكم الواحد السدس، وإذا كثر فالسدس بينهم بالسوية. الفاصل بين الجد الصحيح والفاسد أن الصحيح هو الذي لم يتخلل في نسبته إلى الميت أم، وإن تخلل في نسبه إلى الميت أم فهو فاسد والجد الصحيح كالأب. واختلف مشايخنا في الفتوى في مسائل الجد فامتنع بعضهم من الفتوى أصلاً لكثرة الاختلاف الواقع فيما بين الصحابة، وأفتى بها الآخرون لكن اختلفوا فيما بينهم كان الشيخ الإمام السرخسي يفتي في مسائل الجد بقول أبي يوسف ومحمد، وبعض المتأخرين من مشايخنا اختار الفتوى بالصلح في مواضع الخلاف قالوا كنا نفتي بالصلح في الأجير في مواضع الخلاف المشترك لاختلاف الصحابة واختلاف الصحابة هنا أظهر فكان الفتوى بالصلح هنا أحق. وقال الشيخ الإمام شمس الدين الحلواني : قال مشايخنا بأن الصواب في مسائل الجد أن يعطي الجد ما اتفقوا عليه ثم يقسم بين الجد وبين الإخوة والأخوات نصفين أمروا بالصلح. قال القاضي الإمام عماد الدين النسفي : لا ينبغي للمفتي أن يقول المال كله للجد عند الصديق وإنما قال أبو الثلث، فإن كان الثلث خيراً من المقاسمة كجد وثلاثة إخوة يعطي الثلث ويقسم الباقي بينهم على فرائض الله تعالى.
And the grandfather is like the father if no female intervenes in his lineage except in returning her (the mother) from one-third of the total to one-third of what remains, and in preventing the mother of the father; the grandfather prevents the siblings. That is, the grandfather is like the father if no female intervenes in his lineage to the deceased, and this is the true grandfather, except in two matters: one of them is in returning the mother of the deceased from one-third of the total to one-third of what remains, and preventing the mother of the father in the case of a husband and two parents or a wife and two parents, then the father returns her to it like the grandfather. And in preventing the mother of the father, the father prevents her but not the grandfather. And if a female intervenes in his lineage to the deceased, he is a false (grandfather) and does not inherit except as a relative (dhu arham) because the female intervention cuts off the lineage, and lineage is to fathers because lineage is for identification and fame, and that is by known (males) which are males, not females. And his saying 'like the father' means in the absence of the father, because the grandfather is called a father. Allah said quoting Yusuf (peace be upon him): 'And I followed the religion of my fathers, Ibrahim, Ishaq, and Ya'qub.' Ishaq was his grandfather and Ibrahim was his great-grandfather. And Allah said: 'O children of Adam, let not Satan tempt you as he removed your parents from Paradise,' and they are Adam and Hawwa. So if he is a father, he enters the text either by way of general metaphor or by consensus as we mentioned regarding the son's son. So he has the three states that we mentioned for the father, and he has a fourth state: falling (from inheritance) because of the father, because the father is closer and he derives from him, so he does not inherit with him, but he takes his place in his absence. And his saying: 'and he prevents the siblings' means the grandfather prevents the siblings like the father, because he takes his place. This is the absolute statement of Abu Hanifa, as will be explained, God willing. And the correct view is that the grandfather is of two types: true and false. The false is among the dhawi al-arham, and the true has three states as mentioned for the father, and his ruling in the absence of the father regarding entitlement to the share and agnation is the ruling of the father. The ruling of one (grandfather) is one-sixth, and if there are many, one-sixth is divided equally among them. The distinction between the true and false grandfather is that the true is one in whose lineage to the deceased no female intervenes, and if a female intervenes in his lineage to the deceased, then he is false. The true grandfather is like the father. And our scholars differed on giving fatwa in matters of the grandfather. Some refrained from giving any fatwa due to the abundance of disagreement among the Companions. Others gave fatwa but differed among themselves. Sheikh Imam al-Sarakhsi used to give fatwa according to the statement of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Some later scholars chose reconciliation in points of disagreement. They said: we used to give fatwa for reconciliation for the hireling in points of dispute due to the difference of the Companions, and the difference here is more apparent, so giving fatwa for reconciliation is more appropriate here. Sheikh Imam Shams al-Din al-Halwani said: Our scholars said that the correct in matters of the grandfather is to give the grandfather what they agree upon, then divide between the grandfather and the siblings in half. They recommended reconciliation. Judge Imam Imad al-Din al-Nasafi said: It is not proper for a mufti to say that the entire wealth belongs to the grandfather according to al-Siddiq (Abu Bakr). Rather, Abu Hanifa said that out of veneration for the affair of al-Siddiq. And regarding the principles of Zayd (may Allah be pleased with him), the first principle is that the siblings are like one of them, he (the grandfather) divides with them and they divide with him, and he competes with them and they compete with him as long as division is better for him than one-third of the total wealth, like a grandfather and one brother, as long as he does not decrease from one-third. If one-third is better than division, like a grandfather and three brothers, he takes one-third and the rest is divided among them according to the laws of Allah.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage addresses the inheritance position of the grandfather. It first states that the grandfather is generally treated like the father except in two specific cases: (1) when returning the mother's share from one-third of the total to one-third of the remainder, and (2) in preventing the mother of the father. Then it distinguishes between a true grandfather (whose lineage to the deceased has no female link) and a false grandfather (with a female link). The true grandfather takes the same three states as the father. However, when the grandfather coexists with siblings, there is a well-known dispute among Hanafi scholars. The text presents multiple positions: Abu Hanifa's view that the grandfather excludes siblings (out of reverence for Abu Bakr al-Siddiq), the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad that the grandfather divides with siblings (by muqasamah or taking one-third), and a later recommendation to settle through reconciliation (sulh). The passage also mentions that some scholars refrained from giving fatwa in these cases due to the complexity.

Key Terms
الجد الصحيح (al-jadd al-sahih): The true grandfather, whose lineage to the deceased has no female link.
الجد الفاسد (al-jadd al-fasid): The false grandfather, with a female link; inherits as dhu arham, not as a true heir.
المقاسمة (al-muqasamah): Division between grandfather and siblings as if the grandfather is one of them.
الصلح (al-sulh): Reconciliation; a recommended way to resolve the dispute in grandfather cases.

Key Takeaway
The grandfather's status is like the father with two exceptions, but the extent to which he excludes siblings is a matter of legitimate difference within the Hanafi school, often resolved by reconciliation.

The True Grandfather: Definition and Inheritance Status
Defines the true grandfather and his status as a substitute for the father.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the true grandfather, distinguish him from the false grandfather, and state his basic inheritance rights in the absence of the father.

Core Idea
The true grandfather inherits like the father—by fard and 'asabah—except in two specific situations.

Inheritance law carefully distinguishes between the true grandfather (al-jadd al-sahih) and the false grandfather (al-jadd al-fasid). The true grandfather, a male ancestor with no female in his lineage to the deceased, is treated like the father in most respects. This lesson explores his definition, his status as a substitute for the father, and the two exceptions where the grandfather differs from the father. Understanding these fundamentals is essential before delving into the more complex disputes about his interaction with siblings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of the true grandfather
Read the opening definition: a male ancestor with no female intervening in his lineage to the deceased. Contrast with the false grandfather, where a female intervenes.
The false grandfather inherits only as a uterine relative (dhu rahm).
2
Understand the distinction from the false grandfather
Note the criterion: if a female appears anywhere in the lineage, the grandfather becomes 'false' and does not inherit as a true grandfather.
3
Recognize that the true grandfather is like the father in inheritance
The text states he takes the place of the father in his absence, having the same three states: fard, 'asabah, and being excluded by the father. He also excludes siblings like the father.
This is the default position; the dispute with Abu Yusuf and Muhammad comes later.
4
Note the two exceptions where the grandfather differs from the father
First, in returning the mother's share (al-radd) from one-third of the whole to one-third of the remainder. Second, in excluding the mother of the father (the paternal grandmother) – the father excludes her, the grandfather does not.
These exceptions show the grandfather is not absolutely identical to the father.
5
Summarize the grandfather's inheritance states
The true grandfather has four states: (1) excluded by the father, (2) inherits by fard (1/6) when there is a son or son's son, (3) inherits by 'asabah when alone, and (4) combines fard and 'asabah when there is no son but there are other heirs.
These mirror the father's states except for the two exceptions noted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الفرائض
في نسبه إلى الميت أنثى وهو الجد الصحيح إلا في مسألتين: أحدهما في رد أم الميت من ثلث الجميع إلى ثلث ما بقي وحجب أم الأب في زوج وأبوين أو زوجة وأبوين فإن الأب يردها إليه كالجد وفي حجب أم الأب فإن الأب يحجبها دون الجد، وإن تخلل في نسبه إلى الميت أم النسب كان فاسداً فلا يرث إلا على أنه من ذوي الأرحام لأن تخلل الأم في النسبة يقطع والنسب إلى الآباء لأن النسب للتعريف والشهرة وذلك تكون بالمشهورة وهو الذكور دون الإناث. وقوله كالأب يعني عند عدم الأب لأن الجد يسمى أباً قال الله تعالى حاكياً عن يوسف عليه الصلاة والسلام واتبعت ملة آبائي ابراهيم واسحاق ويعقوب [يوسف: ٣٨] وكان اسحاق جده وإبراهيم جد أبيه. وقال الله تعالى با بني آدم لا يفتننكم الشيطان كما أخرج أبويكم من الجنة [الأعراف: ۲۷] وهما آدم وحواء عليهما السلام فإذا كان أباً دخل في النص إما بطريق عموم المجاز أو بالإجماع على ما نحو ما ذكرنا في ابن الابن فكان له الأحوال الثلاثة التي ذكرناها في الأب وله حالة رابعة وهو السقوط بالأب لأنه أقرب منه ويدلي به فلا يرث معه وإنما يقوم مقامه عند عدمه. وقوله ويحجب الإخوة يعني الجد يحجب الإخوة كالأب لأنه قائم مقامه، وهذا على إطلاقه قول أبي حنيفة على ما يجيء بيانه إن شاء الله تعالى والأصح أن الجد نوعان: صحيح وفاسد. فالفاسد من جملة ذوي الأرحام والصحيح له أحوال ثلاثة على ما نحو ما ذكرنا في الأب وحكمه حال عدم الأب في استحقاقه السهم والتعصيب حكم الأب وحكم الواحد السدس، وإذا كثر فالسدس بينهم بالسوية. الفاصل بين الجد الصحيح والفاسد أن الصحيح هو الذي لم يتخلل في نسبته إلى الميت أم، وإن تخلل في نسبه إلى الميت أم فهو فاسد والجد الصحيح كالأب. واختلف مشايخنا في الفتوى في مسائل الجد فامتنع بعضهم من الفتوى أصلاً لكثرة الاختلاف الواقع فيما بين الصحابة، وأفتى بها الآخرون لكن اختلفوا فيما بينهم كان الشيخ الإمام السرخسي يفتي في مسائل الجد بقول أبي يوسف ومحمد، وبعض المتأخرين من مشايخنا اختار والفتوى بالصلح في مواضع الخلاف قالوا كنا نفتي بالصلح في الأجير في مواضع الخلاف المشترك لاختلاف الصحابة واختلاف الصحابة هنا أظهر فكان الفتوى بالصلح هنا أحق. وقال الشيخ الإمام شمس الدين الحلواني : قال مشايخنا بأن الصواب في مسائل الجد أن يعطي الجد ما اتفقوا عليه ثم يقسم بين الجد وبين الإخوة والأخوات نصفين أمروا بالصلح. قال القاضي الإمام عماد الدين النسفي : لا ينبغي للمفتي أن يقول المال كله للجد عند الصديق وإنما قال أبو حنيفة بذلك تعظيماً لأمر الصديق وأما أصول زيد رضي الله عنه فالأصل الأول أن الإخوة والأخوات كأحدهم يقاسمهم ويقاسمونه ويزاحمهم ويزاحمونه ما دامت المقاسمة خيراً له من ثلث جميع المال كجد وأخ إذ لا ينقص من الثلث، فإن كان الثلث خيراً من المقاسمة كجد وثلاثة إخوة يعطي الثلث ويقسم الباقي بينهم على فرائض الله تعالى.

يجعل الجد له الأصل الثاني أن يعتبر الإخوة والأخوات لأب مع الإخوة والأخوات لأب وأم في مقاسمه الجد حتى يظهر نصيب الجد إذا ظهر نصيبه وأعطى نصيبه رد أولاد الأب ما أخذوا على أولاد الأب والأم، وإن كانوا ذكوراً ومختلطين وخرجوا بغير شيء فقد اعتبرهم في الابتداء وأخرجهم في الانتهاء بيانه : جد وأخ لأب وأم وأخ لأب وإن كان مع الجد أخت لأب وأم وإخوة وأخوات لأب يقسم كما قلنا ثم يرد الاخوة والأخوات لأب على الأخوات لأب وأم إلى تمام النصف، وعلى الأختين لأب وأم إلى تمام الثلثين، ثم إن فضل شيء يكون له وإلا فلا. وفي الذخيرة: فصل في مسائل يقوم الجد مقام الأب في حجب الأخوات لأب وأم أو لأب عند أبي حنيفة وهو قول أبي بكر الصديق وعبد الله بن عباس وأبي موسى الأشعري وطلحة وعليه الفتوى. وقال زيد : يقاسم الجد الإخوة والأخوات ما دامت المقاسمة خيراً له بأن كان لا ينقص نصيبه من الثلث وكأن يجعل الجد كأخ آخر وكأن يجعل نصيبه كنصيب الأخ، إن انتقص نصيبه من الثلث يعطيه ثلث المال وهو قول أبي يوسف ومحمد.

وفي المضمرات نفس المقاسمة أن يجعل الجد في المقاسمة كأحد الإخوة وبيانه في المسائل إذا ترك الرجل أختاً لأب وأم أو لأب وجداً فعلى قول أبي حنيفة المال كله للجد، وعلى قولهما المال بينهما على ثلاثة أسهم ؛ سهمان للجد وسهم للأخت ويجعل الجد في هذه الصورة كأخ آخر لأن المقاسمة خير له فإذا جعلناه كأخ آخر نصيبه سهمان من ثلاثة فيجعل كذلك، وإن ترك ثلاث إخوة لأب وأم أو لأب وجداً أخماساً يقسم المال له سهمان من ثلاثة وإن ترك ثلاث إخوة لأب وأم أو لأب وجداً فللجد الثلث ويجعل الجد كأخ فيقسم المال بينهم أخماساً سهمان للأخ وسهم للأخت ويجعل الجد كأخ ستة آخر لأن المقاسمة خير له لأنا لو أعطيناه الثلث في هذه الحالة أعطيناه سهمين من وسهمان من خمسة خير له من سهمين من ستة. ولو ترك جداً وأخوين لأب وأم وأختاً لأب وأم فهنا يعطي الجد ثلث المال لأن الثلث خير له لأن بالمقاسمة يحصل له سهمان من سبعة، فإذا جعلنا الجد كأخ آخر كان خيراً له. وإن ترك جداً وأخاً لأب وأم أو لأب وأختين لأب في هذه الصورة لا فرق بين المقاسمة وبين الثلث عندهما لأن بالمقاسمة يصير كأنه مات عن ثلاثة إخوة لأب وأم لأنا جعلنا الأختين أخاً وإذا كان كذلك يقسم أثلاثاً فيكون للجذ الثلث سهم من ثلاثة ولو أعطيناه الثلث ابتداء كان على الحساب ثلاثة للجد سهم من ثلاثة فهو معنى قولنا أنه لا فرق بين المقاسمة والفتوى في هذ المسائل وما يتصل بها على قول أبي حنيفة وفي الكافي : ولو ترك جداً وأخوين فالثلث ههنا والمقاسمة سواء، ولو ترك جداً وثلاثة أخوة فالثلث هنا خير من المقاسمة، ودليله في شرح الطحاوي ولو مات وترك جداً وأخاً لأب وأم وأخاً لأب فإن الأخ من الأب لا يرث مع الأخ لأب وأم وجد فإن الأخ لأب يدخل مع الجد لأنه وارث
Book of Inheritance: Regarding a male ancestor who has no female in his lineage to the deceased - that is the true grandfather, except in two matters: one is in returning the mother's share from one-third of the whole to one-third of what remains, and the exclusion of the mother of the father in the case of a husband and parents or a wife and parents; for the father sends her back to it like the grandfather. And in excluding the mother of the father, the father excludes her while the grandfather does not. If there is a female intervening in his lineage to the deceased, the lineage is corrupt, so he does not inherit except as one of the uterine relatives, because the female intervening in the lineage cuts it off, and lineage is to the fathers because lineage is for identity and fame, and that is by the well-known, which is males, not females. His saying 'like the father' means in the absence of the father, because the grandfather is called a father. Allah Almighty said, quoting Yusuf (peace be upon him): 'I followed the religion of my fathers: Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob' (Yusuf 38). Isaac was his grandfather and Abraham was his great-grandfather. And Allah Almighty said: 'O children of Adam, let not Satan tempt you as he expelled your parents from Paradise' (Al-A'raf 27). They were Adam and Eve (peace be upon them). So if he is a father, he enters the text either by way of general metaphor or by consensus, similar to what we mentioned about the son's son. So he has the three states we mentioned for the father, and he has a fourth state: being excluded by the father, because the father is closer and he derives from him, so he does not inherit with him; he only takes his place in his absence. His saying 'and he excludes the siblings' means that the grandfather excludes the siblings like the father, because he takes his place. This, in its absoluteness, is the saying of Abu Hanifa, as will be explained if Allah wills. The correct view is that the grandfather is of two types: true and false. The false is among the uterine relatives, and the true has three states as we mentioned for the father, and his ruling in the absence of the father regarding entitlement to the share and 'asabah is the same as the father's ruling, and the ruling of one is one-sixth, and if there are many, the one-sixth is shared equally among them. The distinction between the true and false grandfather is that the true is one in whose lineage to the deceased no female has intervened. If a female has intervened in his lineage to the deceased, he is false, and the true grandfather is like the father. Our scholars differed regarding fatwa in the matters of the grandfather. Some of them refrained from giving fatwa altogether due to the great difference that occurred among the Companions. Others gave fatwa, but they differed among themselves. The Shaykh Imam al-Sarakhsi gave fatwa in the matters of the grandfather according to the saying of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Some of our later scholars chose fatwa with sulh (compromise) in the points of disagreement. They said: we used to give fatwa with sulh for the hired worker in the points of common disagreement due to the difference of the Companions, and the difference of the Companions here is more apparent, so fatwa with sulh here is more deserving. The Shaykh Imam Shams al-Din al-Halwani said: Our scholars said that the correct approach in the matters of the grandfather is to give the grandfather what they agree upon, then divide between the grandfather and the siblings half and half; they ordered sulh. The Qadi Imam 'Imad al-Din al-Nasafi said: It is not proper for the mufti to say 'all the wealth is for the grandfather' following al-Siddiq; Abu Hanifa only said that to honor al-Siddiq. As for the principles of Zaid (may Allah be pleased with him), the first principle is that the siblings are like one of them; he shares with them and they share with him, and he competes with them and they compete with him as long as the sharing is better for him than one-third of the entire wealth, like a grandfather and a brother, as he is not decreased from the one-third. If one-third is better than sharing, like a grandfather and three brothers, he is given one-third and the rest is divided among them according to the ordinances of Allah. The second principle is that paternal brothers and sisters are considered together with full brothers and sisters in the grandfather's sharing, so that the grandfather's share becomes apparent. When his share appears and is given, the paternal children return what they took to the full children. If they were males and mixed and came out with nothing, they were considered initially and excluded finally. Its explanation: a grandfather, a full brother, and a paternal brother. If with the grandfather there is a full sister and paternal brothers and sisters, we divide as we said, then the paternal siblings return to the full sisters up to half, and to the two full sisters up to two-thirds. Then if there is anything left, it is for him; otherwise not. In al-Dhakhira: A chapter on matters where the grandfather takes the place of the father in excluding full or paternal sisters according to Abu Hanifa, which is the saying of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, Abdullah ibn Abbas, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and Talha, and upon that is the fatwa. Zaid said: The grandfather shares with the siblings as long as sharing is better for him, i.e., his share is not decreased from one-third. It is as if the grandfather is made like another brother and his share is made like the brother's share. If his share decreases from one-third, he is given one-third of the wealth. That is the saying of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. In al-Mudmarat: The sharing itself is that the grandfather is made in the sharing like one of the siblings. Its clarification is in the cases: If a man leaves a full or paternal sister and a grandfather, then according to Abu Hanifa the entire wealth is for the grandfather. According to the two, the wealth is between them in three shares: two shares for the grandfather and one for the sister. In this case the grandfather is made like another brother because sharing is better for him. If we make him like another brother, his share is two out of three, so he is made so. If he leaves three full or paternal brothers and a grandfather, then the grandfather is given one-third, and the wealth is divided among them in fifths: two shares for the brother and one for the sister, and the grandfather is made like another brother because sharing is better for him. If we gave him one-third in this case, we would give him two shares out of six? Two shares out of five are better for him than two out of six. If he leaves a grandfather, two full brothers, and a full sister, here the grandfather is given one-third of the wealth because one-third is better for him, because by sharing he would get two shares out of seven. So if we make the grandfather like another brother, it would be better for him. If he leaves a grandfather, a full or paternal brother, and two paternal sisters, in this case there is no difference between sharing and one-third according to the two, because by sharing it is as if he died leaving three full brothers, as we made the two sisters as a brother. If that is so, it is divided into thirds, so the grandfather gets one-third, one share out of three. If we gave him one-third initially, it would be one share out of three. That is the meaning of our saying that there is no difference between sharing and the fatwa in these matters and what is connected to them according to Abu Hanifa. In al-Kafi: If he leaves a grandfather and two brothers, here one-third and sharing are equal. If he leaves a grandfather and three brothers, one-third here is better than sharing. Its proof is in Sharh al-Tahawi. If he dies leaving a grandfather, a full brother, and a paternal brother, the paternal brother does not inherit with the full brother and grandfather, because the paternal brother enters with the grandfather as he is an heir.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, deals with the inheritance of the grandfather (al-jadd). It opens by defining the true grandfather (al-jadd al-sahih) as a male ancestor who has no female in his lineage to the deceased, contrasting with the false grandfather (al-jadd al-fasid) who has a female intervening and thus inherits only as a uterine relative. The true grandfather is treated like the father in most respects, inheriting by fard (sixth) and 'asabah (residuary) in the absence of the father, and even excluding siblings like the father would. However, the author notes two exceptions where the grandfather differs from the father: (1) in the case of returning the mother's share from a third of the whole to a third of the remainder (al- radd), and (2) in excluding the mother of the father (the grandmother on the father's side). The text then clarifies that the grandfather can be excluded by the father due to proximity. The core of the passage is the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the grandfather's treatment when siblings are present. Abu Hanifa, following the position of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, holds that the grandfather excludes all siblings (full and paternal), taking the entire estate or giving them nothing. In contrast, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) follow the view of Zaid ibn Thabit, which allows for muqasamah (sharing) between the grandfather and siblings when it is more beneficial for the grandfather than taking a fixed one-third. They present a detailed method: the grandfather is treated as one of the siblings, shares with them, but never receives less than one-third of the estate. If sharing gives him less than one-third, he takes one-third instead. The text also discusses the second principle concerning siblings from different parents (full vs. paternal) and how they affect the calculation. Later Hanafi scholars differed on which opinion to give fatwa (ruling) on; some advocated for compromise (sulh) due to the complexity and disagreement. The passage provides numerous case examples to illustrate the difference between the two positions, such as the scenario of a grandfather with a sister, or with three brothers, etc. These examples clarify that the choice between taking one-third or sharing depends on which yields a larger share for the grandfather.

Key Terms
الجد الصحيح (al-jadd al-sahih): The true grandfather: a male ascendant with no female intervening in the lineage to the deceased.
الجد الفاسد (al-jadd al-fasid): The false grandfather: a male ascendant with a female intervening in the lineage; inherits only as a uterine relative.
الرد (al-radd): The return of surplus shares to the rightful heirs; in this context, the return of the mother's share from one-third of the whole to one-third of the remainder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What distinguishes a true grandfather from a false grandfather?
A) The true grandfather is the maternal grandfather, the false is paternal
B) The true grandfather has no female in his lineage to the deceased; the false grandfather does
C) The true grandfather is always alive, the false is dead
D) The true grandfather is from the father's side, the false from the mother's side

Key Takeaway
The true grandfather inherits like the father in the father's absence, except in two specific cases involving the mother's return and exclusion of the paternal grandmother.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
12 min
The Grandfather and Siblings: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Presents the intra-Hanafi dispute on the grandfather's inheritance with siblings, including detailed examples and later fatwa preferences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa's and the two disciples' views on the grandfather's inheritance with siblings, and apply muqasamah to calculate shares in simple cases.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa gives the grandfather all; the two disciples share with siblings via muqasamah—with a one-third floor.

The inheritance of the grandfather when siblings are present is one of the most contested issues in Hanafi fiqh. While Abu Hanifa, following Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, held that the grandfather excludes all siblings, his two principal disciples—Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani—adopted the view of Zaid ibn Thabit, allowing the grandfather to share with siblings through a method called muqasamah. This lesson unpacks the disagreement, the principles behind muqasamah, and how later scholars navigated the ikhtilaf, even recommending compromise (sulh) in some cases.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's position
According to Abu Hanifa, the grandfather excludes all siblings (full and paternal) from inheritance, just as the father would. The entire estate goes to the grandfather except when there are other fard heirs.
This view is attributed to Abu Bakr al-Siddiq and several other Companions.
2
State the two disciples' position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the grandfather does not exclude siblings. Instead, he shares with them using muqasamah, treating the grandfather as one of the brothers. However, the grandfather must never receive less than one-third of the estate.
This view is based on the practice of Zaid ibn Thabit.
3
Understand muqasamah – the sharing method
In muqasamah, the grandfather is treated as an additional sibling. The estate is divided equally among the grandfather and the siblings, with males receiving twice the share of females. This is done only if it gives the grandfather more than one-third; otherwise he takes one-third.
The text gives the example: grandfather and full sister → treat as two brothers, so 2 shares for grandfather, 1 for sister.
4
Apply the one-third floor rule
If muqasamah results in the grandfather receiving less than one-third, he is given one-third instead, and the remaining two-thirds are divided among the siblings. For example, with three brothers, muqasamah would give the grandfather 1/4, which is less than 1/3, so he takes 1/3.
The text provides multiple examples to illustrate when muqasamah is chosen over the one-third floor.
5
Review the second principle: mixing full and paternal siblings
When both full and paternal siblings exist, the paternal siblings are initially considered in the muqasamah to calculate the grandfather's share, but then they must return any shares they received to the full siblings to ensure full siblings get their proper fard shares. This can result in paternal siblings receiving nothing in the end.
This principle shows the complexity of the grandfather cases.
6
Note the later fatwa preferences
The text records that some scholars refrained from fatwa entirely due to the difficulty, while others like al-Sarakhsi gave fatwa according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Some recommended sulh (compromise) where the parties agree to split the difference. The commentator al-Nasafi warns muftis not to simply say 'all wealth is for the grandfather' following Abu Hanifa, as Abu Hanifa's ruling was meant to honor al-Siddiq, not as a binding fatwa.
This shows the evolution of the mufta bihi position.

Source Text

كتاب الفرائض
في نسبه إلى الميت أنثى وهو الجد الصحيح إلا في مسألتين: أحدهما في رد أم الميت من ثلث الجميع إلى ثلث ما بقي وحجب أم الأب في زوج وأبوين أو زوجة وأبوين فإن الأب يردها إليه كالجد وفي حجب أم الأب فإن الأب يحجبها دون الجد، وإن تخلل في نسبه إلى الميت أم النسب كان فاسداً فلا يرث إلا على أنه من ذوي الأرحام لأن تخلل الأم في النسبة يقطع والنسب إلى الآباء لأن النسب للتعريف والشهرة وذلك تكون بالمشهورة وهو الذكور دون الإناث. وقوله كالأب يعني عند عدم الأب لأن الجد يسمى أباً قال الله تعالى حاكياً عن يوسف عليه الصلاة والسلام واتبعت ملة آبائي ابراهيم واسحاق ويعقوب [يوسف: ٣٨] وكان اسحاق جده وإبراهيم جد أبيه. وقال الله تعالى با بني آدم لا يفتننكم الشيطان كما أخرج أبويكم من الجنة [الأعراف: ۲۷] وهما آدم وحواء عليهما السلام فإذا كان أباً دخل في النص إما بطريق عموم المجاز أو بالإجماع على ما نحو ما ذكرنا في ابن الابن فكان له الأحوال الثلاثة التي ذكرناها في الأب وله حالة رابعة وهو السقوط بالأب لأنه أقرب منه ويدلي به فلا يرث معه وإنما يقوم مقامه عند عدمه. وقوله ويحجب الإخوة يعني الجد يحجب الإخوة كالأب لأنه قائم مقامه، وهذا على إطلاقه قول أبي حنيفة على ما يجيء بيانه إن شاء الله تعالى والأصح أن الجد نوعان: صحيح وفاسد. فالفاسد من جملة ذوي الأرحام والصحيح له أحوال ثلاثة على ما نحو ما ذكرنا في الأب وحكمه حال عدم الأب في استحقاقه السهم والتعصيب حكم الأب وحكم الواحد السدس، وإذا كثر فالسدس بينهم بالسوية. الفاصل بين الجد الصحيح والفاسد أن الصحيح هو الذي لم يتخلل في نسبته إلى الميت أم، وإن تخلل في نسبه إلى الميت أم فهو فاسد والجد الصحيح كالأب. واختلف مشايخنا في الفتوى في مسائل الجد فامتنع بعضهم من الفتوى أصلاً لكثرة الاختلاف الواقع فيما بين الصحابة، وأفتى بها الآخرون لكن اختلفوا فيما بينهم كان الشيخ الإمام السرخسي يفتي في مسائل الجد بقول أبي يوسف ومحمد، وبعض المتأخرين من مشايخنا اختار والفتوى بالصلح في مواضع الخلاف قالوا كنا نفتي بالصلح في الأجير في مواضع الخلاف المشترك لاختلاف الصحابة واختلاف الصحابة هنا أظهر فكان الفتوى بالصلح هنا أحق. وقال الشيخ الإمام شمس الدين الحلواني : قال مشايخنا بأن الصواب في مسائل الجد أن يعطي الجد ما اتفقوا عليه ثم يقسم بين الجد وبين الإخوة والأخوات نصفين أمروا بالصلح. قال القاضي الإمام عماد الدين النسفي : لا ينبغي للمفتي أن يقول المال كله للجد عند الصديق وإنما قال أبو حنيفة بذلك تعظيماً لأمر الصديق وأما أصول زيد رضي الله عنه فالأصل الأول أن الإخوة والأخوات كأحدهم يقاسمهم ويقاسمونه ويزاحمهم ويزاحمونه ما دامت المقاسمة خيراً له من ثلث جميع المال كجد وأخ إذ لا ينقص من الثلث، فإن كان الثلث خيراً من المقاسمة كجد وثلاثة إخوة يعطي الثلث ويقسم الباقي بينهم على فرائض الله تعالى.

يجعل الجد له الأصل الثاني أن يعتبر الإخوة والأخوات لأب مع الإخوة والأخوات لأب وأم في مقاسمه الجد حتى يظهر نصيب الجد إذا ظهر نصيبه وأعطى نصيبه رد أولاد الأب ما أخذوا على أولاد الأب والأم، وإن كانوا ذكوراً ومختلطين وخرجوا بغير شيء فقد اعتبرهم في الابتداء وأخرجهم في الانتهاء بيانه : جد وأخ لأب وأم وأخ لأب وإن كان مع الجد أخت لأب وأم وإخوة وأخوات لأب يقسم كما قلنا ثم يرد الاخوة والأخوات لأب على الأخوات لأب وأم إلى تمام النصف، وعلى الأختين لأب وأم إلى تمام الثلثين، ثم إن فضل شيء يكون له وإلا فلا. وفي الذخيرة: فصل في مسائل يقوم الجد مقام الأب في حجب الأخوات لأب وأم أو لأب عند أبي حنيفة وهو قول أبي بكر الصديق وعبد الله بن عباس وأبي موسى الأشعري وطلحة وعليه الفتوى. وقال زيد : يقاسم الجد الإخوة والأخوات ما دامت المقاسمة خيراً له بأن كان لا ينقص نصيبه من الثلث وكأن يجعل الجد كأخ آخر وكأن يجعل نصيبه كنصيب الأخ، إن انتقص نصيبه من الثلث يعطيه ثلث المال وهو قول أبي يوسف ومحمد.

وفي المضمرات نفس المقاسمة أن يجعل الجد في المقاسمة كأحد الإخوة وبيانه في المسائل إذا ترك الرجل أختاً لأب وأم أو لأب وجداً فعلى قول أبي حنيفة المال كله للجد، وعلى قولهما المال بينهما على ثلاثة أسهم ؛ سهمان للجد وسهم للأخت ويجعل الجد في هذه الصورة كأخ آخر لأن المقاسمة خير له فإذا جعلناه كأخ آخر نصيبه سهمان من ثلاثة فيجعل كذلك، وإن ترك ثلاث إخوة لأب وأم أو لأب وجداً أخماساً يقسم المال له سهمان من ثلاثة وإن ترك ثلاث إخوة لأب وأم أو لأب وجداً فللجد الثلث ويجعل الجد كأخ فيقسم المال بينهم أخماساً سهمان للأخ وسهم للأخت ويجعل الجد كأخ ستة آخر لأن المقاسمة خير له لأنا لو أعطيناه الثلث في هذه الحالة أعطيناه سهمين من وسهمان من خمسة خير له من سهمين من ستة. ولو ترك جداً وأخوين لأب وأم وأختاً لأب وأم فهنا يعطي الجد ثلث المال لأن الثلث خير له لأن بالمقاسمة يحصل له سهمان من سبعة، فإذا جعلنا الجد كأخ آخر كان خيراً له. وإن ترك جداً وأخاً لأب وأم أو لأب وأختين لأب في هذه الصورة لا فرق بين المقاسمة وبين الثلث عندهما لأن بالمقاسمة يصير كأنه مات عن ثلاثة إخوة لأب وأم لأنا جعلنا الأختين أخاً وإذا كان كذلك يقسم أثلاثاً فيكون للجذ الثلث سهم من ثلاثة ولو أعطيناه الثلث ابتداء كان على الحساب ثلاثة للجد سهم من ثلاثة فهو معنى قولنا أنه لا فرق بين المقاسمة والفتوى في هذ المسائل وما يتصل بها على قول أبي حنيفة وفي الكافي : ولو ترك جداً وأخوين فالثلث ههنا والمقاسمة سواء، ولو ترك جداً وثلاثة أخوة فالثلث هنا خير من المقاسمة، ودليله في شرح الطحاوي ولو مات وترك جداً وأخاً لأب وأم وأخاً لأب فإن الأخ من الأب لا يرث مع الأخ لأب وأم وجد فإن الأخ لأب يدخل مع الجد لأنه وارث
Book of Inheritance: Regarding a male ancestor who has no female in his lineage to the deceased - that is the true grandfather, except in two matters: one is in returning the mother's share from one-third of the whole to one-third of what remains, and the exclusion of the mother of the father in the case of a husband and parents or a wife and parents; for the father sends her back to it like the grandfather. And in excluding the mother of the father, the father excludes her while the grandfather does not. If there is a female intervening in his lineage to the deceased, the lineage is corrupt, so he does not inherit except as one of the uterine relatives, because the female intervening in the lineage cuts it off, and lineage is to the fathers because lineage is for identity and fame, and that is by the well-known, which is males, not females. His saying 'like the father' means in the absence of the father, because the grandfather is called a father. Allah Almighty said, quoting Yusuf (peace be upon him): 'I followed the religion of my fathers: Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob' (Yusuf 38). Isaac was his grandfather and Abraham was his great-grandfather. And Allah Almighty said: 'O children of Adam, let not Satan tempt you as he expelled your parents from Paradise' (Al-A'raf 27). They were Adam and Eve (peace be upon them). So if he is a father, he enters the text either by way of general metaphor or by consensus, similar to what we mentioned about the son's son. So he has the three states we mentioned for the father, and he has a fourth state: being excluded by the father, because the father is closer and he derives from him, so he does not inherit with him; he only takes his place in his absence. His saying 'and he excludes the siblings' means that the grandfather excludes the siblings like the father, because he takes his place. This, in its absoluteness, is the saying of Abu Hanifa, as will be explained if Allah wills. The correct view is that the grandfather is of two types: true and false. The false is among the uterine relatives, and the true has three states as we mentioned for the father, and his ruling in the absence of the father regarding entitlement to the share and 'asabah is the same as the father's ruling, and the ruling of one is one-sixth, and if there are many, the one-sixth is shared equally among them. The distinction between the true and false grandfather is that the true is one in whose lineage to the deceased no female has intervened. If a female has intervened in his lineage to the deceased, he is false, and the true grandfather is like the father. Our scholars differed regarding fatwa in the matters of the grandfather. Some of them refrained from giving fatwa altogether due to the great difference that occurred among the Companions. Others gave fatwa, but they differed among themselves. The Shaykh Imam al-Sarakhsi gave fatwa in the matters of the grandfather according to the saying of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Some of our later scholars chose fatwa with sulh (compromise) in the points of disagreement. They said: we used to give fatwa with sulh for the hired worker in the points of common disagreement due to the difference of the Companions, and the difference of the Companions here is more apparent, so fatwa with sulh here is more deserving. The Shaykh Imam Shams al-Din al-Halwani said: Our scholars said that the correct approach in the matters of the grandfather is to give the grandfather what they agree upon, then divide between the grandfather and the siblings half and half; they ordered sulh. The Qadi Imam 'Imad al-Din al-Nasafi said: It is not proper for the mufti to say 'all the wealth is for the grandfather' following al-Siddiq; Abu Hanifa only said that to honor al-Siddiq. As for the principles of Zaid (may Allah be pleased with him), the first principle is that the siblings are like one of them; he shares with them and they share with him, and he competes with them and they compete with him as long as the sharing is better for him than one-third of the entire wealth, like a grandfather and a brother, as he is not decreased from the one-third. If one-third is better than sharing, like a grandfather and three brothers, he is given one-third and the rest is divided among them according to the ordinances of Allah. The second principle is that paternal brothers and sisters are considered together with full brothers and sisters in the grandfather's sharing, so that the grandfather's share becomes apparent. When his share appears and is given, the paternal children return what they took to the full children. If they were males and mixed and came out with nothing, they were considered initially and excluded finally. Its explanation: a grandfather, a full brother, and a paternal brother. If with the grandfather there is a full sister and paternal brothers and sisters, we divide as we said, then the paternal siblings return to the full sisters up to half, and to the two full sisters up to two-thirds. Then if there is anything left, it is for him; otherwise not. In al-Dhakhira: A chapter on matters where the grandfather takes the place of the father in excluding full or paternal sisters according to Abu Hanifa, which is the saying of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, Abdullah ibn Abbas, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and Talha, and upon that is the fatwa. Zaid said: The grandfather shares with the siblings as long as sharing is better for him, i.e., his share is not decreased from one-third. It is as if the grandfather is made like another brother and his share is made like the brother's share. If his share decreases from one-third, he is given one-third of the wealth. That is the saying of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. In al-Mudmarat: The sharing itself is that the grandfather is made in the sharing like one of the siblings. Its clarification is in the cases: If a man leaves a full or paternal sister and a grandfather, then according to Abu Hanifa the entire wealth is for the grandfather. According to the two, the wealth is between them in three shares: two shares for the grandfather and one for the sister. In this case the grandfather is made like another brother because sharing is better for him. If we make him like another brother, his share is two out of three, so he is made so. If he leaves three full or paternal brothers and a grandfather, then the grandfather is given one-third, and the wealth is divided among them in fifths: two shares for the brother and one for the sister, and the grandfather is made like another brother because sharing is better for him. If we gave him one-third in this case, we would give him two shares out of six? Two shares out of five are better for him than two out of six. If he leaves a grandfather, two full brothers, and a full sister, here the grandfather is given one-third of the wealth because one-third is better for him, because by sharing he would get two shares out of seven. So if we make the grandfather like another brother, it would be better for him. If he leaves a grandfather, a full or paternal brother, and two paternal sisters, in this case there is no difference between sharing and one-third according to the two, because by sharing it is as if he died leaving three full brothers, as we made the two sisters as a brother. If that is so, it is divided into thirds, so the grandfather gets one-third, one share out of three. If we gave him one-third initially, it would be one share out of three. That is the meaning of our saying that there is no difference between sharing and the fatwa in these matters and what is connected to them according to Abu Hanifa. In al-Kafi: If he leaves a grandfather and two brothers, here one-third and sharing are equal. If he leaves a grandfather and three brothers, one-third here is better than sharing. Its proof is in Sharh al-Tahawi. If he dies leaving a grandfather, a full brother, and a paternal brother, the paternal brother does not inherit with the full brother and grandfather, because the paternal brother enters with the grandfather as he is an heir.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, deals with the inheritance of the grandfather (al-jadd). It opens by defining the true grandfather (al-jadd al-sahih) as a male ancestor who has no female in his lineage to the deceased, contrasting with the false grandfather (al-jadd al-fasid) who has a female intervening and thus inherits only as a uterine relative. The true grandfather is treated like the father in most respects, inheriting by fard (sixth) and 'asabah (residuary) in the absence of the father, and even excluding siblings like the father would. However, the author notes two exceptions where the grandfather differs from the father: (1) in the case of returning the mother's share from a third of the whole to a third of the remainder (al- radd), and (2) in excluding the mother of the father (the grandmother on the father's side). The text then clarifies that the grandfather can be excluded by the father due to proximity. The core of the passage is the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the grandfather's treatment when siblings are present. Abu Hanifa, following the position of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, holds that the grandfather excludes all siblings (full and paternal), taking the entire estate or giving them nothing. In contrast, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) follow the view of Zaid ibn Thabit, which allows for muqasamah (sharing) between the grandfather and siblings when it is more beneficial for the grandfather than taking a fixed one-third. They present a detailed method: the grandfather is treated as one of the siblings, shares with them, but never receives less than one-third of the estate. If sharing gives him less than one-third, he takes one-third instead. The text also discusses the second principle concerning siblings from different parents (full vs. paternal) and how they affect the calculation. Later Hanafi scholars differed on which opinion to give fatwa (ruling) on; some advocated for compromise (sulh) due to the complexity and disagreement. The passage provides numerous case examples to illustrate the difference between the two positions, such as the scenario of a grandfather with a sister, or with three brothers, etc. These examples clarify that the choice between taking one-third or sharing depends on which yields a larger share for the grandfather.

Key Terms
الجد الصحيح (al-jadd al-sahih): The true grandfather: a male ascendant with no female in lineage.
المقاسمة (al-muqasamah): The method of sharing the estate between the grandfather and the siblings, treating the grandfather as one of the brothers.
الصلح (al-sulh): Compromise recommended by some Hanafi scholars in disputed grandfather cases, where the parties agree on a distribution.
أصول زيد (usul Zaid): The two principles attributed to Zaid ibn Thabit: (1) muqasamah with one-third floor, (2) considering paternal siblings with full siblings then returning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two disciples, what is the grandfather's share when he leaves a grandfather and three full brothers?
A) The entire estate
B) One-quarter
C) One-third
D) Three-fifths

Key Takeaway
The grandfather does not always exclude siblings; according to the mufta bihi, he shares with them via muqasamah, but never gets less than one-third.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
8 min
The Grandfather and Siblings: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on grandfather's inheritance with siblings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on grandfather's inheritance with siblings and apply the Sahibayn's rule of muqasamah with a minimum one-third share.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa’s grandfather excludes siblings; the Sahibayn make him share but never less than a third.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents the classic intra-Hanafi dispute on the grandfather's share when siblings survive. Abu Hanifa treats the grandfather like a father, excluding all siblings, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani follow the approach of Zayd ibn Thabit, allowing the grandfather to share with siblings as long as he receives at least one-third of the estate. The text works through several examples to illustrate the difference and concludes that the fatwa is on Abu Hanifa's view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
State clearly what Abu Hanifa holds (grandfather excludes all siblings) and what the Sahibayn hold (grandfather shares with siblings, but not less than one-third).
The Sahibayn's view is also associated with Zayd ibn Thabit.
2
Understand muqasamah
Define muqasamah: the grandfather is treated as one of the siblings, receiving an equal share. Compare this to the fixed one-third.
Muqasamah only applies if it gives the grandfather more than one-third.
3
Apply the Sahibayn's rule to a case
Take the example of grandfather + one sister. Under muqasamah, the estate is divided into three: two for the grandfather, one for the sister. Check if muqasamah is better than one-third: grandfather gets 2/3 > 1/3, so muqasamah applies.
4
Identify when muqasamah and third are equal
In the case of grandfather + brother + two paternal sisters, the share is the same (1/3) under both methods. Recognize scenarios where the difference vanishes.
These cases are listed in al-Kafi.
5
Note the fatwa preference
The text states 'وعليه الفتوى' for Abu Hanifa's view, meaning it is the operative position for fatwa despite the Sahibayn's alternative.
The tarjih is based on the authority of Abu Bakr and other Companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الثاني أن يعتبر الإخوة والأخوات لأب مع الإخوة والأخوات لأب وأم في مقاسمه الجد حتى يظهر نصيب الجد إذا ظهر نصيبه وأعطى نصيبه رد أولاد الأب ما أخذوا على أولاد الأب والأم، وإن كانوا ذكوراً ومختلطين وخرجوا بغير شيء فقد اعتبرهم في الابتداء وأخرجهم في الانتهاء بيانه : جد وأخ لأب وأم وأخ لأب وإن كان مع الجد أخت لأب وأم وإخوة وأخوات لأب يقسم كما قلنا ثم يرد الاخوة والأخوات لأب على الأخوات لأب وأم إلى تمام النصف، وعلى الأختين لأب وأم إلى تمام الثلثين، ثم إن فضل شيء يكون له وإلا فلا. وفي الذخيرة: فصل في مسائل يقوم الجد مقام الأب في حجب الأخوات لأب وأم أو لأب عند أبي حنيفة وهو قول أبي بكر الصديق وعبد الله بن عباس وأبي موسى الأشعري وطلحة وعليه الفتوى. وقال زيد : يقاسم الجد الإخوة والأخوات ما دامت المقاسمة خيراً له بأن كان لا ينقص نصيبه من الثلث وكأن يجعل الجد كأخ آخر وكأن يجعل نصيبه كنصيب الأخ، إن انتقص نصيبه من الثلث يعطيه ثلث المال وهو قول أبي يوسف ومحمد. وفي المضمرات نفس المقاسمة أن يجعل الجد في المقاسمة كأحد الإخوة وبيانه في المسائل إذا ترك الرجل أختاً لأب وأم أو لأب وجداً فعلى قول أبي حنيفة المال كله للجد، وعلى قولهما المال بينهما على ثلاثة أسهم ؛ سهمان للجد وسهم للأخت ويجعل الجد في هذه الصورة كأخ آخر لأن المقاسمة خير له فإذا جعلناه كأخ آخر نصيبه سهمان من ثلاثة فيجعل كذلك، وإن ترك ثلاث إخوة لأب وأم أو لأب وجداً أخماساً يقسم المال له سهمان من ثلاثة وإن ترك ثلاث إخوة لأب وأم أو لأب وجداً فللجد الثلث ويجعل الجد كأخ فيقسم المال بينهم أخماساً سهمان للأخ وسهم للأخت ويجعل الجد كأخ ستة آخر لأن المقاسمة خير له لأنا لو أعطيناه الثلث في هذه الحالة أعطيناه سهمين من وسهمان من خمسة خير له من سهمين من ستة. ولو ترك جداً وأخوين لأب وأم وأختاً لأب وأم فهنا يعطي الجد ثلث المال لأن الثلث خير له لأن بالمقاسمة يحصل له سهمان من سبعة، فإذا جعلنا الجد كأخ آخر كان خيراً له. وإن ترك جداً وأخاً لأب وأم أو لأب وأختين لأب في هذه الصورة لا فرق بين المقاسمة وبين الثلث عندهما لأن بالمقاسمة يصير كأنه مات عن ثلاثة إخوة لأب وأم لأنا جعلنا الأختين أخاً وإذا كان كذلك يقسم أثلاثاً فيكون للجذ الثلث سهم من ثلاثة ولو أعطيناه الثلث ابتداء كان على الحساب ثلاثة للجد سهم من ثلاثة فهو معنى قولنا أنه لا فرق بين المقاسمة والفتوى في هذ المسائل وما يتصل بها على قول أبي حنيفة وفي الكافي : ولو ترك جداً وأخوين فالثلث ههنا والمقاسمة سواء، ولو ترك جداً وثلاثة أخوة فالثلث هنا خير من المقاسمة، ودليله في شرح الطحاوي ولو مات وترك جداً وأخاً لأب وأم وأخاً لأب فإن الأخ من الأب لا يرث مع الأخ لأب وأم وجد فإن الأخ لأب يدخل مع الجد لأنه وارث
The second principle: paternal siblings are included with full siblings in the grandfather's shared portion to determine his share. When his share appears and is given, paternal offspring return what they took to the full siblings. If they were males and mixed and came out with nothing, they were considered initially but excluded finally. Explanation: grandfather, full brother, paternal brother; if with grandfather there is a full sister and paternal brothers and sisters, divide as we said, then paternal siblings return to full sisters until half is complete, and to two full sisters until two-thirds is complete. Then if anything remains, it is for him, otherwise not. In al-Dhakhira: A section on issues where the grandfather takes the place of the father in excluding full or paternal sisters according to Abu Hanifa, which is the view of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, Ibn Abbas, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and Talha, and upon it is the fatwa. Zayd said: The grandfather shares with siblings as long as sharing is better for him such that his share does not fall below one-third, and it is as if the grandfather is made like another brother and his share like a brother's share. If his share falls below one-third, he is given one-third of the estate—this is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. In al-Mudmarat: The sharing itself is to make the grandfather in the sharing like one of the brothers. Its explanation in issues: If a man leaves a full or paternal sister and a grandfather, according to Abu Hanifa all wealth is for the grandfather; according to them the wealth is divided into three shares: two for the grandfather, one for the sister, making the grandfather in this case like another brother because sharing is better for him. If we make him like another brother, his share is two of three, so it is made so. If he leaves three full or paternal brothers and a grandfather, fifths? He divides the wealth: for him two of three? If he leaves three full or paternal brothers and a grandfather, the grandfather gets one-third, and the grandfather is made like a brother, so wealth is divided among them into fifths: two shares for the brother, one for the sister, and the grandfather is made like a sixth brother because sharing is better for him; for if we gave him the third in this case we would give him two shares, and two of five is better for him than two of six. If he leaves a grandfather, two full brothers, and a full sister, here the grandfather is given one-third of the wealth because the third is better for him; because with sharing he gets two of seven, so if we make the grandfather like another brother, it is better for him. If he leaves a grandfather, a full or paternal brother, and two paternal sisters, in this case there is no difference between sharing and the third according to them; because with sharing it becomes as if three full brothers died, since we made the two sisters a brother, and if so it is divided into thirds, so the grandfather gets one-third, one share of three. If we gave him the third initially, the calculation would be the same: three [shares]? for the grandfather one of three. So that is the meaning of our saying there is no difference between sharing and the fatwa in these issues and what relates to them according to Abu Hanifa. In al-Kafi: If he leaves a grandfather and two brothers, the third and sharing are equal; if he leaves a grandfather and three brothers, the third is better than sharing. Its proof is in Sharh al-Tahawi. If he dies leaving a grandfather, a full brother, and a paternal brother, the paternal brother does not inherit with the full brother and grandfather; but the paternal brother enters with the grandfather because he is an heir.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the inheritance of the grandfather when there are siblings. The text presents the second principle of grandfather's inheritance: the grandfather's share is calculated by including all siblings (full and consanguine) in the muqasamah (sharing) to determine his share; if siblings are excluded later, they are still considered initially. It gives examples. Then it cites al-Dhakhira that according to Abu Hanifa, the grandfather stands in place of the father in excluding sisters (full or consanguine), a view attributed to several Companions and relied upon for fatwa. The opposing view of Zayd (likely Zayd ibn Thabit) is that the grandfather shares with siblings as long as sharing is better for him; if sharing would reduce his share below one-third, he gets one-third. This is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn). The text then elaborates from al-Mudmarat: the method of sharing is to treat the grandfather as one of the brothers. Several specific cases are worked out: (1) grandfather with a sister: Abu Hanifa gives all to the grandfather; the Sahibayn divide into three shares (2 for grandfather, 1 for sister). (2) grandfather with three brothers: the Sahibayn give the grandfather one-third when sharing becomes worse. (3) grandfather with two brothers and a sister: the third is better. (4) grandfather with a brother and two sisters: sharing and third yield the same. The text concludes that in many cases there is no practical difference between the two views, as stated in al-Kafi. The passage uses rational reasoning (talil) based on comparing muqasamah and the fixed third to determine the better option for the grandfather, without explicit Quranic or Hadith proof here.

Key Terms
الجد (al-jadd): The paternal grandfather (father's father) as an heir.
المقاسمة (al-muqasamah): Sharing the estate proportionally between the grandfather and siblings as if the grandfather were one of the siblings.
حجب الحرمان (hajb al-hirman): Total exclusion from inheritance; Abu Hanifa applies this to sisters in the presence of the grandfather.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a grandfather and a full sister, what share does the sister receive according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad)?
A) Nothing, she is excluded.
B) One-half.
C) One-third.
D) One-quarter.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's view (grandfather excludes sisters) is the relied-upon fatwa, while the Sahibayn's muqasamah with a minimum one-third is a valid alternative within the school.

The Musharrakah (Himariyyah) Case – A Disputed Inheritance
Describes the Musharrakah case and the ikhtilaf between Abu Bakr and Umar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Musharrakah case and state the positions of Abu Bakr and Umar, and identify which madhhab follows each view.

Core Idea
Umar changed his ruling after a full sibling argued 'Suppose our father were a donkey' – a lasting ikhtilaf.

The passage introduces one of five famous inheritance problems known as al-Musharrakah (or Himariyyah). This case centers on whether full siblings should share with uterine siblings when the deceased leaves a husband, mother, and uterine siblings. The dispute between Abu Bakr (full siblings get nothing) and Umar's later view (full siblings share equally in the third) illustrates the dynamic nature of early ijtihad. This lesson unpacks the historical context and the madhhab positions that followed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their shares
List the heirs: husband (1/2), mother (1/6), uterine siblings (1/3), and a full brother (disputed). Determine the base shares according to Quranic rules.
The presence of uterine siblings triggers the one-third share under Quran 4:12.
2
State the position of Abu Bakr (Hanafi)
According to Abu Bakr, the full brother receives nothing; the one-third is exclusively for uterine siblings.
This is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.
3
State the position of Umar (adopted by Malik and Shafi'i)
Umar initially agreed with Abu Bakr, but later ruled that full siblings share equally with uterine siblings in the one-third.
This ruling was triggered by a powerful argument from a full sibling.
4
Analyze the proof for the opposing view
The full sibling argued: 'Suppose our father were a donkey? Are we not from one mother? A father only adds closeness.' Umar accepted this reasoning.
The proof is a rational argument based on maternal kinship, not a direct textual proof.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, full brother gets zero; under Maliki/Shafi'i, full brother gets a portion from the one-third.
This affects the distribution of the estate in real cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر في المضمرات أن المسائل المتعلقة بالاخوة خمسة أحدها الشركة وهي أن تترك المرأة زوجها وأماً وجداً أو إخوة من أم وأخاً من أب وأم فللزوج النصف وللأم السدس ولولد الأم الثلث ولا شيء للأخ الأب والأم وهذا قول أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه، ويشترك أولاد الأب والأم مع أولاد الأم في الثلث كأنهم أولاد أم واحد سواء فيه الذكر والأنثى، وهذا قول عمر أخذ مالك والشافعي، وكان عمر رضي الله عنه يقول أولاً كما يقول أبو بكر رضي الله عنه ثم رجع إلى قول غيره، وسبب رجوعه أنه سأل هذه المسألة عن فأجاب كما هو مذهبه فقام واحد من أولاد الأب فقال : يا أمير المؤمنين هب أن أبانا كان حماراً ألسنا من أم واحدة والأب لا يزيد إلا قرباً فأطرق عمر رأسه متأملاً ثم رفع رأسه فقال: صدقواهم سواء أم واحدة فنشركهم في الثلث فسميت المسألة مشتركة لتشريك عمر وحمارية لقول القائل . وأما المسألة المنبرية والثالثة الأكدرية والرابعة العثمانية وقد مرت. وأما الخامسة الخمرية وهي ثلاث أخوات متفرقات وثلاث جدات متحاذيات وجد أب الأب تحجب أم الأب بأب الأب وتحجب الأخت من الأم أيضاً والأخت من الأب تدخل في المقاسمة وتخرج بغير شيء على الخلاف وتخرج المسألة من اثني عشر بعد القطع وإنما سميت حمزية لأن حمزة بن حبيب فعلها.
It is mentioned in al-Mudmarat that the problems related to siblings are five. One of them is al-Shirkah (the partnership case), which is: a woman leaves her husband, mother, grandfather or uterine brothers, and a full brother. For the husband is half, for the mother one-sixth, for the children of the mother one-third, and nothing for the full brother. This is the saying of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq. The children of the father and mother share with the children of the mother in the third as if they are all children of one mother, male and female equal. This is the saying of Umar, adopted by Malik and al-Shafi'i. Umar initially said as Abu Bakr said, then retracted to the other saying. The reason for his retraction is that he asked this problem, and [someone] answered according to his own school, then one of the paternal children stood and said: 'O Commander of the Faithful, suppose our father were a donkey? Are we not from one mother? And a father only adds closeness.' Then Umar lowered his head thinking, then raised it and said: 'You have spoken the truth. They are equal, one mother. So we share them in the third.' So the case was called 'Musharrakah' due to Umar's sharing, and 'Himariyyah' due to the speaker's statement. As for the Minbariyyah case, the third Akdariyyah, and the fourth Uthmaniyyah, they have already passed. As for the fifth Khumriyyah: it is three diverse sisters, three conflicting grandmothers, and the grandfather's father. The mother's father excludes the mother's mother? and excludes also the uterine sister; the paternal sister enters in the sharing and comes out with nothing according to difference, and the case comes out from twelve after reduction. It is called 'Hamziyyah' because Hamzah ibn Habib performed it.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage enumerates five famous inheritance problems. It details two: the Musharrakah (also called Himariyyah) and the Khumriyyah. The Musharrakah is notable for the ikhtilaf between Abu Bakr and Umar: Abu Bakr gave the full brother nothing when the deceased left a husband, mother, uterine siblings, and a full brother; Umar initially agreed, but after a poignant argument from a full sibling, he changed his ruling to let full siblings share the one-third with uterine siblings. This became the view of Malik and al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi view is typically the view of Abu Bakr, as indicated earlier. The Khumriyyah (or Hamziyyah) involves complex interactions of diverse sisters and grandmothers; the exact details are brief but it is an exercise in faraid calculation.

Key Terms
المسألة المشتركة (al-mas'alah al-mushtarakah): The inheritance case where full siblings share the one-third with uterine siblings, named after Umar's ruling.
المسألة الخمرية (al-mas'alah al-khumriyyah): A complex faraid case involving three diverse sisters, three grandmothers, and a great-grandfather, solved by Hamzah ibn Habib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the Musharrakah also called Himariyyah?
A) Because a donkey was part of the inheritance.
B) Because a claimant said 'Suppose our father were a donkey'.
C) Because Umar was known as 'Himar'.
D) Because the case involved a donkey as property.

Key Takeaway
The Musharrakah case illustrates that early Companions differed on inheritance, and each school follows a respected authority.

The Khumriyyah (Hamziyyah) Problem – A Complex Faraid Puzzle
Describes the Khumriyyah inheritance problem and its naming.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the heirs involved in the Khumriyyah problem and explain why it is called Hamziyyah.

Core Idea
The Khumriyyah is a complex inheritance puzzle with diverse sisters and grandmothers, solved by Hamzah ibn Habib.

The passage briefly mentions the fifth famous inheritance problem: the Khumriyyah (also called Hamziyyah after its solver). This case involves three diverse sisters, three conflicting grandmothers, and a great-grandfather. The calculation is intricate and results in a base denominator of 12 after reduction. This lesson introduces the structure of the problem and its historical name.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties involved
List the three diverse sisters: a uterine sister, a full sister, and a consanguine sister. Also three grandmothers: mother's mother, father's mother, and mother of the grandfather? And a great-grandfather (father of grandfather).
The exact identities are debated; the term 'diverse' indicates different types.
2
Understand the blocking relationships
According to the passage, the great-grandfather blocks the father's mother? Actually it says 'تحجب أم الأب بأب الأب' – the father's mother is blocked by the great-grandfather? This seems reversed. In Hanafi faraid, a great-grandfather can block certain grandmothers. The specific blocking needs careful analysis.
The text is brief; full calculation would require more details.
3
Note the name 'Khumriyyah' and 'Hamziyyah'
It is called Khumriyyah (wine-like) perhaps for its intoxicating complexity, and Hamziyyah because Hamzah ibn Habib solved it.
The name 'Hamziyyah' is a variant reading.
4
Recognize the computational outcome
The case resolves to a base number of 12 after reduction (قطع). This means the shares combine to a denominator of 12 after adjustments.
This is an exercise in 'قط' (removing fractional inconsistencies).
