Hajb (Exclusion) in Inheritance: Types and Principles
Defines the two types of hajb and lists immune heirs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hajb al-hirman and hajb al-nuqsan, identify the six heirs never excluded, and state the two underlying principles.

Core Idea
Six heirs can never be totally excluded: spouses, parents, and children; others may be removed or reduced.

The science of inheritance (faraid) uses the concept of hajb to determine which heirs receive shares and which are blocked. This passage from al-Dhakhira categorizes hajb into two types and establishes key rules that govern exclusion, providing a foundational framework for calculating shares.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of hajb
Read the opening statement: hajb is of two types – hirman (total exclusion) and nuqsan (reduction). Understand that these are distinct mechanisms affecting different heirs.
2
Memorize the six heirs immune to hirman
The text explicitly lists six heirs who can never be totally excluded: husband, wife, father, mother, daughter, and son. Commit these to memory.
These six are protected regardless of other heirs present.
3
Memorize the heirs subject to nuqsan
The text first states that only three heirs (husband, wife, mother) are subject to reduction, then expands to five (adding grandmother, son's daughter, paternal sister). Note the discrepancy and recognize that the broader list is more comprehensive.
The 'reduction' shifts an heir from a higher share to a lower one.
4
Understand the two principles
The passage concludes with two principles: (1) one who inherits through another (e.g., a grandson via a son) is excluded if that intermediary exists, except children of the mother (uterine siblings); (2) the nearer in degree excludes the farther, as with asabah.
These principles determine who blocks whom.
5
Apply the principles to classify heirs
Given a set of heirs, use the two principles to decide which are totally excluded (hirman), which are reduced (nuqsan), and which are immune. This is the practical skill needed for calculation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الذخيرة فصل في الحجب: يجب أن يعلم بأن الحجب على نوعين: حجب حرمان وحجب نقصان فحجب الحرمان يرد على الكل إلا على ستة: الزوج والزوجة والأب والأم والبنت والابن وحجب النقصان لا يرد إلا على ثلاثة : الزوج والزوجة والأم والحجب على نوعين: حجب نقصان وهو حجب عن سهم إلى سهم وذلك لخمس نفر: الزوجين والأم والجدة وبنت الابن والأخت لأب. وحجب حرمان والورثة فيه فريقان فريق لا يحجبون بحال وهم ستة وهذا ينبني على أصلين: أحدهما أن كل من يدلي إلى الميت بشخص لا يرث مع وجود ذلك الشخص سوى أولاد الأم فإنهم يرثون معها لانعدام استحقاقها التركة، والثاني الأقرب فالأقرب كما في العصبات.
In al-Dhakhira: A chapter on hajb: It must be known that hajb is of two types: hajb hirman (exclusion) and hajb nuqsan (reduction). Hajb hirman applies to everyone except six: the husband, wife, father, mother, daughter, and son. Hajb nuqsan applies only to three: the husband, wife, and mother. And hajb is of two types: hajb nuqsan, which is exclusion from one share to another, and that applies to five persons: the two spouses, the mother, the grandmother, the son's daughter, and the paternal sister. And hajb hirman: the heirs are two groups: a group that is never excluded, and they are six. This is based on two principles: first, whoever connects to the deceased through a person does not inherit in the presence of that person, except children of the mother who inherit with her due to her lack of entitlement; second, the nearer in degree, as in the asabah.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage from al-Dhakhira categorizes hajb into two types: hirman (total exclusion) and nuqsan (reduction to a lower share). Six heirs are never totally excluded: the spouses, parents, and children (son and daughter). Three heirs can be reduced: husband (from 1/2 to 1/4), wife (from 1/4 to 1/8), and mother (from 1/3 to 1/6). The 'reduction' type applies to five specific heirs: spouses, mother, grandmother, son's daughter, and paternal sister—they may be moved from a higher share to a lower one. For hirman, two principles govern: (1) one who inherits through another is excluded if that intermediary exists, except uterine siblings; (2) the nearer relative excludes the farther, as in the case of agnatic heirs (asabah).

Key Terms
حجب الحرمان (hajb al-hirman): Total exclusion from inheritance; certain heirs are completely removed by the presence of a stronger heir.
حجب النقصان (hajb al-nuqsan): Reduction from a higher share to a lower share (e.g., husband from 1/2 to 1/4).
أصول الحجب (usul al-hajb): The two principles governing exclusion: (1) one who inherits through another is excluded by that person, except uterine children; (2) the nearer excludes the farther.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Son's daughter
B) Paternal sister
C) Mother
D) Father

Key Takeaway
Hajb is either total exclusion (hirman) or reduction (nuqsan); six heirs are permanently protected from total exclusion.

Mother's Share: One-Third or One-Sixth
States the Quranic ruling on the mother's inheritance share with conditional proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mother's share in inheritance based on the presence of children or siblings, and apply the conditional rule from Quran 4:11.

Core Idea
The mother's share drops from one-third to one-sixth when a child or two siblings survive.

In this brief passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq, we encounter one of the most frequently applied Quranic inheritance rules: the mother's share is conditional. The matn states the two scenarios clearly, and the sharh confirms them with direct Qur'anic evidence. Understanding this rule is foundational for all faraid calculations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the ruling being stated? The mother gets one-third of the estate in one scenario, one-sixth in another.
Focus on the two scenarios: one-third vs one-sixth.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 4:11 as the proof. Find the exact phrase: 'فإن كان له إخوة فلأمه السدس'.
Recognize that this is a clear Quranic text (qat'i al-thubut wa al-dalalah).
3
Distinguish the conditions
The one-third applies when there is no child (including son's child) and no two siblings. The one-sixth applies when there is a child or two siblings.
Note the conditional 'فإن' and the implied default from the full verse.
4
Clarify scope
The sharh notes that 'لا أولادهم' means siblings' children do NOT reduce the mother's share; only the siblings themselves two or more cause reduction.
Ensure you understand that grandchildren via a son count as 'child' but siblings' children do not.
5
Memorize the rule
This is a memorization anchor. Commit to memory: mother = 1/3 if no child and no 2 siblings; mother = 1/6 if child or 2+ siblings.
Practice with examples.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وللأم الثلث وذلك عند عدم الولد ولد الابن لما تلونا وعند عدم الاثنين من الإخوة والأخوات على ما نبين. قال رحمه الله: (ومع الولد وولد الابن أو الاثنين من الأخوة والأخوات لا أولادهم السدس) يعني مع واحد من هؤلاء المذكورين لا ترث الثلث وإنما ترث السدس لما تلونا ولقوله تعالى فإن كان له إخوة فلأمه السدس [النساء :
He said (may Allah have mercy on him): 'And for the mother is one-third, and that is in the absence of a child or a son's child, as we have recited, and in the absence of two siblings, as we will explain.' He said (may Allah have mercy on him): 'And with the child or son's child, or two siblings, not their children, one-sixth.' Meaning with any of these mentioned, she does not inherit one-third but rather one-sixth, as we have recited, and due to His saying: 'If he has siblings, then for his mother one-sixth' [Quran 4:11].
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is a matn (from Kanz al-Daqaiq) and its sharh by the commentator. The matn states the mother's share: she gets one-third when there is no child (or son's child) and no two siblings (brothers or sisters). If there is a child, a son's child, or two (or more) siblings, she gets one-sixth. The sharh confirms this and quotes the Quranic verse (4:11) as proof: 'فإن كان له إخوة فلأمه السدس' (if he has siblings, then for his mother one-sixth). The phrase 'لا أولادهم' clarifies that the siblings' children do not reduce the mother's share; only the siblings themselves (two or more) cause the reduction.

Key Terms
الولد (al-walad): Child (son or daughter) of the deceased, which reduces the mother's share.
الإخوة (al-ikhwah): Siblings (brothers and sisters) of the deceased; two or more reduce the mother's share to one-sixth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a mother inherit one-sixth instead of one-third?
A) When there is a child or a son's child, or two siblings.
B) When there is a grandmother present.
C) When the father is alive.
D) When there are no siblings.

Key Takeaway
The mother's share is conditional: one-third if no child or son's child and no two siblings; otherwise one-sixth.

The Grandfather's Share in Muqasamah with Siblings and the Mother's Reduction
Faraid ruling on muqasamah and mother's reduction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares when a grandfather, two full brothers, mother, and father are present, applying the Hanafi rule of muqasamah and the reduction of the mother's share.

Core Idea
The grandfather takes one-third by muqasamah with full brothers, and the mother is reduced from thuluth to sudus.

In Hanafi faraid, the grandfather (al-jadd) holds a special status: he can replace the father in some respects, but he does not exclude siblings as the father does. This passage clarifies how the shares are calculated when the grandfather inherits alongside full brothers and the mother, and how the mother's share is affected by the presence of siblings.

Guided Path
1
List the Surviving Heirs
Identify all heirs in the scenario: grandfather (father's father), two full brothers (from same father and mother), mother, and, if present, the father. The text focuses on the case where the father is presumed dead in one case and alive in another.
If the father is alive, he excludes the grandfather and the brothers.
2
Apply Hajb Hirman
Determine which heirs are wholly excluded. The father excludes the grandfather and all siblings. If the father is deceased, the grandfather is not excluded, and the brothers are not excluded by the grandfather.
The grandfather does not block the siblings; they all inherit together.
3
Assign Shares Under Muqasamah
When the grandfather and full brothers inherit together (and no father), they share the estate via muqasamah. The text states that the grandfather is given one-third and the two brothers share two-thirds equally.
Muqasamah means proportional sharing: here the grandfather's share is one-third, each brother one-third of the remainder.
4
Determine the Mother's Share
The mother's share depends on the presence of children or two or more siblings (including inheriting brothers). Since two full brothers are present, the mother takes one-sixth (sudus), not one-third (thuluth). This reduction applies even with the grandfather present.
The mother's share is fixed at one-sixth when there are two or more siblings, regardless of the grandfather.
5
Resolve Conflicting Shares Using Awl
When the mother's share (1/6), grandfather's share (1/3 = 2/6), and brothers' shares (2/3 = 4/6) are totaled, the sum is 7/6, exceeding the estate. Hanafi law applies awl (proportional reduction) by increasing the denominator to 7: mother gets 1/7, grandfather 2/7, each brother 2/7.
The text does not explicitly mention awl, but it is necessary to resolve the imbalance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومع كتاب الفرائض الولد وولد الابن أو الاثنين من الأخوة والأخوات لا أولادهم السدس ومع الأب في حق الجد وإن لم يكن وارثاً في حق الأخ لأب وأم فتكون المقاسمة والثلث سواء، فيعطي للجد الثلث والثلثان للأخوين لكل أخ ثلثه وهذا كما يقول في الأخوين مع الأب يرد الأم من الثلث إلى السدس ومع ذلك لا يرثان مع الأب.
And with the Book of Faraid: The child and the son's child or two siblings (brothers or sisters) not their children [take] the sixth, and with the father regarding the grandfather, even if he is not an heir, regarding the brother from the father and mother, then the division (muqasamah) and the third are equal. So the grandfather is given the third, and two-thirds to the two brothers, each brother a third. And this is as he says regarding the two brothers with the father: the mother is reduced from the third to the sixth, and despite that they do not inherit with the father.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage from the commentary explains the situation when the grandfather (al-jadd) is present alongside the father and siblings. The author clarifies that in the context of the grandfather, the muqasamah (proportional sharing) and the fixed third are considered equal. The grandfather receives one-third, and the two full brothers (from father and mother) receive two-thirds. The mother's share is reduced from one-third to one-sixth, yet the brothers do not inherit with the father. This is based on the principle that the grandfather takes the place of the father in certain aspects but not completely.

Key Terms
الجد (al-jadd): The paternal grandfather (father's father) in inheritance law.
المقاسمة (al-muqasamah): Proportional sharing between heirs, as opposed to fixed shares.
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third (1/3) of the estate.
السدس (al-sudus): One-sixth (1/6) of the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the presence of a grandfather and two full brothers (with no father), what is the grandfather's share per the text?
A) 1/6
B) 1/3
C) 1/2
D) 2/3

Key Takeaway
The grandfather inherits one-third by muqasamah with full brothers, and the mother's share reduces to one-sixth when two or more siblings exist.

The Mushtarakah (Himariyyah) Case: Umar's Reasoning in Inheritance
Narrative of Umar's change of opinion regarding sharing the third with siblings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the facts of the Mushtarakah case, explain the dispute between Abu Bakr and Umar, and derive the share distribution under each view.

Core Idea
Full siblings share with uterine siblings only when a compelling argument from maternal unity convinced Umar.

This passage recounts a well-known incident in Islamic inheritance law where Caliph Umar changed his ruling after a clever argument. The case, known as al-Mushtarakah or al-Himariyyah, involves a specific combination of heirs: husband, mother, grandfather, uterine siblings, and a full sibling. The question is whether the full sibling should share in the one-third portion with the uterine siblings. The story illustrates the use of reasoning (qiyas) and the importance of the maternal link.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their base shares
List the deceased's heirs: husband (1/2), mother (1/6), grandfather, uterine siblings (1/3), and a full brother. Note the assigned shares: husband 1/2, mother 1/6, uterine siblings 1/3.
The grandfather's share is the residue after the fixed shares are allocated.
2
State the initial ruling (Abu Bakr)
Under Abu Bakr, the grandfather takes the residue, and the full sibling receives nothing. This is also Umar's initial view.
The grandfather is treated as a father and excludes all siblings.
3
Describe Umar's change of opinion
A man argued that all siblings share the same mother – even if the father were a donkey, they are from one mother. Umar pondered and then ruled that full siblings share equally in the third with uterine siblings.
The argument convinced Umar that the paternal link should not disadvantage siblings from the same mother.
4
Analyze the reasoning behind each view
Abu Bakr: grandfather excludes siblings because he acts as a father. Umar: uterine connection is stronger; the father only increases closeness.
This is an example of istihsan (juristic preference) and qiyas.
5
Note the resulting difference in distribution
Under Abu Bakr: full sibling gets 0; grandfather gets residue. Under Umar: full sibling shares in the 1/3 portion with uterine siblings equally.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether the full sibling inherits or not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وذكر في المضمرات أن المسائل المتعلقة بالاخوة خمسة أحدها الشركة وهي أن تترك المرأة زوجها وأماً وجداً أو إخوة من أم وأخاً من أب وأم فللزوج النصف وللأم السدس ولولد الأم الثلث ولا شيء للأخ الأب والأم وهذا قول أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه، ويشترك أولاد الأب والأم مع أولاد الأم في الثلث كأنهم أولاد أم واحد سواء فيه الذكر والأنثى، وهذا قول عمر أخذ مالك والشافعي، وكان عمر رضي الله عنه يقول أولاً كما يقول من رضي هو الله عنه وبه أبو بكر رضي الله عنه ثم رجع إلى قول غيره، وسبب رجوعه أنه سأل هذه المسألة عن فأجاب كما هو مذهبه فقام واحد من أولاد الأب فقال : يا أمير المؤمنين هب أن أبانا كان حماراً ألسنا من أم واحدة والأب لا يزيد إلا قرباً فأطرق عمر رأسه متأملاً ثم رفع رأسه فقال: صدقواهم سواء أم واحدة فنشركهم في الثلث فسميت المسألة مشتركة لتشريك عمر وحمارية لقول القائل . وأما المسألة المنبرية والثالثة الأكدرية والرابعة العثمانية وقد مرت. وأما الخامسة الخمرية وهي ثلاث أخوات متفرقات وثلاث جدات متحاذيات وجد أب الأب تحجب أم الأب بأب الأب وتحجب الأخت من الأم أيضاً والأخت من الأب تدخل في المقاسمة وتخرج بغير شيء على الخلاف وتخرج المسألة من اثني عشر بعد القطع وإنما سميت حمزية لأن حمزة بن حبيب فعلها.
And it is mentioned in al-Mudmarat that the cases related to siblings are five: the first is the partnership (shirkah), which is that a woman leaves her husband, mother, grandfather, and siblings from the mother and a brother from the father and mother. Then for the husband half, for the mother the sixth, for the siblings from the mother the third, and nothing for the brother from the father and mother. This is the saying of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (RA). And the children of the father and mother share with the children of the mother in the third as if they were children of one mother, equal whether male or female. This is the saying of Umar (RA), taken by Malik and al-Shafi'i. And Umar (RA) used to say initially as Abu Bakr (RA) said, then he reverted to another's saying. The reason for his reversion is that he asked about this case and was answered according to his own madhhab, then a man from the children of the father stood up and said: 'O Commander of the Faithful, even if our father were a donkey, are we not from one mother? The father only increases closeness.' So Umar hung his head pondering, then lifted his head and said: 'You have spoken the truth. They are all equal, from one mother. So we make them share in the third.' Thus this case was called 'mushtarakah' because of Umar's sharing, and 'himariyyah' because of the man's statement. As for the minbariyyah case, the third akdariyyah, and the fourth uthmaniyyah, they have already passed. And as for the fifth khamriyyah, it is three sisters of different types and three grandmothers conflicting, and the grandfather of the father excludes the mother's father, and also excludes the sister from the mother, and the sister from the father enters into muqasamah and exits with nothing according to a difference, and the case works out from twelve after cutting. It is called hamziyyah because Hamzah ibn Habib did it.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage presents the famous 'Mushtarakah' or 'Himariyyah' case in inheritance law. The case involves a deceased woman who leaves her husband (1/2), mother (1/6), grandfather, and siblings (both uterine and full). The dispute between Abu Bakr and Umar was whether the full siblings (from both parents) share with the uterine siblings in the one-third portion, or are excluded. Initially, Abu Bakr (and Umar) held that the full siblings do not share, as the grandfather takes the remaining. Umar later changed his view after being persuaded by the argument that all siblings are from the same mother, and the father only increases closeness. Thus, the full siblings are included in the third. This ruling was adopted by Malik and al-Shafi'i as well. The story illustrates the use of reasoning (qiyas) in inheritance and the importance of the mother's side. The passage then lists four other famous cases: al-minbariyyah, al-akdariyyah, al-uthmaniyyah, and al-khamriyyah (also called hamziyyah).

Key Terms
المشتركة (al-mushtarakah): The case where full siblings share with uterine siblings in the one-third portion.
الحمارية (al-himariyyah): Another name for the mushtarakah case, derived from the man's statement 'if our father were a donkey'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Mushtarakah case, why did Umar change his ruling?
A) He received a revelation
B) A man argued that all siblings are from the same mother
C) Abel was considered closer than brothers
D) The grandfather was absent

Key Takeaway
The Mushtarakah case demonstrates how a powerful analogy based on maternal unity can override a default exclusion rule.

Types of Hijab in Faraid: Hirmān and Nuqsān
Classification of hijab into hirmān and nuqsān

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hajb hirmān and hajb nuqsān and identify which heirs are subject to each type.

Core Idea
Hajb hirmān excludes all but six; hajb nuqsān reduces shares of only five.

This passage from al-Dhakhirah provides a foundational classification of hijab in Hanafi inheritance law. Understanding these two types is crucial for correctly applying exclusion rules in faraid calculations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of hijab
Read the passage and note that hijab is divided into hirmān (total exclusion) and nuqsān (reduction). Understand the difference: hirmān removes the person entirely; nuqsān shifts them from a larger share to a smaller one.
The text explicitly states 'حجب على نوعين: حجب حرمان وحجب نقصان'.
2
List the six heirs never totally excluded
Locate the phrase 'الكل إلا على ستة' and list the six: husband, wife, father, mother, daughter, son. Memorize this set—they are protected from hirmān.
These six are always entitled to some share, though they may be reduced.
3
Identify the five heirs subject to share reduction
Find 'حجب نقصان لا يرد إلا على ثلاثة' and the later list of five: spouses, mother, grandmother, daughter's son, paternal half-sister. Understand that these heirs can have their shares lowered but never entirely removed.
The passage mentions two lists; the later list of five includes the grandmother and daughter's son, expanding the initial three.
4
Grasp the two underlying principles
The text gives two principles: (1) an heir related through an intermediate is excluded by that intermediate, except uterine siblings because their mother does not take the whole estate; (2) the nearer degree excludes the farther among 'asabat. These explain how hirmān operates.
Principle (1) is about 'proxy exclusion'; principle (2) is the standard 'nearest first' rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الذخيرة فصل في الحجب: يجب أن يعلم بأن الحجب على نوعين: حجب حرمان وحجب نقصان فحجب الحرمان يرد على الكل إلا على ستة: الزوج والزوجة والأب والأم والبنت والابن وحجب النقصان لا يرد إلا على ثلاثة : الزوج والزوجة والأم والحجب على نوعين: حجب نقصان وهو حجب عن سهم إلى سهم وذلك لخمس نفر: الزوجين والأم والجدة وبنت الابن والأخت لأب. وحجب حرمان والورثة فيه فريقان فريق لا يحجبون بحال وهم ستة وهذا ينبني على أصلين: أحدهما أن كل من يدلي إلى الميت بشخص لا يرث مع وجود ذلك الشخص سوى أولاد الأم فإنهم يرثون معها لانعدام استحقاقها التركة، والثاني الأقرب فالأقرب كما في العصبات.
And in al-Dhakhirah, a chapter on hijab: We must know that hijab is of two types: hijab of prevention (hirmān) and hijab of reduction (nuqsān). Hijab of prevention applies to all except six: the husband, the wife, the father, the mother, the daughter, and the son. Hijab of reduction applies only to three: the husband, the wife, and the mother. And hijab is of two types: hijab of reduction—which is removal from one share to another—and that is for five persons: the two spouses, the mother, the grandmother, the daughter's son, and the sister from the father. And hijab of prevention—the heirs are two groups: a group that are never excluded (six) and this is based on two principles: first, everyone who is connected to the deceased through a person does not inherit in the presence of that person, except the children of the mother, for they inherit with her because she does not have entitlement to the estate; second, the nearest [in relation] takes precedence, as in the 'asabat.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage from al-Dhakhirah provides a concise classification of hijab (exclusion) in inheritance. Hijab is of two fundamental types: (1) Hijab hirmān (total exclusion) which prevents an heir from inheriting anything. This applies to all heirs except six: the husband, wife, father, mother, son, and daughter. (2) Hijab nuqsān (partial reduction) which reduces an heir's share from a larger fixed share to a smaller one. This applies only to the husband, wife, and mother. The text also mentions that nuqsān can affect an additional two: the grandmother and the daughter's son? Actually, it lists five persons for nuqsān: the spouses, mother, grandmother, daughter's son, and half-sister. Then it reiterates that six persons are never excluded. This is based on two principles: first, that an heir who is related through an intermediate person is excluded by that intermediate person, except for uterine siblings who inherit with their mother because she does not take the entire estate; second, the rule of the nearer excluding the farther applies among the 'asabat.

Key Terms
حجب حرمان (hajb hirmān): Total exclusion from inheritance.
حجب نقصان (hajb nuqsān): Reduction of share from a larger prescribed share to a smaller one.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 3
B) 6
C) 5
D) 7

Key Takeaway
Hijab in faraid includes both total exclusion (hirmān) and share reduction (nuqsān), with six heirs completely protected from the former and five subject to the latter.

The Mother's Share: Three States and the Quranic Proof
Ruling with proof on mother's share and its variations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three possible shares of the mother in Hanafi faraid, apply the conditions that trigger each, and explain the Quranic proof and the ikhtilaf with Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
The mother takes one-third, one-sixth, or one-third of the remainder — each determined by the presence of children, siblings, or a surviving spouse.

The mother's share in inheritance is not a single fixed fraction; it shifts depending on the other heirs present. This lesson unpacks the three scenarios from the matn and the commentary, grounding each in the Quran and the reasoning of the Companions. You will learn the precise conditions that reduce her share from one-third to one-sixth or adjust it to one-third of the remainder.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three possible shares
State the three fractions the mother can inherit: thuluth (1/3), sudus (1/6), and thuluth al-baqi (1/3 of the remainder).
2
Link each share to its conditions
For 1/3: no child or child of a son, and fewer than two siblings. For 1/6: existence of a child/child of a son or at least two siblings. For thuluth al-baqi: presence of the father along with one spouse.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
Analyze verse 4:11: 'If he has siblings, then for his mother the sixth.' Understand how the word 'ikhwah' is interpreted by the majority to include two or more.
4
Consider the ikhtilaf with Ibn Abbas
Ibn Abbas held that 'ikhwah' (plural) requires at least three. The majority refute this using Quranic examples where dual is referred to with plural pronouns.
5
Understand thuluth al-baqi and the logic behind it
When the father and one spouse survive, the mother receives a third of what remains after the spouse's share. The commentary explains why she does not take a full third, citing the principle that the father should receive double the mother's share when they inherit together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( وللأم الثلث وذلك عند عدم الولد ولد الابن لما تلونا وعند عدم الاثنين من الإخوة والأخوات على ما نبين. قال رحمه الله: (ومع الولد وولد الابن أو الاثنين من الأخوة والأخوات لا أولادهم السدس) يعني مع واحد من هؤلاء المذكورين لا ترث الثلث وإنما ترث السدس لما تلونا ولقوله تعالى فإن كان له إخوة فلأمه السدس [النساء : ۱۱] فاسم الولد في المتلو يتناول الولد وولد الابن على قول جمهور الصحابة، وروي عن ابن عباس أنه لا تحجب الأم من الثلث إلى السدس إلا بثلاثة منهم عملاً بظاهر الآية فإن الإخوة جمع وأقله ثلاثة والجمهور على أن الجمع يطلق على المثنى قال الله تعالى وهل أتاك نبؤا الخصم إذ تسوروا المحراب إذا دخلوا على داود ففزع منهم قالوا لا تخف خصمان بغي بعضنا على بعض [ص: ۲۲] فأعاد ضمير الجمع في «تسوروا» و «دخلوا» وفي «منهم» على المثنى الملكان اللذان دخلا عليه كما في محله عرف ومثل هذا كثير شائع في كلام العرب. قال رحمه الله : (ومع الأب واحد الزوجين ثلث الباقي بعد فرض أحدهما فيكون لهما السدس مع الزوج والأب والربع مع الزوجة والأب لأنه هو الثلث الباقي بعد فرض أحدهما فصار للأم ثلاثة أحوال : ثلث الكل وثلث الباقي بعد فرض أحد الزوجين، والسدس. وقد ذكرنا الكل بتوفيق الله تعالى ولذا جعل الله للأم ثلث ما ترثه هي والأب عند عدم الولد والإخوة لا ثلث الكل لقوله تعالى وورثه أبواه فلأمه الثلث [النساء : ۱۱] أي ثلث ما يرثانه والذي أحد الزوجين هو الباقي من فرضه ولأنها لو أخذت ثلث الكل يكون نصيبها ضعف يرثانه مع نصيب الأب مع الزوج أو قريباً من نصيبه مع الزوجة والنص يقتضي تفضيله عليها بالضعف إذا لم يوجد الولد والإخوة ولهذا قال ابن مسعود في الرد عليه ما أراد الله تفضيل الأنثى على الذكر. وقال زيد لا أفضل الأنثى على الذكر ومرادهما عند الاستواء في القرابة والقرب، وأما عند الاختلاف فلا يمتنع تفضيل الأنثى على الذكر ولهذا لو كان مكان الأب جد كان للأم ثلث الجميع فلا يبالي بتفضيلها عليه لكونها أقرب منه . وأما عند أبي يوسف لها ثلث الباقي أيضاً مع الجد وهو مروي عن عمر وابن مسعود رضي الله عنهما فإنهما ما كانا يفضلان الأم على الجد. قال رحمه الله : (وللجدات وإن كثرن السدس إن لم يتخلل جد فاسد في نسبتها إلى الميت قال في الأصل والكلام في الجدات في مواضع في ترتيبهن ومعرفة الصحيحة من الفاسدة منهن وفي قدر ميراثهن وفيما يسقطن به ؛ فالأول كل شخص له جدتان أم أم وأم أب ولأبيه وأمه كذلك وهكذا إلى كل واحد من الأصول إلى أن ينتهي إلى آدم وحواء عليهما السلام، فالصحيحة منهن من لا يتخلل في نسبتها إلى الميت ذكر بين انثيين، والفاسدة من تخلل في نسبتها ذكر وذلك جد فاسد فمن يدلي به يكون فاسداً ذكراً كان أو أنثى، وعند سعد بن أبي وقاص الفاسدة من تدلي بذكر مطلقاً. وإذا أردت تنزيل كل عدد من الجدات الوارثات المتحاذيات فاذكر أولاً لفظة أم أم بمقدار العدد الذي تريده ثم نقول ثانياً أم أم وتجعل مكان الأم الأخيرة أباً ثم في كل مرة تبدل مكان الأم أباً على الأول إلى أن تبقى لفظة
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And for the mother is the third, that is when there is no child or child of a son, as we recited, and when there are not two siblings (brothers/sisters), as we will explain.' He said: 'And with the child or child of a son, or two siblings, not their children, the sixth'—meaning with one of these mentioned, she does not inherit the third but rather the sixth, as we recited and for His saying: 'If he has siblings, then for his mother the sixth' (al-Nisa 4:11). So the word 'child' in the recited verse includes the son and the son's son according to the majority of the Companions. And it is narrated from Ibn Abbas that the mother is not prevented from the third to the sixth except by three, acting on the apparent meaning of the verse, for 'siblings' is plural and its minimum is three. But the majority holds that the plural can refer to the dual. Allah said: 'Has the news come to you of the disputants who climbed the wall of the sanctuary? When they entered upon David, he was alarmed by them. They said: Fear not, we are two disputants, one of us has wronged the other.' (Sad 38:21-22). He used the plural pronouns 'tasaraw' and 'dakhalu' and 'minhum' for the two angels. And many similar examples are common in Arabic speech. He said: 'And with the father, or one of the spouses, she takes a third of the remainder after the share of one of them, so that it becomes for them the sixth with the husband and father, and the fourth with the wife and father, because it is the third of the remainder after the share of one of them. So for the mother there are three cases: a third of the whole, a third of the remainder after the share of one of the spouses, and the sixth. We have mentioned all by the grace of Allah. That is why Allah made for the mother a third of what she and the father inherit when there is no child or siblings, not a third of the whole, for His saying 'And if he is inherited by his parents, for his mother is the third' (al-Nisa 4:11) means a third of what they two inherit. And if one of the spouses is present, it is the remainder after his share. And because if she took a third of the whole, her share would be double the share of the father with the husband, or close to his share with the wife, whereas the text necessitates preferring him over her by double when there is no child or siblings. Hence Ibn Mas'ud said in refutation: 'Allah did not intend to prefer the female over the male.' And Zayd said: 'I do not prefer the female over the male.' Their intent is when they are equal in relationship and proximity. But when there is a difference, it is not impossible to prefer the female over the male. For this reason, if the grandfather were in place of the father, the mother would take a third of the whole, and he would not care about preferring her over him because she is closer. According to Abu Yusuf, she also takes a third of the remainder with the grandfather, and this is narrated from Umar and Ibn Mas'ud, for they did not prefer the mother over the grandfather. He said: 'And for grandmothers, even if numerous, is the sixth, provided that no unsound grandfather intervenes in their relationship to the deceased.' He said in al-Asl: The discussion about grandmothers is in several places: about their ranking, knowing the sound from the unsound among them, about the amount of their inheritance, and about what excludes them. The first: Every person has two grandmothers: the mother's mother and the father's mother, and likewise for his father and mother, and so on up to each of the ancestors until reaching Adam and Eve, peace be upon them. The sound among them is she in whose relationship to the deceased no male intervenes between two females. The unsound is she in whose relationship a male intervenes, that being an unsound grandfather. So whoever is connected through him is unsound, whether male or female. According to Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, the unsound is she who is connected through a male absolutely. When you want to list any number of inheriting grandmothers who are conflicting, first mention the phrase 'mother's mother' according to the number you want, then secondly say 'mother's mother' and replace the last mother with 'father', then each time replace the place of mother with father from the beginning until the phrase remains ...
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the mother's share (al-umm) in inheritance. It first restates the ruling from the matn: the mother receives one-third when there is no child or child of a son, and when there are not two siblings. If there is a child or two siblings, her share reduces to one-sixth. The proof is the Quranic verse 'if he has siblings, then for his mother the sixth' (al-Nisa 4:11). There is a subtle difference of opinion with Ibn Abbas, who held that the plural 'ikhwah' requires at least three siblings for reduction to the sixth. However, the majority of Companions and scholars hold that the plural can apply to two, citing Quranic examples where dual is referred to with plural pronouns. The author then discusses the case with the father or one of the spouses: the mother takes a third of the remainder after the share of the spouse. This results in three possible states for the mother: a third of the whole (when no child or siblings and no spouse), a third of the remainder (when one parent and a spouse are present), and the sixth (when there are children or siblings). The reasoning is that the Quran says 'for his mother the third' but meaning a third of what the parents inherit, not the whole estate. With a spouse, the remainder is less. The author also addresses the objection that the mother might receive more than the father in certain cases (e.g., with a spouse). Ibn Mas'ud and Zayd argued that preferring the female over the male is not intended except when they are equally close, but here the father is closer, so he should receive double. However, if the grandfather is in place of the father, the mother can take a third of the whole because she is closer to the deceased than the grandfather. Abu Yusuf differs, giving the mother a third of the remainder even with the grandfather. The passage then shifts to the grandmothers (al-jaddāt). They receive one-sixth as long as no unsound grandfather intervenes. The definition of a sound grandmother is one in whose line of relationship to the deceased no male appears between two females. An unsound grandmother has a male (an unsound grandfather) in the line. Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas holds that any grandmother who is connected through a male is unsound. The author begins to explain a method for listing multiple inheriting grandmothers when they conflict.

Key Terms
ثلث الباقي (thuluth al-baqi): A third of the remaining estate after the share of one of the spouses has been taken.
إخوة (ikhwah): Siblings (brothers and/or sisters). In the context of inheritance, their presence (at least two by majority) reduces the mother's share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Companions, how many siblings reduce the mother's share to one-sixth?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
The mother's share in Hanafi faraid is dynamic: 1/3, 1/6, or 1/3 of the remainder, each triggered by specific heirs, grounded in Quran 4:11 with a clear linguistic argument against Ibn Abbas' stricter view.

The Grandmothers' Inheritance: Sound vs. Unsound, and the Sixth Share
Definition and ruling on grandmothers' inheritance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define a sound grandmother (al-jaddah al-sahihah) in Hanafi faraid, state her share (one-sixth), and identify the condition for multiple grandmothers inheriting.

Core Idea
A grandmother inherits one-sixth if she is 'sound' — no male between two females in her lineage to the deceased.

The inheritance of grandmothers is a nuanced area in faraid. The passage defines which grandmothers qualify as heirs (sound) and which do not (unsound). It also outlines the method for ranking multiple grandmothers to avoid errors in distribution. This lesson focuses on the key concepts and the ruling of one-sixth.

Guided Path
1
Define the sound grandmother
A sound grandmother (al-jaddah al-sahihah) is one in whose lineage to the deceased no male intervenes between two females. For example, the mother's mother (no male between) and the father's mother (the father is between, but that is a male between two females? Wait: father's mother: father (male) between grandmother and deceased. Actually, the definition: no male between two females. In father's mother lineage: deceased -> father (male) -> paternal grandmother (female) -> paternal great-grandmother (female). There is a male (father) between the deceased and the paternal grandmother, but not between two females. The definition is when tracing the lineage, if you have a male appearing between two females, that makes it unsound. So for father's mother, it is sound because the male (father) is between the deceased and the grandmother, but that is not between two females. The condition is: no male appears between two consecutive females. Let's check: in father's mother, we have deceased (male?) -> father (male) -> grandmother (female). There is no female before the grandmother? Actually, the lineage goes from deceased up: the first female encountered is the mother, then mother's mother, etc. For father's mother: first female is father's mother? The chain: deceased (male) -> father (male) -> father's mother (female). So there is a male (father) between the deceased and the first female? The definition says 'between two females'. So if the chain is female-female-female, it's sound. If there is a male in between any two females, it's unsound. Example: mother's mother: females all the way. Father's mother: father (male) is between the deceased and the grandmother, but there is no female after father before the grandmother? Actually, the grandmother is female, and the previous link (father) is male, so there is a male between the deceased (male) and the grandmother (female). Is that considered 'between two females'? No, because the deceased is male. So the condition is specifically no male between two females. So father's mother is sound because the male (father) is not between two females; he is before the first female. So the sound grandmothers are all those where, when you go up the tree, you do not encounter a male standing between two consecutive females. This includes the mother's mother, father's mother, and higher up as long as the chain has no male between females.
Additional step: explain the difference with Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas who said any grandmother connected through a male is unsound.
2
Contrast with the unsound grandmother
An unsound grandmother is one in whose lineage a male appears between two females. For example, if the chain is female - male - female, that grandmother is unsound and does not inherit.
3
State the share of the sound grandmother
Sound grandmother(s) receive one-sixth (1/6) of the estate, shared equally among them if multiple, provided no closer heir (like the mother) excludes them.
4
Understand the method for listing multiple grandmothers
When multiple grandmothers inherit and some are closer, the method helps determine who is included. The text begins to explain but cuts off; in practice, the closest generation takes the sixth.

He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And for the mother is the third, that is when there is no child or child of a son, as we recited, and when there are not two siblings (brothers/sisters), as we will explain.' This passage is a detailed commentary on the mother's share (al-umm) in inheritance. Key Terms
الجدة الصحيحة (al-jaddah al-sahihah): A grandmother in whose lineage to the deceased no male appears between two females.
الجدة الفاسدة (al-jaddah al-fasidah): A grandmother in whose lineage a male appears between two females, or (per Sa'd) any grandmother connected through a male.

Mother's Share in Inheritance: Three States and the Grandfather Dispute
Explains the three possible shares of the mother and a dispute regarding the grandfather.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three possible shares of the mother in Hanafi faraid and explain the relied-upon position when the grandfather inherits.

Core Idea
The mother inherits one-third of the whole, one-third of the residue, or one-sixth; with the grandfather, she takes one-third of the whole per the mufta bihi.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the mother's inheritance shares alongside the father and one spouse. It interprets the Quranic verse, addresses the principle of male preference, and presents an internal Hanafi dispute about the grandfather's effect on the mother's share.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three states of the mother’s share
List the three scenarios: one-third of the whole (no child/sibling, no spouse), one-third of the residue after spouse’s share (no child/sibling, with spouse), and one-sixth (with child or multiple siblings).
The third state (one-sixth) is mentioned but not elaborated here.
2
Analyze the Quranic proof (4:11)
The verse 'فلأمه الثلث' is interpreted as one-third of what the parents inherit, not one-third of the whole estate, due to the context of the spouse's share.
This interpretation avoids giving the mother more than the father in the presence of a spouse.
3
Examine the reasoning against giving the mother one-third of the whole with father and spouse
The author shows that giving the mother one-third of the whole would violate the principle that the male gets double the female's share when equal in kinship.
Ibn Mas'ud and Zayd are quoted: 'Allah did not intend to prefer the female over the male.'
4
Contrast the position of Abu Yusuf regarding the grandfather
Abu Yusuf holds that with the grandfather, the mother gets one-third of the residue, citing Umar and Ibn Mas'ud. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad) give her one-third of the whole.
The dispute hinges on whether the grandfather is analogized to the father in reducing the mother's share.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is that the mother takes one-third of the whole with the grandfather, because she is closer in kinship than the grandfather, and male preference applies only when equal.
This is the tarjih by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحد الزوجين ثلث الباقي بعد فرض أحدهما فيكون لهما السدس مع الزوج والأب والربع مع الزوجة والأب لأنه هو الثلث الباقي بعد فرض أحدهما فصار للأم ثلاثة أحوال : ثلث الكل وثلث الباقي بعد فرض أحد الزوجين، والسدس. وقد ذكرنا الكل بتوفيق الله تعالى ولذا جعل الله للأم ثلث ما ترثه هي والأب عند عدم الولد والإخوة لا ثلث الكل لقوله تعالى وورثه أبواه فلأمه الثلث [النساء : ۱۱] أي ثلث ما يرثانه والذي أحد الزوجين هو الباقي من فرضه ولأنها لو أخذت ثلث الكل يكون نصيبها ضعف يرثانه مع نصيب الأب مع الزوج أو قريباً من نصيبه مع الزوجة والنص يقتضي تفضيله عليها بالضعف إذا لم يوجد الولد والإخوة ولهذا قال ابن مسعود في الرد عليه ما أراد الله تفضيل الأنثى على الذكر. وقال زيد لا أفضل الأنثى على الذكر ومرادهما عند الاستواء في القرابة والقرب، وأما عند الاختلاف فلا يمتنع تفضيل الأنثى على الذكر ولهذا لو كان مكان الأب جد كان للأم ثلث الجميع فلا يبالي بتفضيلها عليه لكونها أقرب منه . وأما عند أبي يوسف لها ثلث الباقي أيضاً مع الجد وهو مروي عن عمر وابن مسعود رضي الله عنهما فإنهما ما كانا يفضلان الأم على الجد.
One of the spouses takes one-third of the remainder after the share of the other. So for them both (the parents) is the sixth with the husband and the father, and the quarter with the wife and the father, because it is the one-third of the remainder after the share of one of the spouses. Thus the mother has three states: one-third of the whole, one-third of the remainder after the share of one of the spouses, and one-sixth. We have mentioned the whole by the grace of Allah. And for this Allah made for the mother one-third of what she and the father inherit, not one-third of the whole, in the absence of children and siblings, due to His statement: 'And if he has no child and his parents inherit him, then to his mother is one-third' [An-Nisa 4:11] meaning one-third of what they both inherit, and that which one of the spouses takes is the remainder of his share. And because if she took one-third of the whole, her share would be double what she inherits with the father's share with the husband, or close to his share with the wife, while the text requires giving him preference over her by double when there is no child or sibling. For this reason Ibn Mas'ud said in refutation of it: 'Allah did not intend to prefer the female over the male.' And Zayd said: 'I do not prefer the female over the male.' Their meaning is when they are equal in kinship and closeness. As for when they differ, there is no prevention of preferring the female over the male. So if instead of the father there were a grandfather, the mother would have one-third of the whole, and there is no concern for preferring her over him because she is closer than him. As for Abu Yusuf, she has one-third of the remainder also with the grandfather, which is narrated from Umar and Ibn Mas'ud, radiya Allahu anhum, for they did not prefer the mother over the grandfather.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and proof concerning the mother's share when inheriting alongside one spouse and the father. The author (al-Marghinani) explains the three possible scenarios for the mother: she gets one-third of the entire estate when there is no child or sibling and no spouse; one-third of the remainder after the spouse's share when the father is absent and a spouse is present; or one-sixth when there is a child or multiple siblings. The primary proof is the Quranic verse 4:11, which the author interprets as 'one-third of what the parents inherit' (i.e., after the spouse's share). The passage also discusses a dispute with Abu Yusuf, who holds that the mother gets one-third of the remainder even when the grandfather is present, citing Umar and Ibn Mas'ud. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that with the grandfather, the mother gets one-third of the whole, not the remainder. The author clarifies that preferring the female over the male is not always prohibited; it is prohibited only when equal in kinship.

Key Terms
أم (umm): The mother of the deceased.
ثلث الباقي (thulth al-baqi): One-third of what remains after the spouse's share is taken.
ثلث الكل (thulth al-kull): One-third of the entire estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the absence of children and siblings, what is the mother's share when the father and spouse are present?

B) One-sixth of the whole estate

D) One-half of the estate

Key Takeaway
The mother's share varies based on the presence of spouse, children, and siblings; with the grandfather, she takes one-third of the whole according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

The Inheritance of Grandmothers: The Sixth Share and the Classification into Sound and Unsound
Defines the share of grandmothers and the test for soundness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish a sound grandmother from an unsound grandmother and state that all sound grandmothers collectively inherit one-sixth equally.

Core Idea
All sound grandmothers share one-sixth equally; an unsound grandmother does not inherit.

In Hanafi inheritance law, grandmothers are treated as a group of Quranic heirs with a fixed share of one-sixth. However, not every woman who is a grandmother qualifies. The key distinction lies in whether a male intervenes between two females in her lineage to the deceased. This lesson defines the terms, provides the ruling, and gives a method to enumerate inheriting grandmothers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for grandmothers
What is the share of grandmothers according to the text? It is one-sixth provided no false grandfather intervenes.
2
Define sound vs unsound grandmothers
A sound grandmother has no male between two females in her lineage; an unsound one does. The male that intervenes is called a false grandfather.
3
Enumerate inheriting grandmothers
Use the method: start with the required number of 'mother's mother' and then replace one 'mother' with 'father' for each successive grandmother from the paternal side.
4
Examine the proof
The hadith of Ubadah ibn al-Samit and the practice of Abu Bakr establish the sixth shared equally.
5
Consider the dispute
Some Hanafi scholars argue that when the father is alive, all grandmothers are excluded, but the relied-upon view is that sound grandmothers inherit regardless.
This dispute is discussed in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

يعلم بأن الجدات طبقتان : طبقة هي من جملة أصحاب الفرائض يعرفن بالثابتات، وطبقة وهي من جملة ذوي الأرحام يعرفن بالساقطات. فالحاصل إذا كان لميت أم الأب وأم أم الأم والأب حي فعند بعض المشايخ لا شيء لواحدة منهن لأن أم أم الأم تصير محجوبة بأم الأب وأم الأب تصير محجوبة بالأب، وعند بعض المشايخ ترث الجدة من قبل الأم وفريضة الواحدة منهن السدس بينهن بالسوية وهذا قول عامة الصحابة. وفي المضمرات الجدة الواحدة والجدات فصاعداً السدس لا يزاد عليه إلا عند الرد ولا ينقص إلا عند العول. والجدات ست ثنتان لك، وثنتان لأمك، وثنتان لأبيك، والكل وارثات إلا واحدة وهي أم أب. عنه : .
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And for grandmothers, even if they are many, is the sixth, provided that a false grandfather does not intervene in their relation to the deceased.' He said in al-Asl: The discussion about grandmothers occurs in several places: regarding their arrangement, distinguishing the sound from the unsound among them, the amount of their inheritance, and what excludes them. First: every person has two grandmothers: mother's mother and father's mother; and his father similarly, and his mother similarly, and so on up to each of the roots until reaching Adam and Eve, peace be upon them. The sound ones are those in whose lineage to the deceased there is no male between two females. The unsound one is one in whose lineage a male intervenes, and that is a false grandfather; so whoever traces through him becomes unsound, whether male or female. According to Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, the unsound one traces through a male absolutely. If you want to place any number of inheriting grandmothers who are at the same level, first mention the phrase 'mother's mother' to the number you want, then secondly say 'mother's mother' and replace the last 'mother' with 'father', then each time replace a 'mother' with 'father' until only one 'mother' remains. Example: If you ask about four inheriting grandmothers at the same level, say 'mother's mother's mother's mother' four times to establish the level where they can be imagined to meet; because they cannot be imagined to meet except if they ascend the number of levels. So four inheriting grandmothers cannot be imagined to meet except at the fourth level. So you say 'mother's mother's mother's mother' four times – this is one of them, from the mother's side. Then bring another from the father's side at her level, so you say 'mother's mother's mother's father'. Then bring another from the grandfather's side, so you say 'mother's mother's father's father'. Then bring another from the great-grandfather's side, so you say 'mother's father's father's father'. And it cannot be imagined that more than that gather at this level, because for every true grandfather there is an inheriting mother, and similarly his mother's mother even if high, and it cannot be imagined that there is an inheriting grandmother from every father except one. So you need to bring from the fathers a number equal to them except one, which is the one from the mother's side. The second traces through the father, so in the second expression you removed one 'mother' and replaced it with 'father'. The third traces through the grandfather, so you removed two and replaced them with two 'father's. The fourth traces through the great-grandfather, so you removed three 'mother's and replaced them with three 'father's. This is the method for more than them ad infinitum. This is the knowledge of the sound ones. If you want to know the corresponding unsound ones from the sound ones, take the number of sound ones, place it on your right, subtract two from it, and place them on your left as the remainder on your right. The total is the number of all sound and unsound grandmothers. Then if you subtract the number of sound ones, the remainder are the unsound ones. Example: If you ask about four sound grandmothers, how many unsound ones correspond to them? Take four on your right, subtract two, take them on your left. Then if you double this subtracted number by what remains on your right, it becomes eight, which is the total number of all grandmothers in this category. Then if you subtract the number of sound ones, which are four, four remain, which are the unsound ones. And their inheritance is the sixth, even if they are many; they share it equally, due to the narration of Ubadah ibn al-Samit that the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, decreed between two grandmothers when they come together a sixth, shared equally. And Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him, associated the two grandmothers in the sixth. He will mention what excludes them. In al-Zahiriyya: Know that every human being besides Jesus, peace be upon him, must have two grandmothers: one from the mother's side, which is the mother's mother, and the other from the father's side, which is the father's mother. You must know that grandmothers are of two categories: a category that is among the Ashab al-Fara'id (the Quranic heirs), known as the established ones, and a category that is among the Dhawi al-Arham (distant kindred), known as the excluded ones. So the conclusion: If the deceased has the father's mother and the mother's mother's mother and the father is alive, then according to some mashayikh, neither of them gets anything, because the mother's mother's mother is excluded by the father's mother, and the father's mother is excluded by the father. According to other mashayikh, the grandmother from the mother's side inherits, and the prescribed share for one of them is the sixth, divided among them equally. This is the saying of the generality of the Companions. In al-Mudmarat: One grandmother and more get the sixth; it is not increased except in the case of radd, and not decreased except in the case of awl. The grandmothers are six: two for you [the father's side?], two for your mother, and two for your father. All are inheriting except one, which is the mother of the father. From him: .
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling regarding the inheritance of grandmothers. The author explains that all grandmothers, however many, share one-sixth of the estate, provided that no 'false grandfather' (a male ancestor between the grandmother and the deceased who is not a true grandfather) intervenes. The text then classifies grandmothers into 'sound' (sahihah) and 'unsound' (fasidah). A sound grandmother is one whose lineage to the deceased does not contain a male between two females (i.e., she connects through a chain of females with no male except the deceased himself). An unsound grandmother has a male in her lineage, which makes her a 'false grandmother' who does not inherit. The author provides a mathematical method to enumerate inheriting grandmothers at the same level and compute the corresponding unsound ones. This method is based on the principle that at each level, only one grandmother from each line (mother's side, father's side, grandfather's side, etc.) can inherit. The proof is a hadith from Ubadah ibn al-Samit that the Prophet (PBUH) gave two grandmothers a sixth to share equally, and the practice of Abu Bakr. The passage also notes a dispute among later Hanafi scholars: when the father is alive, some mashayikh exclude all grandmothers (because the father excludes the father's mother, and the mother's mother's mother is excluded by the father's mother), while others allow the grandmother from the mother's side to inherit. The relied-upon position is that the sixth is for grandmothers as a general rule, subject to conditions of being sound.

Key Terms
جدات (jaddat): Grandmothers of the deceased, both paternal and maternal.
جد فاسد (jadd fasid): A false grandfather, i.e., a male ancestor who is not a true grandfather in the lineage (e.g., mother's father? Actually a false grandfather is one through whom a grandmother traces but who is not a direct male line ancestor of the deceased. More precisely, any male between two females in the grandmother's line to the deceased makes her unsound, and that male is a false grandfather).
صحيحة (sahihah): A sound grandmother whose lineage to the deceased contains no male between two females.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) She is the only grandmother

Key Takeaway
Sound grandmothers, however many, share one-sixth equally; unsound grandmothers do not inherit.

Grandmothers' Inheritance: One-Sixth Shared Equally
States the ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that all inheriting grandmothers share a fixed one-sixth equally, identify exceptions based on exclusion, and classify grandmothers as thabitat (fixed-share recipients) or saqitat (uterine relatives).

Core Idea
All inheriting grandmothers share one-sixth equally; the share never increases except by radd, never decreases except by 'awl.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the inheritance of grandmothers in the Hanafi school. The fixed share of one-sixth is established by the Prophet's decree and the practice of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq. The text also categorizes grandmothers into two classes—those who take fixed shares (thabitat) and those who do not (saqitat)—and addresses a disagreement among Hanafi scholars regarding exclusion when the father is alive. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to the conditions of inheritance and the equal division among multiple grandmothers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the fixed inheritance share for grandmothers as given in the passage: one-sixth, regardless of number, divided equally among them.
The share is fard (fixed) for those not excluded.
2
Locate the Proof
Find the proof cited: the hadith of 'Ubadah ibn al-Samit that the Prophet decreed the sixth equally between two grandmothers, and the practice of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted as evidence in faraid.
3
Classify Grandmothers
Distinguish between thabitat (grandmothers with fixed shares) and saqitat (those excluded or from dhawi al-arham).
Only thabitat inherit the one-sixth.
4
Apply Equal Division
When multiple grandmothers inherit, they share the one-sixth equally, as per the Prophet's judgment.
The share does not increase beyond one-sixth except by radd; does not decrease except by 'awl.
5
Examine Exclusion Scenarios
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement: when the father is alive, some mashayikh exclude both grandmothers, while others allow the maternal grandmother to inherit. The relied-upon position follows the generality of Companions.
The father excludes the paternal grandmother, and she in turn excludes the maternal grandmother according to one view; but the stronger view is that both inherit if not blocked by a closer heir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وميراثهن السدس وإن كثون يشتركن فيه لما روي عبادة بن الصامت أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قضى بين الجدتين إذا اجتمعتا بالسدس بالسوية، وأبو بكر الصديق رضي الله، أشرك بين الجدتين في السدس وسيذكر ما يسقطن به وفي الظهيرية: فاعلم أنه لا بد لكل واحد من بني آدم سوى عيسى عليه السلام أن يكون له جدتان إحداهما من قبل الأم وهي أم الأم والأخرى من قبل الأب وهي أم الأب يجب أن يعلم بأن الجدات طبقتان: طبقة هي من جملة أصحاب الفرائض يعرفن بالثابتات، وطبقة وهي من جملة ذوي الأرحام يعرفن بالساقطات. فالحاصل إذا كان لميت أم الأب وأم أم الأم والأب حي فعند بعض المشايخ لا شيء لواحدة منهن لأن أم أم الأم تصير محجوبة بأم الأب وأم الأب تصير محجوبة بالأب، وعند بعض المشايخ ترث الجدة من قبل الأم وفريضة الواحدة منهن السدس بينهن بالسوية وهذا قول عامة الصحابة. وفي المضمرات الجدة الواحدة والجدات فصاعداً السدس لا يزاد عليه إلا عند الرد ولا ينقص إلا عند العول. والجدات ست ثنتان لك، وثنتان لأمك، وثنتان لأبيك، والكل وارثات إلا واحدة وهي أم أب.
And their inheritance is the sixth, even if they are numerous they share in it, because it is narrated from 'Ubadah ibn al-Samit that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) decreed between two grandmothers when they come together the sixth equally. And Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him) made them share in the sixth. And he will mention by what they are excluded. And in al-Zahiriyyah: Know that it is necessary for every human being except Jesus (peace be upon him) to have two grandmothers: one from the mother's side, who is the mother of the mother, and the other from the father's side, who is the mother of the father. He must know that grandmothers are of two classes: a class that is among the owners of fixed shares, known as the thabitat (established), and a class that is among the dhawi al-arham (uterine relatives), known as the saqitat (fallen). So the bottom line is: if a deceased has a paternal grandmother (mother of father) and a maternal grandmother (mother of mother of mother) and the father is alive, then according to some mashayikh there is nothing for either of them, because the maternal grandmother of the mother is excluded by the paternal grandmother, and the paternal grandmother is excluded by the father. And according to some mashayikh, the grandmother from the mother's side inherits, and the obligation of one of them is the sixth divided among them equally, and this is the saying of the generality of the Companions. And in al-Mudmarat: the one grandmother and grandmothers and above, the sixth, it is not increased except in radd (return), and it is not decreased except in 'awl (increase). And the grandmothers are six: two for you, two for your mother, two for your father, and all are inheritors except one: the mother of the father.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling that all inheriting grandmothers share the one-sixth equally among them. It provides proof from the hadith of 'Ubadah ibn al-Samit (which is a basis for this ruling) and the practice of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq. The text then classifies grandmothers into two categories: those with fixed shares (thabitat) and those who are dhawi al-arham (saqitat). The discussion includes a disagreement among mashayikh regarding a scenario where the father is alive: some say both grandmothers are excluded (by the father or each other), while others say the maternal grandmother inherits. The text also quotes from Al-Mudmarat that the share does not increase beyond one-sixth except in cases of radd and does not decrease except in 'awl. It concludes by listing the six specific grandmothers, noting that all are inheritors except the mother of the father (who is excluded by the father).

Key Terms
ثابتات (thabitat): Grandmothers who are among the ashab al-fara'id (fixed share recipients) and inherit.
ساقطات (saqitat): Grandmothers who are among dhawi al-arham (uterine relatives) and do not inherit.
رد (radd): Return of the surplus to the sharers proportionally after the fixed shares are taken, in the absence of residuary heirs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only two grandmothers can inherit, and they split it

Key Takeaway
All Hanafi inheriting grandmothers share the fixed one-sixth equally among themselves, regardless of number, subject to exclusion rules and possible adjustment by radd or 'awl.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Effect of Multiple Lineages on Grandmother's Share
Intra-Hanafi dispute on grandmothers' shares

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding multiplicity of lineages and apply them to calculate the grandmothers' shares in an inheritance.

Core Idea
Two Hanafi giants disagree: Abu Yusuf gives equal shares; Muhammad counts each lineage.

In this passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq, the author presents an internal Hanafi dispute on whether a grandmother's multiple familial connections (jihaat) increase her inheritance share. Abu Yusuf holds that all grandmothers share the reserved sixth equally, while Muhammad holds that the share should be proportional to the number of lineages. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your faraid skills and reveals the depth of Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The core question: does a grandmother with two or three lineages get a larger share than a grandmother with one?
Lineages refer to the different familial connections (e.g., maternal and paternal) through which a grandmother is related to the deceased.
2
State each position
Abu Yusuf: No consideration for multiplicity; all grandmothers share the sixth equally. Muhammad: Multiplicity is considered; the sixth is divided according to the number of lineages.
These are both Hanafi positions; the school later adopts Abu Yusuf's view as mufta bihi.
3
Work through the examples
The text gives two examples: one from two lineages, one from three. Reconstruct the family trees to see how a grandmother gets multiple connections and how the sixth would be divided under each opinion.
Draw the marriage scenario to clearly see the lineages.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Yusuf, each grandmother gets an equal share of the sixth (e.g., 1/12 of the total estate if two grandmothers). Under Muhammad, a grandmother with two lineages gets 2/3 of the sixth (1/9 total) and the other gets 1/3 (1/18 total).
The practical difference is significant.
5
Note the tarjih
The relied-upon position is Abu Yusuf's (equality), as it aligns with the literal hadith and is simpler.
Later Hanafi works confirm this preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : وذات جهة كذات جهتين) يعني الجدة إذا كانت من جهة واحدة وسهم: والأخرى لها جهتان فهما سواء في الميراث. قال في الأصل وإن كانت للميت جدة من جهة واحدة وجدة من جهتين أو ثلاث جهات قال أبو يوسف : لا عبرة لكثرة الجهات والسدس بينهن بالسوية. وقال محمد : لكثرة الجهات عبرة والسدس بينهن على عدد الجهات وصورتها من جهتين : امرأة زوجت ابنة ابنها من ابن ابنها فولد بينهما غلام فهذه المرأة لهذا الغلام جدة من جهتين فإنها أم أم أم هذا الغلام وأم أب أب هذا الغلام، فلو مات هذا الغلام وترك هذه الجدة وجدة أخرى من جهة الأب فهي أم أم أبيه. قال أبو يوسف : السدس بينهما بالسوية. وقال محمد السدس بينهما أثلاثاً ثلثاه لذات الجهتين وثلثه لذات الجهة الواحدة وصورتها من الجهات الثلاثة هذه المرأة المزوجة زوجت بنت بنت بنت لأخرى هذا الغلام المولود فولد بينهما غلام فإن هذه الزوجة لهذا الغلام المولود الثاني من ثلاث من جهات من جهة هي أم أم أم أمه وهي من جهة هي أم أم أم أبيه ومن جهة أم أب أب أبيه، فلو مات هذا الغلام وترك هذه الجدة وجدة أخرى من قبل الأب وهي أم أم الأب فعلى قول أبي يوسف أن السدس بينهن بالسوية. وعلى قول محمد على أربعة أسهم ثلاثة أسهم للجدة واحد للجدة الأخرى.
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And the one with one lineage is like the one with two lineages' means the grandmother if she is from one lineage and the other has two lineages, then they are equal in inheritance. He said in al-Asl: If the deceased has a grandmother from one lineage and a grandmother from two or three lineages, Abu Yusuf said: No consideration is given to multiplicity of lineages, the sixth is divided among them equally. And Muhammad said: Multiplicity of lineages is considered, the sixth is divided among them according to the number of lineages. And its example from two lineages: A woman marries her son's daughter to her son's son, and a boy is born to them. This woman is for this boy a grandmother from two lineages: she is the mother of the mother of the mother of this boy and the mother of the father of the father of this boy. If this boy dies leaving this grandmother and another grandmother from the father's side, who is the mother of the mother of the father, Abu Yusuf said: The sixth is between them equally. And Muhammad said: The sixth is between them in thirds: two-thirds for the one with two lineages and one-third for the one with one lineage. And its example from three lineages: This married woman marries the daughter of the daughter of the daughter of another to this born boy, and a boy is born to them. This wife is for this second born boy from three lineages: from a lineage she is the mother of the mother of the mother of the mother of him, and from a lineage she is the mother of the mother of the mother of the father of him, and from a lineage she is the mother of the father of the father of the father of him. If this boy dies leaving this grandmother and another grandmother from the father's side, who is the mother of the mother of the father, then according to Abu Yusuf the sixth is between them equally. And according to Muhammad, it is according to four shares: three shares for the grandmother and one share for the other grandmother.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the effect of multiple lineages (jihaat) on the share of a grandmother. Abu Yusuf holds that all grandmothers, regardless of how many lineages they have, share the one-sixth equally. Muhammad holds that the share is divided according to the number of lineages: a grandmother from two lineages gets two-thirds of the sixth, and from three lineages gets three-fourths, etc. The text provides concrete examples through marriage scenarios that produce grandmothers with multiple familial connections. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Yusuf, as it is easier and more widely accepted, while Muhammad's view is considered a minority opinion within the school.

Key Terms
جهة (jihah): A lineage or familial connection through which a grandmother is related to the deceased.
جدة ذات جهات (jaddah dhat jihaat): A grandmother who is related to the deceased through more than one lineage (e.g., through both maternal and paternal lines).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Yusuf, if there are two grandmothers, one with two lineages and one with one, how is the sixth divided?
A) Equally between them
B) Two-thirds to the one with two lineages
C) Three-fourths to the one with two lineages
D) The one with two lineages takes all

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi inheritance, the mufta bihi is that multiple lineages do not increase a grandmother's share; all grandmothers share the sixth equally.
