Nearer Grandmother Excludes the Farther: Hanafi Rule and Counter-Arguments
States the principle that a nearer grandmother excludes a farther one, with counter-arguments and response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on exclusion of grandmothers and evaluate the opposing view using the principle of precedence by birth.

Core Idea
A nearer grandmother always excludes a farther one in inheritance, regardless of lineage side.

In inheritance law, the presence of closer relatives often blocks more distant ones. This lesson examines a specific case: grandmothers. The Hanafi school holds that a grandmother who is nearer in lineage excludes a more distant one, even if they come from different sides of the family. However, companions like Ibn Mas'ud and Zayd ibn Thabit held a different view. We will analyze the evidence and reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Recite the rule: 'The farther grandmother is excluded by the nearer,' regardless of whether they are from one side or two.
The text explicitly says 'sawa'an kana min jihah wahidah aw min jihatayn'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Quote the narration from Ibn Mas'ud: only the mother excludes grandmothers. Then the combined narration of Ibn Mas'ud and Zayd: a nearer from father's side does not exclude a farther from mother's side, but the reverse excludes.
The opponent's reasoning is based on analogy with the intermediary (the parent).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand their logic: grandmothers inherit through birth from parents, so each takes the ruling of the person through whom they trace. Since the father does not exclude maternal grandmothers, his mother should not exclude them. But the mother does exclude farther grandmothers, so her mother should also exclude.
This seems inconsistent: if the rule were consistent, the nearer from father's side would also exclude the farther from mother's side, but they claim it does not.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi counter: grandmothers inherit by virtue of birth itself, not as representatives. Therefore, closeness matters, just as with fathers. Also, not every ruling of the intermediary transfers: e.g., the maternal grandmother inherits only 1/6 and is excluded by the mother and father, unlike the mother herself.
The Hanafi argument uses qiyas (analogy) with fathers: a nearer father excludes a farther one.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: If a paternal grandmother (mother of father) and a maternal grandmother (mother of mother) survive, and the paternal is closer (e.g., the paternal grandmother is the mother of the father, the maternal is the mother of the mother's mother), under Hanafi the paternal excludes the maternal. Under opposing view, the nearer from father's side does not exclude the farther from mother's side, so both inherit.
The disagreement affects distribution in mixed-side scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : ( والبعدى تحجب بالقربى) سواء كانا من جهة واحدة أو من جهتين، وسواء كانت القربى وارثة أو محجوبة بالأب أو بالجد. وفي رواية عن ابن مسعود لا تحجب الجدات إلا الأم، وفي رواية عنه وعن زيد بن ثابت أن القربي إذا كانت من جهة الأب لا تحجب البعدى من جهة الأم وبالعكس تحجب لأن الجدات يرثن بولادة الأبوين فوجب أن تعطى كل واحدة منهن حكم من تدلي به والأب لا يحجب الجدات من قبل الأم فكذا أمه والأم تحجب كل واحدة هي أبعد منها فكذا أمها. ولنا أن الجدات يرثن باعتبار الولاد فوجب أن يقدم الأدنى على العبدى كالأب الأدنى مع الأب الأبعد وليس كل حكم ثبت بواسطة يثبت لمن تدلى به ألا ترى أن أم الأم لا يزيد إرثها على السدس وتحجب بالأم والأب بخلاف ذلك
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And the farther is excluded by the nearer', whether they are from one lineage or two lineages, and whether the nearer is an inheritor or excluded by the father or grandfather. And in a narration from Ibn Mas'ud: 'Only the mother excludes grandmothers.' And in a narration from him and from Zayd ibn Thabit: 'If the nearer is from the father's side, it does not exclude the farther from the mother's side, and vice versa it excludes, because grandmothers inherit by virtue of the birth of the two parents, so it is necessary to give each of them the ruling of the one through whom she traces. The father does not exclude grandmothers from the mother's side, so likewise his mother; and the mother excludes every one who is farther than her, so likewise her mother.' And for us: grandmothers inherit by virtue of birth, so it is necessary to give precedence to the nearer over the farther, just like the nearer father with the farther father. And not every ruling established through an intermediary is established for the one who traces through that intermediary. Do you not see that the mother of the mother's inheritance does not increase beyond the sixth and she is excluded by the mother and father, contrary to that?
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage establishes the Hanafi principle that a nearer grandmother (in terms of generational distance) excludes a farther grandmother, regardless of whether they are from the same side or different sides. The text cites opposing views from Ibn Mas'ud and Zayd ibn Thabit. Ibn Mas'ud reportedly said that only the mother excludes grandmothers, implying no grandmother excludes another. The narration from both Ibn Mas'ud and Zayd holds that a nearer grandmother from the father's side does not exclude a farther one from the mother's side (because the father does not exclude maternal grandmothers), but a nearer from the mother's side does exclude a farther one from the father's side (because the mother excludes paternal grandmothers). The Hanafi response argues that grandmothers inherit by virtue of birth, so the nearer should take precedence just as a nearer father excludes a farther one. They also point out that the ruling of the intermediary does not necessarily transfer to the one tracing through him; for example, the maternal grandmother's share is only one-sixth and she is excluded by the mother and father, unlike the mother herself. Thus, the Hanafi position is that the nearer grandmother always excludes the farther.

Key Terms
حجب (hajb): Exclusion of an heir from inheritance due to the presence of a closer heir.
قربى وبعدى (qurba wa bu'da): Nearer and farther in terms of generational distance from the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, always
B) No, never
C) Only if the nearer is from the mother's side
D) Only if the farther is from the father's side

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi inheritance law, a nearer grandmother excludes a farther one, regardless of side, based on the principle of closeness by birth.

Exclusion of Grandmothers by Mother and Father
States the rule of grandmother exclusion with reasoning and companion evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule of grandmother exclusion, identify the evidence (ijma and companion qawl), and distinguish the ikhtilaf regarding the father's exclusion.

Core Idea
The mother excludes all grandmothers; the father excludes only his mother.

In Hanafi faraid, the presence of certain heirs can exclude others. This lesson focuses on how the mother and father affect the inheritance of grandmothers. You will learn the rule, its reasoning, the evidence from companions, and a companion disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rules
The passage states two rules: (1) the mother excludes all grandmothers when she inherits, and (2) the father excludes his own mother (paternal grandmother) when he inherits. Note the scope: mother excludes both maternal and paternal grandmothers; father excludes only his mother.
The father does not exclude the maternal grandmother.
2
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The passage gives a ratio: grandmothers inherit through birth, but the mother is closer in that relation. The maternal grandmother traces her relation through the mother, so when the mother is present, she blocks her. By analogy, the paternal grandmother is even weaker, so she is also blocked. For the father's mother, the father is the direct root, so he blocks her.
This analogical reasoning is based on proximity and strength of relation.
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
The author cites consensus (ijma) on the mother's exclusion and narrations from prominent Companions (Uthman, Ali, Zubayr, Sa'd, Zayd ibn Thabit) for both rules. This is a strong proof because these Companions were known for their knowledge of faraid.
Consensus and Companion practice are authoritative sources in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Recognize the ikhtilaf
The passage mentions that some Companions (Umar, Ibn Mas'ud, Imran ibn al-Husayn, Abu Musa, Abu al-Tufayl) held a different view, believeing that the father does not exclude his mother. The majority opinion (Jumhur) is preferred.
This ikhtilaf is within the generation of Companions; the Hanafi school follows the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (والكل بالأم) أي يحجب الجدات كلهن بالأم والمراد إذا كانت الأم وارثة وعليه الإجماع والمعنى فيه أن الجدات إنما يرثن بطريق الولادة والأم أبلغ حالاً منهن في ذلك فلا يرثن معها، ولأنها أصل في قرابة الجدة التي من قبلها إلى الميت وتدلي بها فلا ترث مع وجودها لما عرف في باب الحجب، فإذا حجبت التي من قبلها كانت أولى أن تحجب التي من قبل الأب لأنها أضعف حالاً منها ولهذا تؤخر في الحضانة فتحجب بها وكذا الأبويات منهن يحجبهن بالأب إذا كان وارثاً. روي عن عثمان وعلي والزبير وسعد وزيد بن ثابت رضي الله عنهم وبه أخذ جمهور العلماء، وروي عن عمر وابن مسعود وعمران بن الحصين وأبي موسى الأشعري وأبي الطفيل عامر بن واثلة أنهم
He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: 'And all are by the mother' – meaning the mother excludes all grandmothers, and the intent is when the mother is an inheritor, and there is consensus on it. The meaning of it is that grandmothers only inherit by way of birth, and the mother is more deserving in that regard, so they do not inherit with her. And because she is the root in the relationship of the grandmother from her side to the deceased, and the grandmother traces through her, so she does not inherit in her presence, as is known in the chapter of hajb. So if the one from her side is excluded, then it is more appropriate to exclude the one from the father's side, because she is weaker in status than her. For this reason she is delayed in custody, so she is excluded by her. Likewise, the paternal ones among them are excluded by the father if he is an inheritor. It is narrated from 'Uthman, 'Ali, al-Zubayr, Sa'd, and Zayd ibn Thabit (may Allah be pleased with them), and the majority of scholars adopted this. And it is narrated from 'Umar, Ibn Mas'ud, 'Imran ibn al-Husayn, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and Abu al-Tufayl 'Amir ibn Wathilah that they...
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage establishes that the mother excludes all grandmothers when she is an inheritor, and that the father excludes his own mother (the paternal grandmother). The author states there is consensus (ijma') on the first point. The reasoning is that grandmothers inherit through birth ties, and the mother is closer in that respect. Moreover, the grandmother from the mother's side traces her relationship through the mother; if the mother is present, she blocks her. By analogy, the grandmother from the father's side is even weaker in claim, so she is also blocked. The text also mentions that the paternal grandmother is excluded by the father if he is an inheritor. This is supported by narrations from several Companions, and it is the position of the majority of scholars. The passage ends mid-sentence, noting that other Companions (like 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud) had a different view, but the text cuts off.

Key Terms
أبويات (abawayyat): Grandmothers from the father's side (i.e., paternal grandmothers).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The father
B) The mother
C) The grandfather
D) Any nearer heir

Key Takeaway
The mother excludes all grandmothers by consensus; the father excludes only his mother, a position held by the majority of Companions and later scholars.

Grandmother's Inheritance: Multiplicity of Lineages and Exclusion
Intra-Hanafi dispute and exclusion rules for grandmothers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on grandmothers' inheritance, apply the rule of exclusion by a closer grandmother, and calculate the division of the sixth when multiple grandmothers are present.

Core Idea
Grandmothers inherit one-sixth, but multiplicity of lineages does not increase the share; closer excludes distant.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding grandmothers' inheritance. It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad about the effect of multiple lineages, and then explains the rules of exclusion. We will work through these rules step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
State that a grandmother inherits 1/6 when not excluded by a closer relative.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on multiplicity
Examine the disagreement between Abu Yusuf (equal division regardless of lineages) and Muhammad (division proportional to number of lineages).
This is an ikhtilaf within the school; the mufta bihi is Abu Yusuf's view.
3
Apply the exclusion rule
Learn that a closer grandmother excludes a more distant one, and all grandmothers are excluded by the mother.
This is based on qiyas: closer in lineage takes precedence.
4
Understand the basis of exclusion
Trace the Hanafi proof: grandmothers inherit by virtue of birth, so the nearer in degree is preferred, analogous to fathers.
The text also reports dissent from Ibn Mas'ud and Zayd ibn Thabit regarding paternal grandmothers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : وذات جهة كذات جهتين) يعني الجدة إذا كانت من جهة واحدة والأخرى لها جهتان فهما سواء في الميراث. قال في الأصل وإن كانت للميت جدة من جهة واحدة وجدة من جهتين أو ثلاث جهات قال أبو يوسف : لا عبرة لكثرة الجهات والسدس بينهن بالسوية. وقال محمد : لكثرة الجهات عبرة والسدس بينهن على عدد الجهات وصورتها من جهتين : امرأة زوجت ابنة ابنها من ابن ابنها فولد بينهما غلام فهذه المرأة لهذا الغلام جدة من جهتين فإنها أم أم أم هذا الغلام وأم أب أب هذا الغلام، فلو مات هذا الغلام وترك هذه الجدة وجدة أخرى من جهة الأب فهي أم أم أبيه. قال أبو يوسف : السدس بينهما بالسوية. وقال محمد السدس بينهما أثلاثاً ثلثاه من جهة هي أم أم أم أمه وهي من جهة هي أم أم أم أبيه ومن جهة أم أب أب أبيه، فلو مات هذا الغلام وترك هذه الجدة وجدة أخرى من قبل الأب وهي أم أم الأب فعلى قول أبي يوسف أن السدس بينهن بالسوية. وعلى قول محمد على أربعة أسهم ثلاثة أسهم للجدة واحد للجدة الأخرى. قال رحمه الله : ( والبعدى تحجب بالقربى) سواء كانا من جهة واحدة أو من جهتين، وسواء كانت القربى وارثة أو محجوبة بالأب أو بالجد. وفي رواية عن ابن مسعود لا تحجب الجدات إلا الأم، وفي رواية عنه وعن زيد بن ثابت أن القربي إذا كانت من جهة الأب لا تحجب البعدى من جهة الأم وبالعكس تحجب لأن الجدات يرثن بولادة الأبوين فوجب أن تعطى كل واحدة منهن حكم من تدلي به والأب لا يحجب الجدات من قبل الأم فكذا أمه والأم تحجب كل واحدة هي أبعد منها فكذا أمها. ولنا أن الجدات يرثن باعتبار الولاد فوجب أن يقدم الأدنى على العبدى كالأب الأدنى مع الأب الأبعد وليس كل حكم ثبت بواسطة يثبت لمن تدلى به ألا ترى أن أم الأم لا يزيد إرثها على السدس وتحجب بالأم والأب بخلاف ذلك قال رحمه الله : (والكل بالأم) أي يحجب الجدات كلهن بالأم والمراد إذا كانت الأم وارثة وعليه الإجماع والمعنى فيه أن الجدات إنما يرثن بطريق الولادة والأم أبلغ حالاً منهن في ذلك فلا يرثن معها، ولأنها أصل في قرابة الجدة التي من قبلها إلى الميت وتدلي بها فلا ترث مع وجودها لما عرف في باب الحجب، فإذا حجبت التي من قبلها كانت أولى أن تحجب التي من قبل الأب لأنها أضعف حالاً منها ولهذا تؤخر في الحضانة فتحجب بها وكذا الأبويات منهن يحجبهن بالأب إذا كان وارثاً. روي عن عثمان وعلي والزبير وسعد وزيد بن ثابت رضي الله عنهم وبه أخذ جمهور العلماء، وروي عن عمر وابن مسعود وعمران بن الحصين وأبي موسى الأشعري وأبي الطفيل عامر بن واثلة أنهم جعلوا لها السدس مع الأب وبه أخذ طائفة من أهل العلم من التابعين لما روي أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام ورث جدة وابنها حي ولأنها ترث ميراث الأم فلا يحجبها الأب كما لا يحجب الأم وكما لا يحجب الجد، ولأنها ترث بطريق الفرض فلا تكون العصوبة حاجبة لها كما لا يحجبها عم الميت الذي هو ابنها. قلنا إن أم الأب تدلي بالأب فلا ترث مع وجوده كبنت الابن مع الابن ولا حجة لهم في الحديث لأنه حكاية حال فيحمل أن ذلك الأب كان عماً للميت لا أباً ولا نسلم أنها ترث ميراث الأم بل ميراث الأب لأن له السدس فرضاً فترث ذلك عند عدمه، ولئن كان ميراث الأم لا يلزم منه عدم الحجب بغيره ره ألا تری بنات الابن يرثن ومع هذا يحجبن بالأبوين، وكذا الجد يحجب أبويه لما ذكرنا إلا أم الأب فإنها لا يحجبها وإن علت لأن إرثها ليس من قبله وكذا كل جدة لا تحجب الجدة التي ليست من قبلها فصارت الجدة لها حالتان السدس والسقوط .
He said (may Allah have mercy on him): 'And one with one lineage is like one with two lineages.' meaning the grandmother if she is from one lineage and the other has two lineages, then they are equal in inheritance. He said in al-Asl: If the deceased has a grandmother from one lineage and a grandmother from two or three lineages, Abu Yusuf said: No consideration is given to multiplicity of lineages, and the sixth is divided equally among them. Muhammad said: Multiplicity of lineages is given consideration, and the sixth is divided among them according to the number of lineages. Its example from two lineages: A woman married her son's daughter to her son's son, and a boy was born from them; this woman is a grandmother to this boy from two lineages: she is the mother of the mother of the mother of this boy and the mother of the father of the father of this boy. If this boy dies and leaves this grandmother and another grandmother from the father's side, who is the mother of the mother of his father: Abu Yusuf said: the sixth is between them equally. Muhammad said: the sixth is between them in thirds: two-thirds for the one with two lineages and one-third for the one with one lineage. Its example from three lineages: this married woman married the daughter of the daughter of the daughter of another's son? to this born boy, and a boy was born between them; then this wife is to this second born boy from three lineages: from one lineage she is the mother of the mother of the mother of his mother, from another lineage she is the mother of the mother of the mother of his father, and from another lineage she is the mother of the father of the father of his father. If this boy dies and leaves this grandmother and another grandmother from the father's side, who is the mother of the mother of the father: according to Abu Yusuf, the sixth is divided among them equally. According to Muhammad, into four shares: three shares for the one grandmother and one for the other grandmother. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): 'And the distant one is excluded by the close one' whether they are from one lineage or two lineages, and whether the close one is an heir or excluded by the father or grandfather. There is a narration from Ibn Mas'ud that grandmothers are only excluded by the mother. And in a narration from him and from Zayd ibn Thabit that the close one if from the father's side does not exclude the distant one from the mother's side, and vice versa excludes, because grandmothers inherit through the parentage of the parents, so it is necessary that each of them be given the ruling of the one through whom she connects: the father does not exclude grandmothers from the mother's side, so likewise his mother; and the mother excludes every one who is more distant than her, so likewise her mother. Our evidence is: grandmothers inherit by virtue of birth, so it is necessary to give precedence to the closer over the distant, like the closer father with the more distant father. And not every ruling established through an intermediary is established for the one who connects through that intermediary; do you not see that the mother of the mother does not increase her inheritance beyond the sixth and is excluded by the mother and father, unlike that. He said (may Allah have mercy on him): 'And all are by the mother' meaning he excludes all grandmothers by the mother, and the intended meaning is when the mother is an heir, and there is consensus on this. The meaning is that grandmothers only inherit through the way of birth, and the mother is more strong in that regard than them, so they do not inherit with her. And because she is the source in the kinship of the grandmother who is from her side to the deceased, and she connects through her, so she does not inherit with her existence, as known in the chapter of exclusion. So if the one from her side is excluded, it is more appropriate to exclude the one from the father's side, because she is weaker in condition than her, and for this reason she is delayed in custody, so she is excluded by her. Similarly, those from the father's side among them are excluded by the father if he is an heir. It is narrated from 'Uthman, 'Ali, al-Zubayr, Sa'd, and Zayd ibn Thabit (may Allah be pleased with them) and this is what the majority of scholars adopted. And it is narrated from 'Umar, Ibn Mas'ud, 'Imran ibn al-Husayn, Abu Musa al-Ash'ari, and Abu al-Tufayl 'Amir ibn Wathila that they gave her (the paternal grandmother) a sixth with the father, and a group of scholars from the Tabi'un adopted this, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave inheritance to a grandmother while her son was alive, and because she inherits the inheritance of the mother, so the father does not exclude her just as the mother does not exclude her and just as the grandfather does not exclude her, and because she inherits by way of Allah? prescribed share, so 'usubah (residuary) cannot be a barrier for her, just as the paternal uncle of the deceased who is her son does not exclude her. We said: The paternal grandmother connects through the father, so she does not inherit with his existence like the daughter's daughter, the son? with the son. And their proof from the hadith is not valid because it is a specific case report, so it can be interpreted that that father was a paternal uncle of the deceased, not a father. And we do not accept that she inherits the inheritance of the mother; rather she inherits the inheritance of the father, because he gets a sixth as a prescribed share, so she inherits that in his absence. And even if it were the inheritance of the mother, it does not necessitate the absence of exclusion by another; do you not see that the daughters of the son inherit, and yet they are excluded by the parents? Similarly, the grandfather excludes his parents? for what we mentioned, except the paternal grandmother's father? she is not excluded by him no matter how high, because her inheritance is not from his side. Similarly, every grandmother does not exclude a grandmother who is not from her side. So the grandmother has two states: the sixth and falling (by exclusion).
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the inheritance of grandmothers. It opens with an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad over whether multiplicity of lineages increases the share. Abu Yusuf says all grandmothers share the sixth equally regardless of how many ways they are related; Muhammad says the sixth is divided according to the number of lineages. The text provides concrete examples: a grandmother from two sides gets two-thirds of the sixth according to Muhammad. The passage then turns to the rule that a closer grandmother excludes a more distant one (ba'da tahjabu bi-l-qurba). This is the relied-upon Hanafi position. It considers both maternal and paternal lines and addresses a dissenting view from Ibn Mas'ud and Zayd ibn Thabit. The Hanafi response uses qiyas: grandmothers inherit by virtue of birth (wilaada), so precedence goes to the nearer in degree, just as a nearer father excludes a more distant father. The rule 'all grandmothers are excluded by the mother' (al-kullu bi-l-umm) is affirmed by ijma. The text also discusses the special case of the paternal grandmother's father? who is not excluded by the paternal grandfather? because her connection is not through him. The conclusion: the grandmother has only two states—either she inherits one-sixth or she falls from inheritance entirely.

Key Terms
جدة (jaddah): Grandmother of the deceased, inheriting one-sixth when not excluded.
جهة (jihah): Lineage direction or number of ways a grandmother is related to the deceased.
حجب (hajb): Exclusion from inheritance by a nearer relative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Abu Yusuf), if there are two grandmothers: one related through two lineages and one through one lineage, how is the sixth divided?
A) Equally between them
B) Two-thirds to the one with two lineages, one-third to the other
C) The one with two lineages takes the whole sixth
D) They are both excluded by a closer heir

Key Takeaway
Grandmothers inherit one-sixth equally when present, but closer grandmothers exclude distant ones, and the mother excludes all grandmothers.
